Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation to Follow the Preponderant Opinion
Rasm rule prohibiting fatwa with marjuh, supported by consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a mufti must follow the preponderant opinion (rajih) and identify the consensus (ijma') that prohibits acting upon the weak opinion (marjuh) in fatwa.

Core Idea
Following the weak opinion in fatwa is forbidden by consensus — only the preponderant opinion is binding.

This lesson establishes a fundamental rule for muftis: you cannot issue a fatwa based on a weak opinion (marjuh) when a stronger preponderant opinion (rajih) exists within your school. The author cites multiple scholars and consensus to demonstrate that this prohibition is agreed upon. Understanding this rule prevents arbitrary fatwa-giving and ensures that legal rulings are based on sound scholarly preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Locate the main rule: 'It is wajib to follow the preponderant opinion; it is not permissible to act or issue fatwa with the weak opinion.' Note the exception: 'except in some instances' which will be covered later.
This is the core principle of the lesson.
2
Understand the Evidence
The author states consensus (ijma') on this rule. Identify the scholars quoted: Ibn Hajar, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, al-Qarafi, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. Understand that consensus makes this ruling binding.
Consensus is a strong proof in usul.
3
Apply the Rule to Individuals
The rule applies to both the mujtahid (when he can preponderate) and the muqallid (who must follow the preponderant view of his school). For the mujtahid, if evidence is conflicting and he cannot preponderate, he must judge with one of the two opinions by consensus.
This clarifies the scope of the rule.
4
Note the Status of the Weak Opinion
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha states that the weak opinion is like non-existence compared to the preponderant. This emphasizes that the marjuh has no practical effect in fatwa.
This is a key reminder for muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم بأن الواجب اتباع ما ترجيحه عن أهله قد عُلما أو كان ظاهر الرواية ولم يرجحوا خلاف ذاك فاعلم [عدم جواز العمل والإفتاء بالمرجوح] يتبع أي أن الواجب على من أراد أن يعمل لنفسه أو يفتي غيره، أن القول الذي رجحه علماء مذهبه فلا يجوز له العمل أو الإفتاء بالمرجوح إلا في بعض المواضع، كما سيأتي في النظم. وقد نقلوا الإجماع على ذلك. ففي الفتاوى الكبرى للمحقق ابن حجر المكي: قال في زوائد الروضة: إنه لا يجوز للمفتي والعامل أن يفتي أو يعمل بما شاء من القولين أو الوجهين من غير نظر. وهذا لا خلاف فيه. وسبقه إلى حكاية الإجماع فيهما ابن الصلاح، والباجي من المالكية في المفتي. وكلام القرافي دال على أن المجتهد والمقلد لا يحل لهما الحكم والإفتاء بغير الراجح؛ لأنه اتباع للهوى، وهو حرام إجماعا، وأن محله في المجتهد ما لم تتعارض الأدلة عنده، ويعجز عن الترجيح، وأن المقلده حينئذ الحكم بأحد القولين إجماعا. وقال الإمام المحقق العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا في أول كتابه "تصحيح القدوري": إني رأيت من عمل في مذهب أئمتنا دم بالتشهي، حتى لفظ بعض القضاة: "هل" ثم "حجر ؟" فقلت: نعم! اتباع سمعت من الهوى حرام، والمرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجح في المتقابلات ممنوع. وقال في "كتاب الأصول" لليعمري: من لم يطلع على المشهور من الروايتين أو القولين فليس له التشهي والحكم ما شاء منهما من غير نظر في الترجيح.
Know that the obligatory is to follow what has been known to be preponderant from its people, or the apparent transmission even if they did not deem preponderant the opposite of that, so know. [The impermissibility of acting upon or issuing fatwa with the weak opinion] continues. That is, it is obligatory upon one who wants to act for himself or issue a fatwa for others to follow the opinion that the scholars of his school have deemed preponderant; thus it is not permissible for him to act or issue fatwa with the weak opinion except in some instances, as will come in the poem. And they have transmitted consensus on this. In al-Fatawa al-Kubra by the investigator Ibn Hajar al-Makki: He said in Zawa'id al-Rawdah: 'It is not permissible for the mufti and the practitioner to issue a fatwa or act according to whichever of the two opinions or two views they wish without consideration. There is no disagreement on this.' Ibn al-Salah preceded him in narrating consensus on these two issues, as did al-Baji from the Malikis regarding the mufti. And al-Qarafi's speech indicates that the mujtahid and the muqallid are not permitted to judge or issue fatwa with other than the preponderant, because it is following desire, which is forbidden by consensus. Its application is for the mujtahid when evidence is not conflicting and he is unable to preponderate, and for the muqallid at that time [he must] judge with one of the two opinions by consensus. And the investigator, the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said at the beginning of his book Tashih al-Quduri: 'I saw that those who act in the school of our imams are blamed for caprice, until some judges said: "Is there... then... a stone?" So I said: Yes! Following desire is forbidden, and the weak opinion in comparison to the preponderant is like non-existence, and preponderating without a preponderator between opposites is prohibited.' And he said in the book al-Usul by al-Ya'muri: 'Whoever is not aware of the well-known of the two transmissions or the two opinions, it is not for him to act capriciously and judge whichever he wishes without consideration of preponderance.'
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage presents the first rasm rule of the book: it is obligatory to follow the preponderant opinion (rajih) and forbidden to act upon or issue fatwa with the weak opinion (marjuh), except in certain exceptions that will be discussed later. The author cites consensus (ijma') on this prohibition. He quotes several scholars: Ibn Hajar al-Makki, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, al-Qarafi, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, all affirming that following the weak opinion is like following desire, which is haram by consensus. The rule applies to both the mujtahid and the muqallid. For the mujtahid, he must not choose arbitrarily but must give preponderance based on evidence. For the muqallid, he must follow the preponderant view in his school. The author also notes that the weak opinion is considered as non-existent compared to the preponderant. This rule is fundamental to the discipline of ifta', ensuring that fatwas are based on sound legal reasoning rather than personal inclination.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjuh): The weak opinion that is not preponderant in the school.
راجح (rajih): The preponderant opinion that is stronger in evidence and relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hajar al-Makki, what is the ruling on a mufti or practitioner arbitrarily choosing between opinions without consideration?
A) Permissible with certain conditions
B) Not permissible, with no disagreement on this
C) Recommended if both are strong
D) Required to choose the easier one

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always follow the preponderant opinion (rajih) and never the weak opinion (marjuh), based on scholarly consensus.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
10 min
The Ruling on Using Weaker Opinions: Prohibition and Exceptions
Rasm al-Mufti: prohibition of marjuh with consensus evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of acting on and giving fatwa with the weaker opinion (marjuh), identify the consensus evidence, and apply the exception when no preponderance is possible.

Core Idea
The weaker opinion is like non-existence against the preponderant; following it without necessity is following whim, which is haram.

This passage establishes a fundamental condition for valid fatwa within the Hanafi madhhab: the mufti must only use the preponderant (rajih) opinion. The authors cite consensus (ijma) from major scholars across schools. However, an exception exists when no tarjih is possible, to be discussed later. Understanding this principle protects the mufti from falling into prohibited personal whim (tashahhi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What is the primary obligation stated for a mufti or a person acting for himself?
Look for the phrase 'لا يجوز العمل والإفتاء بالمرجوح'.
2
Recognize the authority: consensus (ijma)
The passage claims that the prohibition is established by consensus. List the scholars cited as witnesses to this consensus.
Ibn Hajar al-Makki, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, al-Qarafi, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, Ibn Kamal Pasha.
3
Understand the reasoning: following whim
Why is using the marjuh prohibited? What does it equate to?
It is following whim (hawa), which is haram unanimously. The marjuh is like non-existence in comparison to the rajih.
4
Distinguish mufti vs. judge
How does the passage differentiate the roles of mufti and judge regarding this rule?
The mufti gives the ruling, the judge enforces it; both must follow the rajih.
5
Note the exception
The passage hints at an exception for when no tarjih is possible. What is the indication?
'وسيأتي ما إذا لم يوجد ترجيح مرجوح القولين' — will be discussed later.

Source Text

شرح عقود رسم المفتي عدم جواز العمل والإفتاء بالمرجوح يتبع أي أن الواجب على من أراد أن يعمل لنفسه أو يفتي غيره، أن القول الذي رجحه علماء مذهبه فلا يجوز له العمل أو الإفتاء بالمرجوح إلا في بعض المواضع، كما سيأتي في النظم. وقد نقلوا الإجماع على ذلك. ففي الفتاوى الكبرى للمحقق ابن حجر المكي: قال في زوائد الروضة: إنه لا يجوز للمفتي والعامل أن يفتي أو يعمل بما شاء من القولين أو الوجهين من غير نظر. وهذا لا خلاف فيه. وسبقه إلى حكاية الإجماع فيهما ابن الصلاح، والباجي من المالكية في المفتي. وكلام القرافي دال على أن المجتهد والمقلد لا يحل لهما الحكم والإفتاء بغير الراجح؛ لأنه اتباع للهوى، وهو حرام إجماعا، وأن محله في المجتهد ما لم تتعارض الأدلة عنده، ويعجز عن الترجيح، وأن المقلد حينئذ الحكم بأحد القولين إجماعا. وقال الإمام المحقق العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا في أول كتابه "تصحيح القدوري": إني رأيت من عمل في مذهب أئمتنا دم بالتشهي، حتى لفظ بعض القضاة: "هل" ثم "حجر ؟" فقلت: نعم! اتباع الهوى حرام، والمرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجح في المتقابلات ممنوع. وقال في "كتاب الأصول" لليعمري: من لم يطلع على المشهور من الروايتين أو القولين فليس له التشهي والحكم ما شاء منهما من غير نظر في الترجيح. وقال الإمام أبو عمرو في آداب المفتي: اعلم أن من يكتفي بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقا لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع. وحكى الباجي أنه وقعت له واقعة فأفتوا فيها بما يضره، فلما سألهم قالوا ما علمنا أنها لك، وأفتوه بالرواية الأخرى التي توافق قصده. قال الباجي وهذا لا خلاف بين المسلمين ممن يعتد به في الإجماع أنه لا يجوز. قال في أصول الأقضية ولا فرق بين المفتي والحاكم إلا أن المفتي بالحكم، والقاضي ملزم به ثم نقل بعده: وأما الحكم والفتيا بما هو لأحد فخلاف الإجماع، وسيأتي ما إذا لم يوجد ترجيح مرجوح القولين. وقولي: "عن أهله أي أهل الترجيح، إشارة إلى أنه لا يكتفى بترجيح أي عالم كان. مخبر [؟] وقال العلامة شمس الدين محمد بن سليمان الشهير بـ"ابن كمال باشا" في بعض رسائله لا بد للمفتي المقلد أن يعلم حال من يفتي بقوله، ولا نعني بذلك معرفته باسمه ونسبه ونسبته إلى بلد من البلاد؛ إذ يسمن ذلك ولا يغني بل معرفته في الرواية، ودرجته في الدراية، وطبقته من طبقات الفقهاء؛ ليكون على بصيرة وافية في التمييز بين القائلين المتخالفين، وقدرة كافية في الترجيح بين القولين المتعارضين.
Explanation of the treatise on the drawing of the mufti. The impermissibility of acting and giving fatwa by the weaker opinion. Continuation: That is, it is obligatory upon one who wants to act for himself or give fatwa to others to follow the opinion that the scholars of his madhhab have preponderated. So it is not permissible for him to act or give fatwa by the weaker opinion except in some places, as will come in the poem. And they have transmitted consensus on that. In al-Fatawa al-Kubra by the muhaqqiq Ibn Hajar al-Makki: He said in Zawa'id al-Rawda: It is not permissible for the mufti and the practitioner to give fatwa or act with whichever of the two statements or two aspects he pleases without consideration. There is no disagreement on this. Ibn al-Salah preceded him in relating consensus on both, and al-Baji from the Malikiyyah regarding the mufti. The words of al-Qarafi indicate that the mujtahid and the muqallid are not permitted to judge or give fatwa with other than the preponderant; because it is following whim, which is unanimously forbidden. And that its place in the mujtahid is when the evidences are not contradictory for him and he is unable to preponderate; and that the muqallid then judges with one of the two statements by consensus. Imam, muhaqqiq, allama Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said at the beginning of his book Tashih al-Quduri: I have seen people acting in the madhhab of our imams according to whim, even to the extent that a judge uttered: 'Hal?' then 'Hajar?' So I said: Yes! Following whim is forbidden, and the weaker opinion in comparison to the preponderant is like non-existence, and preponderance without a preponderator in opposites is prohibited. He said in Kitab al-Usul by al-Ya'mari: Whoever has not come to know the well-known of the two transmissions or two statements, it is not for him to whimsically judge whichever he pleases without consideration of preponderance. Imam Abu Amr said in Adab al-Mufti: Know that whoever content himself that his fatwa or action agrees with a statement or aspect in the issue, and acts with whichever of the statements and aspects he pleases without considering preponderance, has been ignorant and violated consensus. Al-Baji related that an incident occurred to him and they gave a fatwa that harmed him. When he asked them, they said: We did not know it was for you, and they gave him a fatwa from the other narration that agreed with his objective. Al-Baji said: This is, without disagreement among Muslims whose consensus is considered, not permissible. He said in Usul al-Aqdiya: There is no difference between the mufti and the judge except that the mufti gives a ruling (hukm) and the judge enforces it. Then he transmitted thereafter: As for judging and giving fatwa with what is for someone, it is contrary to consensus. And it will come later when there is no preponderance of the weaker of the two statements. And my statement: 'from its people, meaning the people of preponderance, indicates that the preponderance of any scholar is not sufficient. [Unclear: مخبر?] And the allama Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Sulayman, famous as Ibn Kamal Pasha, said in some of his treatises: It is necessary for the muqallid mufti to know the status of the one whose statement he gives fatwa by. We do not mean by that knowledge of his name, lineage, or attribution to a town, for that neither fattens nor suffices; rather, knowledge of his status in narration, his rank in knowledge, and his class from the layers of the fuqaha, so that he may have sufficient insight for distinguishing between differing spokesmen and adequate capability for preponderance between contradictory statements.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm al-mufti) establishing a fundamental principle: the mufti and any Muslim acting on the madhhab must only use the preponderant (rajih) opinion. The weaker (marjuh) opinion is prohibited except when explicitly allowed (e.g., in cases of necessity, to be discussed later). The author begins by stating this obligation for both the one acting for himself and the one giving fatwa. He then cites consensus (ijma) from major scholars: Ibn Hajar al-Makki, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji (from the Maliki school), and al-Qarafi. The core argument is that following the weaker opinion without a valid reason is following personal desire (hawa), which is unanimously haram. Qasim ibn Qutlubugha adds that the marjuh is like non-existence compared to the rajih. Ibn Kamal Pasha emphasizes that the muqallid mufti must know the level (tabaqa) of the scholar he favors, not just his name, in order to properly preponderate between conflicting reports. The passage also distinguishes the mufti from the judge: the mufti merely declares the ruling, while the judge enforces it. However, both are bound by the same rule of following the rajih. The exception (when no tarjih is possible) will be addressed later. Overall, this text is a memorization anchor for a key condition of valid ifta: avoiding the marjuh except in designated circumstances.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The weaker or less preponderant opinion in the madhhab, not taken as the relied-upon position.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion that is stronger due to evidence or scholarly weight.
التشهي (al-tashahhi): Acting according to personal whim in choosing legal opinions.
طبقات الفقهاء (tabaqat al-fuqaha): The hierarchical layers of Hanafi jurists based on knowledge and authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on a mufti giving a fatwa based on a marjuh opinion without a valid reason?
A) Permissible if he is a mujtahid
B) Prohibited by consensus (ijma)
C) Permissible if it benefits the questioner
D) Permissible if he does not know the rajih

Key Takeaway
The mufti and every Muslim acting on the madhhab must only use the preponderant (rajih) opinion; using the weaker (marjuh) is prohibited by consensus, except when no tarjih is possible.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Prohibition of Fatwa by Weak Opinion Without Tarjih
Rasm rule prohibiting fatwa by weak opinion without tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that acting or issuing fatwa by a marjuh opinion without tarjih is prohibited, and apply it to a fatwa scenario by identifying the necessity of tarjih and the consequence of ignoring it.

Core Idea
It is prohibited by consensus to give fatwa by the weaker opinion without weighing evidence.

This lesson examines a fundamental principle in Hanafi ifta: the prohibition of issuing a fatwa based on a weaker opinion (marjuh) without proper tarjih. The passage cites consensus and warns against mere convenience, illustrating the danger with al-Baji's story. Understanding this rule is essential for any mufti to maintain integrity and avoid violating scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening line: 'لا يجوز العمل والإفتاء بالمرجوح'. Identify that this is a prohibition (hukm: haram? Actually it is a rasm rule: impermissible (la yajuz) which in ifta context means it is prohibited to act or give fatwa by the weaker opinion without tarjih.
The ruling is clear: the weaker opinion cannot be acted upon or used for fatwa unless preponderated.
2
Recognize the proof
The author cites Imam Abu Amr and al-Baji, who state that ignoring tarjih is a breach of consensus (ijma'). Analyze the story of al-Baji: the muftis gave a fatwa based on a weaker narration to benefit the questioner, and al-Baji condemned this as universally prohibited.
The proof is ijmāʿ, which is a primary source; no need for further evidence.
3
Understand the exception
Note the phrase 'وسيأتي ما إذا لم يوجد ترجيح مرجوح القولين'. This indicates an exception: when no tarjih is possible and both opinions are weak, the rule may defer to another principle.
The exception is not detailed here, but it signals that the prohibition is not absolute in all cases.
4
Distinguish mufti from judge
The text says 'لا فرق بين المفتي والحاكم إلا أن المفتي بالحكم، والقاضي ملزم به'. Both mufti and judge are bound by the prohibition, but the judge's ruling is binding while the mufti's is advisory.
This distinguishes the two roles but emphasizes that both must follow tarjih.
5
Recognize the requirement to know scholars' ranks
Ibn Kamal Pasha stresses that a mufti must know the tabaqa (layer) of the scholars he follows, not just names, to properly perform tarjih.
This is a practical condition: tarjih requires knowing which scholars are more authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدم جواز العمل والإفتاء بالمرجوح
شرح عقود رسم المفتي وقال الإمام أبو عمرو في آداب المفتي: اعلم أن من يكتفي بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقا لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع. وحكى الباجي أنه وقعت له واقعة فأفتوا فيها بما يضره، فلما سألهم قالوا ما علمنا أنها لك، وأفتوه بالرواية الأخرى التي توافق قصده. قال الباجي وهذا لا خلاف بين المسلمين ممن يعتد به في الإجماع أنه لا يجوز. قال في أصول الأقضية ولا فرق بين المفتي والحاكم إلا أن المفتي بالحكم، والقاضي ملزم به ثم نقل بعده: وأما الحكم والفتيا بما هو لأحد فخلاف الإجماع، وسيأتي ما إذا لم يوجد ترجيح مرجوح القولين. وقولي: "عن أهله أي أهل الترجيح، إشارة إلى أنه لا يكتفى بترجيح أي عالم كان.
مخبر
فقد قال العلامة شمس الدين محمد بن سليمان الشهير بـ"ابن كمال باشا" في بعض رسائله لا بد للمفتي المقلد أن يعلم حال من يفتي بقوله، ولا نعني بذلك معرفته باسمه ونسبه ونسبته إلى بلد من البلاد؛ إذ يسمن ذلك ولا يغني بل معرفته في الرواية، ودرجته في الدراية، وطبقته من طبقات الفقهاء؛ ليكون على بصيرة وافية في التمييز بين القائلين المتخالفين، وقدرة كافية في الترجيح بين القولين المتعارضين.
Non-permissibility of acting and issuing fatwa by the weaker opinion. Commentary on The Contract of the Mufti's Code. Imam Abu Amr said in Adab al-Mufti: Know that whoever is satisfied that his fatwa or action is in agreement with a statement or aspect in the matter, and acts with whichever statements and aspects he wishes without consideration of tarjih, has acted ignorantly and breached consensus. Al-Baji narrated that an incident occurred to him, and they gave a fatwa that harmed him. When he asked them, they said 'We did not know it was for you,' and they gave him a fatwa by the other narration that suited his desire. Al-Baji said: There is no disagreement among Muslims whose opinion is considered in consensus that this is not permissible. He said in Usul al-Aqdiya: There is no difference between the mufti and the judge except that the mufti [gives] a ruling, and the judge is bound by it. Then later he narrated: As for adjudication and fatwa by that which is [favorable] to someone, it is contrary to consensus. And it will come later regarding when there is no tarjih between two weak opinions. And my statement: 'from its people' i.e., the people of tarjih, an indication that tarjih by any scholar is not sufficient. A reporter [or a section]. Indeed the scholar Shams al-Din Muhammad bin Sulayman, known as Ibn Kamal Pasha, said in some of his treatises: It is necessary for the muqallid mufti to know the status of the one by whose statement he gives fatwa. We do not mean by that knowing his name, lineage, and attribution to a country, for that neither benefits nor suffices. Rather, his knowledge in transmission (riwaya), his level in understanding (diraya), and his layer among the layers of fuqaha, so that he may have complete insight in distinguishing between conflicting authorities, and sufficient ability in giving tarjih between contradictory statements.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (methodological rule for muftis) stating that it is impermissible to act or issue a fatwa based on a weak (marjuh) opinion without proper tarjih. The text opens with a clear ruling and supports it with quotes from earlier authorities. Imam Abu Amr's statement in Adab al-Mufti declares that anyone who follows any opinion at will without considering which is preponderant has violated ijmāʿ (consensus). The story of al-Baji illustrates the danger: a mufti gave a fatwa favoring the questioner's desire, unaware it was against al-Baji himself; this is universally condemned. The text then equates mufti and judge in this regard, except that the judge's ruling is binding. Finally, Ibn Kamal Pasha emphasizes that a mufti must know the scholarly rank (tabaqa) of the authorities he follows, not just their names, to properly perform tarjih. This passage guards against a common misunderstanding: that any opinion from a valid scholar is equally usable; rather, one must follow the preponderant view in the madhhab.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjūḥ): The weaker opinion among conflicting views, which has less evidence or is outweighed by the preponderant (rajih) view.
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): The process of weighing evidence or authorities to determine which opinion is stronger.
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahid scholars of the ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Baji's incident illustrate?
A) That a mufti must follow the majority opinion.
B) That issuing a fatwa to please the questioner is permissible.
C) That acting by a weaker opinion without tarjih violates consensus.
D) That a mufti is not obliged to know the questioner's situation.

Key Takeaway
A mufti is prohibited by consensus from issuing a fatwa by the weaker opinion (marjuh) without proper tarjih; he must follow the preponderant view.

Necessity of Referencing Original Sources
Stating the rule and illustrating with a case on hiring for Quran recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of referring to original sources (al-ma'khadh al-asli) to identify and correct a transmitted error in Hanafi fatwa, using the case of hiring for Quran recitation.

Core Idea
A mufti must trace every ruling to its original source; blind transmission of later works leads to error.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle of Hanafi mufti conduct: the duty to verify rulings by consulting the original sources (al-ma'khadh al-asli) rather than relying solely on later abridgments. The author illustrates the danger with a concrete case: a mistaken fatwa on hiring for Quran recitation that spread through many later works. You will learn why such errors occur and how to avoid them by adhering to the proper methodology of iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the core rule: a mufti must refer to the original source (al-ma'khadh al-asli) for any ruling, not rely solely on later abridgments or popular compilations.
The rule is derived from the statement of Shaykh Salih al-Jinini and the author's own emphasis.
2
Recognize the danger of transmitted errors
Understand that a single mistaken ruling can be copied by many later authors, leading to widespread error. The author gives two examples: one from Ibn Nujaym and the detailed case of hiring for recitation.
This highlights the mufti's responsibility to verify before issuing fatwas.
3
Examine the mistaken fatwa case
Analyze the case: some later authors claimed the fatwa is on the validity of hiring for mere Quran recitation. Trace the origin of this error.
The error began with a misinterpretation of the later scholars' allowance for teaching Quran.
4
Trace the original Hanafi position
Recover the original ruling from the three Imams (Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): hiring for acts of worship is invalid. Then understand the later exception for teaching Quran due to necessity (darurah), and the rationale.
The later scholars did not repeal the original; they made a limited exception based on necessity.
5
Apply the rule to correct the error
Learn how to reject the incorrect transmission: verify that the claimed ruling lacks necessity, contradicts the original sources, and leads to harm (turning Quran into a trade).
This is the practical application for a mufti: always compare later claims to the original source.

The necessity of referring to the original source. [Books like] al-Qunyah, or abridged works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Haskafi, al-Nahr, and al-Ayni's commentary on al-Kanz. Our teacher Salih al-Jinini said: It is not permissible to issue fatwas from these books unless one knows the transmitted [original] and reviews their sources. This is what I heard from him, and he is a famous authority in fiqh, and the responsibility is upon him. [The necessity of referring to the original source] I say: It may happen that a statement is transmitted in about twenty books of the later scholars, and the statement is mistaken; the first who set it down made an error, then those after him transmit it, and thus they transmit from one another. 1. As occurred in some issues of 'what may be attached and what may not', as pointed out by Allamah Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 2. Among them is the issue of hiring for the mere recitation of the Quran. It happened that the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawharah Sharh al-Quduri said: The fatwa is on the validity of hiring; but the matter was reversed for him, for the fatwa is on the validity of hiring for teaching the Quran, not for its recitation. Then most of the authors who came after him followed him in that and transmitted it, and it is a clear mistake. Rather, many of them said: The fatwa is on the validity of hiring for acts of worship, and they put it broadly and say it is the school of the later scholars. Some of them branch out from that to the validity of hiring for Hajj, and all of this is a more glaring error than the first. For the transmissions from our three Imams—Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—agree that hiring for acts of worship is invalid. But there came after them from among the mujtahids (those capable of ijtihad and tarjih) those who gave a fatwa allowing it for teaching the Quran due to necessity; because teachers used to receive stipends from the treasury, and when those stopped, if hiring and taking fees were not valid, the Quran would be lost, and in that is loss of the religion, due to the teachers' need to earn a living. And those after them also gave fatwa allowing it for adhan and imamah, because they are rites of the religion, so they validated hiring for them also due to necessity. This is what the later scholars after Abu Hanifah and his companions gave fatwa on; because they knew that if Abu Hanifah and his companions were in their time, they would have said the same, and would have retracted their earlier statement. The authoritative texts, commentaries, and fatwa collections are unanimous on transmitting the invalidity of hiring for acts of worship except for what was mentioned, and they justified it by necessity, which is fear of loss of the religion, and they explicitly stated that reasoning. So how can it be said that the school of the later scholars is the validity of hiring for mere recitation, when there is no such necessity? For if time passed and no one hired anyone for that, no harm would occur. Rather, harm lies in hiring for it, since the Quran has become a means of earning and a trade to be profited from, and the reciter among them does not recite anything purely for the sake of Allah, but only recites for payment, which is pure show (riya) which is doing deeds for other than Allah. Then how can he obtain the reward that the hirer intended to gift to his deceased? Imam Qadi Khan said: Taking payment in exchange for dhikr prevents deserving reward. And the like is in Fath al-Qadir regarding the muadhdhin taking payment. And if he knew that there is no reward, he would not pay a single penny. So they came to a way of collecting...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti establishes a critical rasm al-mufti rule: a mufti must always refer back to the original source (al-ma'khadh al-asli) of a ruling and cannot rely solely on later abridged works or popular compilations. The author first quotes his teacher's warning that it is impermissible to issue fatwas from secondary books like al-Qunyah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, etc., without knowing the original transmission and sources. He then provides a concrete illustration of the danger: a mistaken fatwa regarding hiring for Quran recitation (al-istijar 'ala tilawat al-Quran al-mujarradah). An earlier scholar incorrectly stated that the fatwa is on the validity of hiring for recitation, but the correct fatwa is for teaching Quran. This error was then blindly copied by many later authors, some even extending it to hiring for all acts of worship and Hajj. The author emphasizes that the three founding Imams (Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) all agreed that hiring for acts of worship is invalid. However, later mujtahids, due to necessity (darurah), allowed hiring specifically for teaching Quran, adhan, and imamah—but not for mere recitation. The necessity was that teachers' stipends were cut off, threatening the preservation of Quranic knowledge. The later scholars did not repeal the original ruling; they made an exception under the principle that necessity permits the otherwise invalid. The author rebukes those who wrongly attribute to the later school a blanket permission for hiring for recitation, pointing out that no such necessity exists, and that such hiring actually causes harm by turning Quran recitation into a trade and preventing sincere worship. He cites Qadi Khan and Fath al-Qadir to show that taking payment for dhikr nullifies reward. Thus, the mufti must distinguish between the original Hanafi position and later exceptions, and always verify the source of a fatwa before issuing it.

Key Terms
المأخذ الأصلي (al-ma'khadh al-asli): The original source text from which a ruling is derived, as opposed to later abridgments or commentaries.
الاستئجار على التلاوة المجردة (al-istijar 'ala al-tilawah al-mujarradah): Hiring someone to recite Quran without teaching, seeking reward for the deceased or living.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because they believed the original ruling was abrogated.
B) Due to necessity (darurah) to preserve the Quran when teachers' stipends were cut.
C) Because they considered teaching Quran a lesser act of worship.
D) Because the three Imams disagreed on the matter.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always trace a ruling back to its original source and not rely on later transmissions without verifying the reasoning and conditions.

Necessity-Based Fatwas: Scope and Limits of Darurah
Critique of extending necessity-based dispensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-darurah tubihu al-mahzura' to distinguish legitimate necessity-driven fatwas from impermissible extensions in hiring for acts of worship.

Core Idea
A necessity-based fatwa cannot be extended beyond its cause; the later Hanafi permission was conditional, not a blanket rule.

This passage from Ibn 'Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti commentary illustrates a critical principle in ifta: a fatwa issued due to necessity (darurah) is strictly limited to the scope of that necessity. Later scholars permitted hiring for Quran teaching when state stipends ceased, but some improperly extended this to all Quran recitation. You will learn how to identify the legitimate application of 'al-darurah tubihu al-mahzura' and avoid common errors in extending dispensations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Original Ruling
State the original Hanafi ruling on hiring for acts of worship (ibadat). The source states that the madhhab unanimously held it invalid because reward belongs to the doer and wages corrupt sincerity.
The original ruling is a baseline – any departure requires a clear justification.
2
Identify the Necessity that Triggered the Exception
Find in the passage the specific necessity that led later scholars to permit hiring for teaching Quran. It was the cutting off of state stipends, which threatened the preservation of Quranic knowledge.
The necessity is described as 'خوف ضياع الدين' (fear of loss of religion).
3
Apply the Qawida: al-Darurah Tubihu al-Mahzura
Explain how the qawida operates: necessity permits what is normally prohibited, but only to the extent needed. The permission for teaching Quran was limited to that context.
The qawida is from the pre-populated analytical toolbox.
4
Evaluate the Challenged Extension
Assess the claim that later scholars permitted hiring for mere recitation (tilaawah mujarradah) without necessity. The author argues this is invalid because no harm would occur if it were not done, and it leads to corruption.
Key phrase: 'فلو مضى الدهر ولم يستأجر أحد أحدا على ذلك، لم يحصل به ضرر'.
5
Formulate the Fatwa Hierarchy
Determine the mufta bihi position: hiring for acts of worship is invalid except where genuine necessity exists (preserving religion). Mere recitation without necessity remains prohibited.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

لزوم المراجعة إلى المأخذ الأصلي أهل التخريج والترجيح، فأفتوا بصحته على تعليم القرآن للضرورة؛ فإنه كان للمعلمين عطايا من بيت المال وانقطعت فلو لم يصح الاستئجار وأخذ الأجرة لضاع القرآن، وفيه ضياع الدين؛ لاحتياج المعلمين إلى الاكتساب. وأفتى من بعدهم أيضا من أمثالهم بصحته على الأذان والإمامة؛ لأنهما من شعائر الدين، فصححوا الاستئجار عليهما للضرورة أيضا. فهذا ما أفتى به المتأخرون عن أبي حنيفة وأصحابه؛ لعلمهم بأن أبا حنيفة وأصحابه لو كانوا في عصرهم لقالوا بذلك، ورجعوا عن قولهم الأول. وقد أطبقت المتون والشروح والفتاوى على نقلهم بطلان الاستئجار على الطاعات إلا فيما ذكر، وعللوا ذلك بالضرورة، وهي خوف ضياع الدين، وصرحوا بذلك التعليل، فكيف يصح أن يقال: إن مذهب المتأخرين صحة الاستئجار على التلاوة المجردة، مع عدم الضرورة المذكورة؛ فإنه لو مضى الدهر، ولم يستأجر أحد أحدا على ذلك، لم يحصل به ضرر، بل الضرر صار في الاستئجار عليه، حيث صار القرآن مكسبا وحرفة يتجر بها، وصار القاري منهم لا يقرأ شيئا لوجه الله تعالى خالصا بل لا يقرأ إلا للأجرة، وهو الرياء المحض الذي هو إرادة العمل لغير الله تعالى، فمن أين يحصل له الثواب الذي طلب المستأجر أن يهديه لميته؟ وقد قال الإمام قاضي خان: إن أخذ الأجر في مقابلة الذكر يمنع استحقاق الثواب. ومثله في "فتح القدير" في أخذ المؤذن الأجر. ولو علم أنه لا ثواب له لم يدفع له فلسا واحدا فصاروا يتوصلون إلى جمع الحطام الحرام بوسيلة الذكر والقرآن وصار الناس يعتقدون ذلك من أعظم القرب، وهو من أعظم القبائح المترتبة على القول بصحة الاستئجار، مع غير ذلك مما يترتب عليه: من أكل أموال الأيتام، والجلوس في بيوتهم على فرشهم وإقلاق النائمين بالصراخ، ودق الطبول، والغناء، واجتماع النساء والمردان، وغير ذلك من المنكرات الفظيعة، كما أوضحت ذلك كله مع بسط النقول عن أهل المذهب في رسالتي المسماة: "شفاء العليل وبل الغليل في بطلان الوصية بالختمات والتهاليل"، وعليها تقاريظ فقهاء أهل العصر، من أجلّهم خاتمة الفقهاء والعباد الناسكين مفتي مصر القاهرة، سيدي المرحوم السيد أحمد الطحطاوي صاحب الحاشية الفائقة على "الدر المختار"، رحمه الله تعالى.
The necessity of referring to the original source. The people of takhrij and tarjih issued fatwas permitting hiring for teaching the Quran due to necessity; for teachers used to receive stipends from the treasury and these were cut off. If hiring and taking wages were not valid, the Quran would be lost, and in that is the loss of religion because teachers need to earn. Those after them also issued fatwas permitting it for adhan and imamah because they are symbols of religion; they validated hiring for them also due to necessity. This is what the later scholars after Abu Hanifa and his companions issued fatwas on, knowing that Abu Hanifa and his companions, had they been in their era, would have said the same and retracted their earlier statement. The texts, commentaries, and fatwas have unanimously reported the invalidity of hiring for acts of worship except for what was mentioned, and they explained it by necessity, which is fear of the loss of religion, and they explicitly stated that reasoning. So how can it be said that the school of the later scholars is the validity of hiring for mere recitation without the mentioned necessity? For if time passed and no one hired anyone for that, no harm would occur; rather the harm has occurred in hiring for it, as the Quran has become a means of earning and a trade, and the reciter recites nothing solely for the sake of Allah but only for wages, which is pure hypocrisy (riya'), i.e., performing deeds for other than Allah. So from where does he obtain the reward that the hirer intended to gift to his deceased? Imam Qadi Khan said: Taking wages in exchange for dhikr prevents entitlement to reward. Similar is in Fath al-Qadir regarding the mu'adhdhin taking wages. If it were known that there is no reward, not a single penny would be paid. So they have resorted to collecting forbidden trash through dhikr and Quran, and people consider that among the greatest acts of devotion, while it is among the greatest evils resulting from the opinion of validity of hiring, along with other consequences: consuming orphans' wealth, sitting in their homes on their furnishings, disturbing sleepers with screaming, beating drums, singing, gatherings of women and beardless youths, and other terrible evils, as I have explained all that with extensive quotations from the scholars of the madhhab in my treatise titled 'Shifa' al-‘Alil wa Ball al-Ghalil fi Butlan al-Wasiyyah bi al-Khatimat wa al-Tahalil', which has endorsements from contemporary jurists, among the greatest of whom is the final jurist and devout worshipper, the Mufti of Cairo, my master the late Sayyid Ahmad al-Tahtawi, author of the superior gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion (rasm al-mufti) about the necessity of referring to original sources when issuing fatwas, using the case of hiring for acts of worship as an example. The author, Ibn ‘Abidin (likely from his Rasm al-Mufti commentary), explains that later Hanafi scholars (mutakkhirin) permitted hiring for teaching Quran, adhan, and imamah due to necessity (darurah) — namely, to preserve the religion when state funding ceased. They reasoned that Abu Hanifa and his companions would have agreed had they been in that situation. However, the author argues that this permission was limited to genuine necessity, and that the current practice of hiring for mere recitation without necessity is a grave corruption. He cites Imam Qadi Khan that taking wages for dhikr negates reward, and lists evils arising from this practice, including hypocrisy and social ills. The passage emphasizes that fatwas must be grounded in original principles and that muftis cannot extend a dispensation beyond its cause. The author also references his own treatise on the invalidity of bequests for Quran khatms and tahalil, endorsed by Shaykh Ahmad al-Tahtawi.

Key Terms
الاستئجار على الطاعات (al-isti'jar 'ala al-ta'at): Hiring someone to perform acts of worship (e.g., Quran recitation, adhan, teaching Quran) for a fee.
الضرورة (al-darurah): A situation where failure to permit an otherwise prohibited act would lead to loss of religion or essential interests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did later Hanafi scholars permit hiring for teaching Quran?
A) Because it is always permissible to hire for any act of worship.
B) Due to necessity (darurah) because teachers' stipends stopped and without hiring, Quranic education would be lost.
C) Because the Quran itself allows hiring for its recitation.
D) Because the earlier Hanafi scholars had already permitted it.

Key Takeaway
A necessity-based fatwa is strictly limited to its cause; extending it without necessity invalidates the ruling and leads to corruption.

Correcting a Common Error: The Hanafi Position on the Blasphemer's Repentance
Correction of misconception about Hanafi ruling on blasphemer's repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authentic Hanafi position on the repentance of a blasphemer and apply the principle of source verification (maraja'ah ila al-makhadh al-asli) to correct later misattributions.

Core Idea
A mufti must return to the early texts to verify madhhab positions; later quotes may misattribute an ikhtilaf as the madhhab's own view.

This passage addresses a common pitfall in Hanafi ifta': the misattribution of a ruling on the blasphemer's repentance. Later scholars, including Ibn al-Humam, cited works from other madhhabs—like al-Shifa' of Qadi 'Iyad (Maliki) and al-Sarim al-Maslul of Ibn Taymiyya (Hanbali)—and erroneously claimed that the Hanafi school rejects repentance altogether. The author clarifies that these sources actually ascribe that view to the Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and one Maliki narration, while the authentic Hanafi position—preserved in early works like Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj—is that repentance is accepted. This lesson teaches the critical skill of verifying citations and distinguishing between intra-madhhab transmissions and inter-madhhab reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the error being corrected
The passage points to a widespread mistake: later Hanafi scholars (e.g., author of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, Ibn al-Humam) claimed that the Hanafi school does not accept the blasphemer's repentance and mandates execution. This ruling is actually from other schools. Recognise that the 'error' is a misattribution.
The claimant cited al-Shifa' and al-Sarim al-Maslul, but those works describe the Shafi'i/Hanbali view, not the Hanafi view.
2
Contrast the claimed position with the authentic one
The author contrasts what the later scholars said (repentance not accepted) with what the early Hanafi sources state (repentance accepted). Notice the explicit mention of early works: Kitab al-Kharaj, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Nutaf. These are from the nucleus of the madhhab.
The early sources are considered more authoritative because they are closer to the founding imams.
3
Understand the method of correction
The author does not simply assert the correct view; he shows the chain of misattribution: later scholars copied from each other without returning to the original sources. The corrective method is maraja'ah ila al-makhadh al-asli—returning to the original references.
This is a key adab al-mufti: always verify the source before issuing a fatwa.
4
Apply the lesson to ifta' practice
As a mufti, you must distinguish between what is actually in early Hanafi texts and what later commentators wrote. If a later work attributes a view to the Hanafi school, check the early sources. This passage trains you to be critical of chain citations.
The error here is not in the ruling itself but in its attribution. The correct Hanafi ruling is that repentance is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣- ومن ذلك مسألة عدم قبول توبة الساب للجناب الرفيع ، فقد نقل صاحب الفتاوى البزازية أنه يجب قتله عندنا، ولا تقبل توبته وإن أسلم وعزا ذلك إلى "الشفاء" للقاضي عياض المالكي، و"الصارم المسلول لابن تيمية الحنبلي. ثم جاء عامة من بعده وتابعه على ذلك، وذكروه في كتبهم، حتى خاتمة المحققين ابن الهمام، وصاحب "الدرر والغرر"، مع أن الذي في "الشفاء" و"الصارم المسلول": أن ذلك مذهب الشافعية والحنابلة وإحدى الروايتين عن الإمام مالك، الجزم بنقل قبول التوبة عندنا، وهو المنقول في كتب المذهب المتقدمة، ك "كتاب الخراج" لأبي يوسف، و"شرح مختصر الإمام الطحاوي"، و"النتف"، وغيرها من كتب المذهب، كما أوضحت ذلك غاية الإيضاح
3. Among that is the issue of non-acceptance of the repentance of the blasphemer against the noble personality (the Prophet). The author of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya narrated that he must be killed in our school, and his repentance is not accepted even if he embraces Islam, and he attributed that to al-Shifa' of Qadi 'Iyad al-Maliki and al-Sarim al-Maslul of Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali. Then many after him came and followed him on that, and mentioned it in their books, even the seal of the investigators Ibn al-Humam and the author of al-Durar wa al-Ghurar, whereas what is in al-Shifa' and al-Sarim al-Maslul is that it is the school of the Shafi'is and Hanbalis and one of two narrations from Imam Malik. The definitive transmitted position accepting repentance in our school is what is transmitted in the earlier books of the madhhab, such as Kitab al-Kharaj of Abu Yusuf, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Imam al-Tahawi, al-Nutaf, and other books of the madhhab, as I have explained in great detail.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage addresses a common error in later Hanafi fatwas regarding the repentance of a blasphemer (sabb al-rasul). Some later Hanafi scholars, including Ibn al-Humam, wrongly attributed to the Hanafi school the ruling that a blasphemer's repentance is not accepted and he must be killed regardless. The author corrects this by showing that the sources they cited (al-Shifa' and al-Sarim al-Maslul) actually state that this is the position of the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools, not Hanafi. The authentic Hanafi position, found in early authoritative texts like Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj, is that the repentance of a blasphemer is accepted. This is a classic example of the need for careful source verification (maraja'ah ila al-makhadh al-asli) in ifta'. The author emphasizes that even though some later scholars mentioned the contrary, the correct transmission (naql) from the early madhhab is acceptance of repentance.

Key Terms
الساب (al-sabb): One who curses or insults the Prophet Muhammad (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).
التوبة (al-tawbah): Sincere repentance from the sin of blasphemy, which in Hanafi school removes the liability to capital punishment if done before apprehension.
المراجعة إلى المخاذ الأصل (al-muraja'ah ila al-makhadh al-asli): Returning to the original sources for verification; a key adab al-mufti principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must still be executed because the sin is unforgivable.
B) His repentance is accepted, and he is not executed.
C) He is imprisoned for life.
D) He is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir).

Key Takeaway
The mufti must always verify the madhhab's ruling from early, authoritative sources (zahir al-riwayah) and be cautious of later works that may misattribute views from other schools.

The Necessity of Referring to Original Sources in Fatwa
Methodological rule with a case study on pawn liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Hanafi position on a disputed fatwa issue by verifying original sources, and apply the rule of referring to al-ma'khadh al-asli when issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
The correct madhhab is verified by original sources, not by the number of later books that repeat a ruling.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's works underscores a critical principle for muftis: a ruling found in multiple later authoritative books is not automatically the relied-upon position. The author demonstrates this with the case of pawn liability, where several later texts erroneously state a position contrary to the established Hanafi madhhab. You will learn how to trace a ruling back to its original source to ensure accuracy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is the liability of a pawner (rahin) when the pawned item is claimed to be destroyed. Some later books state that the pawner is liable for the full value if he cannot prove destruction, and not liable if he proves it.
This appears in al-Durar, Sharh al-Majma', and al-Tanwir.
2
Recognize the erroneous transmission
The author points out that these later books actually transmitted a ruling that matches the Maliki madhhab, not the Hanafi madhhab. The error originated from inaccurate citation or oversight.
Shaykh Khayr al-Din even gave a fatwa based on this erroneous transmission.
3
Trace the correct Hanafi position
The correct Hanafi position, as clarified in al-Shurunbulaliyya from al-Haqa'iq, is that the pawner is liable for the lesser of the value and the debt, regardless of whether destruction is proven by evidence or not.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Apply the principle to fatwa practice
A mufti must not rely solely on later compilations; he must verify rulings by consulting earlier authoritative texts (al-ma'khadh al-asli). The author's gloss Radd al-Muhtar is committed to this method.
This is a core rule of rasm al-mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لزوم المراجعة إلى المأخذ الأصلي بما لم أسبق إليه - والله تعالى الحمد والمنة – في كتاب سميته "تنبيه الولاة والحكام على أحكام شاتم عليه وعليهم الصلاة والسلام". -٤ خير الأنام، أو أحد أصحابه الكرام ومن ذلك مسألة ضمان الرهن بدعوى الهلاك، فقد ذكر في "الدرر" و"شرح المجمع" لابن ملك : أنه يضمن بدعوى الهلاك بلا برهان. وتبعهما في متن "التنوير". ومقتضاه أنه يضمن قيمته بالغة ما بلغت، أفتى العلامة الشيخ خير الدين، وأنه لا يضمن شيئا إذا برهن، م أن ذلك مذهب الإمام مالك، ومذهبنا ضمانه بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين، بلا فرق بين ثبوت الهلاك ببرهان وبدونه، كما أوضحه في "الشرنبلالية" عن "الحقائق"، ونبهت عليه في حاشيتي "رد المحتار على و به !! الدر المختار"، مع بيان من أفتى بما هو المذهب، ومن ردّ خلافه. ولهذا الذي ذكرناه نظائر كثيرة، اتفق فيها صاحب "البحر"، و"النهر"، و"المنح"، و"الدر المختار" وغيرهم، وهي سهو، منشأها الخطأ في النقل، أو سبق النظر. نبهت عليها في حاشيتي "رد المحتار"؛ لالتزامي فيها مراجعة الكتب المتقدمة التي يعزون المسألة إليها. فأذكر أصل العبارة التي وقع السهو في النقل عنها، وأضم إليها نصوص الكتب الموافقة لها، فلذا كانت تلك الحاشية عديمة النظير في بابها، لا يستغني عن تطلابها، أسأله سبحانه أن يُعينني على إتمامها. فإذا نظر قليل الاطلاع، ورأى المسألة مسطورة في كتاب أو أكثر، يظن أحد أن هذا هو المذهب، ويفتي به، ويقول: إن هذه الكتب للمتأخرين الذين اطلعوا على كتب من قبلهم وحرروا فيها ما عليه العمل، و لم يدر أن ذلك أغلبي، وأنه يقع منهم خلافه، كما سطرناه لك.
The Necessity of Referring to the Original Source. By that which I have not preceded to - and for Allah is all praise and favor - in a book I named 'Tanbih al-Wulat wa al-Hukkam 'ala Ahkam Shatim 'alayhi wa 'alayhim al-salat wa al-salam'. - Fourth: The best of mankind, or one of his noble companions. And among that is the issue of the guarantee of the pawn by a claim of destruction. It was mentioned in 'al-Durar' and 'Sharh al-Majma'' by Ibn Malik that he is liable by a claim of destruction without proof. And they were followed in the text of 'al-Tanwir'. And its implication is that he is liable for its value whatever it reaches, as the scholar Shaykh Khayr al-Din gave a fatwa, and that he is not liable for anything if he provides proof, and that is the madhhab of Imam Malik, and our madhhab is his liability for the lesser of its value and the debt, without distinction between establishing destruction by proof or without it, as clarified in 'al-Shurunbulaliyya' from 'al-Haqa'iq', and I alerted to it in my gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar', along with the explanation of who gave fatwa according to the madhhab and who rejected its contrary. And this which we have mentioned has many parallels, concerning which the authors of 'al-Bahr', 'al-Nahr', 'al-Minh', and 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' and others agreed, and they are oversights, whose origin is error in transmission or preceding opinion. I alerted to them in my gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar'; because of my commitment in it to review the earlier books to which they attribute the issue. So I mention the original phrase in which the error in transmission occurred, and I append to it the texts of the books that agree with it, so that gloss was unparalleled in its topic, indispensable for those who seek it. I ask Him, the Exalted, to help me complete it. So when a person of limited knowledge looks, and sees a issue recorded in one or more books, he thinks that this is the madhhab, and gives fatwa accordingly, and says: These books are by later scholars who examined the books of those before them and determined there what is practiced upon, and he does not know that this is the general case, and that contrary occurs from them, as we have recorded for you.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule for muftis: the need to refer back to original sources when issuing fatwas. The author begins by mentioning his own work 'Tanbih al-Wulat' concerning rulings on those who insult the Prophet. Then he presents a case study: the issue of the liability of a pawn when the pawner claims it was destroyed. Some later books like 'al-Durar' and 'Sharh al-Majma' state that the pawner is liable without proof, but the correct Hanafi position is that he is liable for the lesser of the value or the debt, regardless of proof. The author points out that many later works agreed on the erroneous ruling, which is a mistake due to inaccuracy in transmission or haste. He then mentions his own gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar' where he corrects such errors by tracing the original source. He warns that those with limited knowledge may assume that if a ruling appears in many later books, it must be the correct madhhab, but that is not always the case.

Key Terms
ضمان الرهن (daman al-rahin): Guarantee of the pawned item; liability of the pawner for the pawned item if it is destroyed
بدعوى الهلاك (bi-da'wa al-halak): By claiming destruction; the pawner claims that the pawned item was destroyed
المأخذ الأصلي (al-ma'khadh al-asli): The original source or reference for a legal ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is liable for the full value if he cannot prove destruction.
B) He is liable for the lesser of the value and the debt, regardless of proof.
C) He is not liable if he can prove destruction.
D) He is liable for the full value in all cases.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify rulings by tracing them to original sources, not rely solely on later compilations, as even authoritative works can contain transmission errors.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Obligation to Follow Zahir al-Riwayah in Fatwa
Definition and listing of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and apply the rule that fatwa must be based on these books unless later scholars have explicitly corrected a different transmission.

Core Idea
Fatwa defaults to the widely transmitted rulings; rare transmissions are only followed if explicitly corrected.

A mufti does not have the freedom to pick any ruling from any book. The Hanafi tradition has a strict hierarchy: the primary source for fatwa is the set of six books known as Zahir al-Riwayah, authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson explains what those books are and why they are authoritative, and outlines the conditions under which a rare transmission (riwayah shadhdhah) may be used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authority hierarchy
Recognize that the mufti must first consult Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage states that rulings from these books are followed even if not explicitly corrected, but if a correction from a non-Zahir source is made, the corrected ruling takes precedence.
2
Memorize the six book titles
Use the didactic poem to imprint the six books: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. These form the core canon.
The poem also mentions that the Nawadir and Nawazil are separate.
3
Distinguish Zahir al-Riwayah from other transmissions
Contrast Zahir al-Riwayah with rare transmissions (riwayah shadhdhah). The latter are not to be used unless specifically adopted by later scholars.
Shaykh al-Tarsusi's quote reinforces that a muqallid judge cannot judge by shadhdh riwaya.
4
Apply the rule to a hypothetical scenario
Suppose a ruling appears in al-Nawadir but not in any of the six books. The default is not to use it unless a later text like al-Hidayah corrects the six-book ruling or explicitly recommends it.
The phrase 'نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يتبع ما صححوه' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية
وقولي: "أو كان ظاهر الرواية إلخ " معناه أن ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرة، يفتى به وإن لم يصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يتبع ما صححوه.
قال العلامة الطرسوسي في "أنفع الوسائل" في مسألة الكفالة إلى شهر: "إن القاضي المقلد لا يجوز له أن يحكم إلا بما هو ظاهر الرواية، لا بالرواية الشاذة، إلا أن ينصوا على أن الفتوى عليها".
وكتب ظاهر الروايات أتت ستا وبالأصول أيضا سمّيت

الصغير والكبير والسير صنفها محمد الجامع

Obligation of fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah.
And my statement: 'or if it is Zahir al-Riwayah etc.' means that whatever rulings are in the books that are widely transmitted from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, are to be given fatwa by, even if they did not explicitly declare them correct. Yes, if they correct another ruling from non-Zahir al-Riwayah books, then they follow what they corrected.
Shaykh al-Tarsusi said in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il' regarding the issue of suretyship until a month: 'The muqallid judge is not permitted to judge except by what is in Zahir al-Riwayah, not by the rare transmission (al-riwaya al-shadhdha), unless they specify that the fatwa is upon it.'
And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came six, and by the principles also named.
Al-Shaybani authored in them the great Nu'mani madhhab.
Al-Saghir, al-Kabir, and al-Siyar, Muhammad composed al-Jami'.
Then al-Ziyadat with, and so, and al-Saghir, al-Mabsut, widespread with authentic chains.
He has the Nawadir books, their chains are not manifest in the books.
And after them the Nawazil issues, extracted by the shuyukh with proofs.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental rasm al-mufti rule: the mufti must give fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known transmitted rulings). The author explains that 'Zahir al-Riwayah' refers to rulings found in the books that are widely transmitted from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. These rulings are authoritative even if later scholars did not explicitly correct them. However, if scholars do correct a ruling from non-Zahir al-Riwayah sources, then that corrected ruling is followed. He then quotes Shaykh al-Tarsusi that a muqallid judge (who must follow the madhhab) cannot judge except by Zahir al-Riwayah, not by shadhdh (rare) transmissions, unless specifically stated that fatwa is upon it. The passage concludes with a didactic poem listing the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The poem also notes that the Nawadir (rare transmissions) and Nawazil (later case rulings) are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah. This teaches that the mufti must first rely on these six core books, and only turn to other books when necessary and when the scholars have indicated.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known and widely transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, compiled in six specific books.
رواية شاذة (Riwāyah Shādhah): Rare or weak transmissions that are not widely narrated; not to be acted upon unless specifically designated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Hidayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Bahr, al-Nahr

Key Takeaway
A mufti must base his fatwa on the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah unless later scholars have explicitly corrected a different transmission.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Obligation to Give Fatwa by Zahir al-Riwayah
Ruling on source hierarchy for Hanafi muftis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchy of Hanafi fatwa sources (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, Nawazil) and apply the rule that a mufti must base his fatwa on Zahir al-Riwayah unless a validated exception exists.

Core Idea
Fatwa must be based on the manifest transmission of the six books; unqualified muftis face severe punishment.

This passage from the commentary on 'Rasm al-Mufti' establishes a foundational principle: the mufti's authority is bound by the school's most reliable transmissions. It distinguishes the qualified mufti who can navigate the hierarchy from the unqualified who may cause corruption. It also defines the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah and their relation to the less authoritative Nawadir and Nawazil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage begins by stating that fatwa is obligatory according to Zahir al-Riwayah of the school. Identify this as the foundational principle.
Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the manifest transmissions in the six books.
2
Distinguish the qualified mufti (mahir)
The author contrasts the mahir (skilled mufti) with the unqualified. The mahir has a mental faculty to distinguish correct rulings and is fit to be a mediator between people and Allah.
The unqualified mufti who ascends to this position faces severe punishment (ta'zir).
3
Define Zahir al-Riwayah
The passage explains that issues in books narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with manifest transmission are to be followed even if not explicitly validated. However, if later scholars validate a narration from non-Zahir books, that validated opinion is followed.
This establishes the supremacy of Zahir al-Riwayah but allows exceptions when explicitly endorsed.
4
List the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
The poem enumerates the six books: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. All are by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
These books form the core of the reliable transmissions.
5
Understand the hierarchy beyond Zahir
Beyond the six books are the Nawadir (rare transmissions with weaker chains) and Nawazil (later fatwas extracted by later shaykhs). The hierarchy is: Zahir al-Riwayah > Nawadir (if validated) > Nawazil.
This hierarchy guides muftis in prioritizing sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتي وجوب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية المذهب، فلا يجوز تقليدهم فيها بخلاف الماهر الذي أخذ العلم عن أهله، وصارت له فيه ملكة نفسانية، فإنه يميز الصحيح من غيره، ويعلم المسائل وما يتعلق بها على الوجه المعتد به فهذا هو الذي يفتى الناس ويصلح أن يكون واسطة بينهم وبين الله تعالى، وأما غيره، فيلزمه إذا تسوّر هذا المنصب الشريف - التعزير البليغ والزجر الشديد الزاجر ذلك لأمثاله عن هذا الأمر القبيح الذي يؤدي إلى مفاسد لا تحصى. والله تعالى أعلم.
وجوب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية
وقولي: "أو كان ظاهر الرواية إلخ " معناه أن ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرة، يفتى به وإن لم يصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يتبع ما صححوه.
قال العلامة الطرسوسي في "أنفع الوسائل" في مسألة الكفالة إلى شهر: "إن القاضي المقلد لا يجوز له أن يحكم إلا بما هو ظاهر الرواية، لا بالرواية الشاذة، إلا أن ينصوا على أن الفتوى عليها".
وكتب ظاهر الروايات أتت ستا وبالأصول أيضا سمّيت

Explanation of the poem 'Rasm al-Mufti': The obligation of giving fatwa according to the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the school. So it is not permissible to follow them (those who are not qualified) therein, unlike the skilled one who has taken knowledge from its people and has acquired a mental faculty for it; he distinguishes the correct from others and knows the issues and what pertains to them in a reliable manner. This is the one who gives fatwa to people and is suitable to be a mediator between them and Allah Almighty. As for others, if he climbs this noble position, severe punishment and strong deterrence are necessary to deter his likes from this ugly matter that leads to countless corruptions. And Allah knows best. The obligation of giving fatwa by Zahir al-Riwayah. My saying: 'or it is from Zahir al-Riwayah, etc.' means that whatever issues are in the books that were narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with a manifest narration are given fatwa by, even if they did not explicitly validate it. Yes, if they validate another narration from non-Zahir al-Riwayah books, what they have validated is followed. Allamah Tarsusi said in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il' regarding the case of suretyship up to a month: 'A non-mujtahid judge may only judge by what is Zahir al-Riwayah, not by the odd narration (shadhdhah), unless they state that the fatwa is upon it.' The books of Zahir al-Riwayah are six, and they are also called the principles. Al-Shaybani compiled in them the Nu'mani school: the great, the small, and the Siyar. He authored the Jami', then the Ziyadat, with it also the small, al-Mabsut transmitted with sound chain. He has issues of Nawadir with chains in books non-Zahir, and after them issues of Nawazil extracted by the shaykhs with evidences.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) from the field of iftaa. It begins by stating the foundational principle: fatwa must be given according to the manifest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the Hanafi school. The author distinguishes between the qualified mufti (al-mahir) who has attained a deep understanding and can distinguish authentic from weak rulings, and the unqualified person who must not ascend to this noble position. For the latter, severe punishment is prescribed. The passage then defines 'Zahir al-Riwayah' as rulings found in books narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani with reliable chains, and these are to be followed even if not explicitly validated by later scholars. However, if later scholars validate an alternative narration from non-Zahir al-Riwayah sources, that validated opinion is followed. The author quotes Tarsusi to reinforce that a non-mujtahid judge must adhere to Zahir al-Riwayah. Finally, the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are enumerated in poetic form: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Beyond these are the Nawadir (rare transmissions) and then the Nawazil (later fatwas).

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifestly transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad in the six books, upon which fatwa is obligatory.
ماهر (mahir): A qualified mufti who has mastered the school and can distinguish authentic rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum requirement for a judge when giving a verdict?
A) He may use any narration he prefers.
B) He must base his verdict on Zahir al-Riwayah unless the odd narration is explicitly endorsed.
C) He must consult all six books but can choose any ruling.
D) He may only use the opinions of Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti is bound by the manifestly transmitted rulings (Zahir al-Riwayah) of the six books; only explicit endorsement by later scholars can authorize use of weaker transmissions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Three Levels of Hanafi Masail: Usul, Nawadir, and Nawazil
Classification of Hanafi legal rulings into three hierarchical strata.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three hierarchical layers of Hanafi masail and distinguish between the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir for fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Hanafi masail are hierarchically ranked: Usul (highest), Nawadir (lower), Nawazil (later) – fatwa rests on the highest.

In this passage, the author presents a foundational classification every Hanafi mufti must internalize. Understanding the three layers – Usul, Nawadir, and Nawazil – is essential for proper fatwa practice, as each layer carries different epistemological weight. This classification is not merely historical; it determines which ruling is operative in fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three layers
Name them: Masail al-Usul, Masail al-Nawadir, and the implied third (Nawazil). The passage explicitly discusses the first two, but later tradition adds Nawazil.
2
Understand the first layer (Usul/Zahir al-Riwayah)
These are rulings from the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) found in the six books of Muhammad (al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir). They are transmitted with strong chains (mutawatir or mashhur), giving them highest authority.
This is the default authority for fatwa.
3
Understand the second layer (Nawadir)
Rulings from the same founders but outside the six core books. They appear in other works by Muhammad (e.g., al-Kaysaniyat) or works by other early scholars (e.g., al-Mujarrad by Hasan ibn Ziyad, al-Amali of Abu Yusuf). Their chains are weaker, so they are not automatically relied upon.
They may be used if no Usul ruling exists, but with caution.
4
Recognize the compilation method of Amaali
The passage explains how Amaali books were created through dictation sessions: the scholar speaks, students write, then compile the notes into a book.
This illustrates how some Nawadir works were compiled.
5
Apply the hierarchy in fatwa
When giving fatwa, start with Usul. If no clear ruling, then check Nawadir. If still none, consult later Nawazil collections. Never skip layers without justification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طبقات المسائل
اعلم أن مسائل أصحابنا الحنفية على ثلاث طبقات: الأولى مسائل الأصول، وتسمى ظاهر الرواية أيضا، وهي مسائل رويت عن أصحاب المذهب، وهم أبو حنيفة، وأبو يوسف، ومحمد ، ويقال لهم "العلماء الثلاثة". وقد يلحق بهم زفر والحسن وغيرهما ممن أخذ الفقه عن أبي حنيفة، لكن الغالب الشائع في ظاهر الرواية أن يكون قول الثلاثة، أو قول بعضهم. ثم هذه المسائل التي تسمى بـ الرواية والأصول، هي ما وجد في كتب محمد التي هي "المبسوط"، و"الزيادات"، و"الجامع الصغير"، و"السير" الصغير"، و"الجامع الكبير" ، والسير الكبير. وإنما سميت بظاهر الرواية؛ لأنها رويت عن محمد ظاهر برواية الثقات، فهي ثابتة عنه إما متواترة أو مشهورة عنه. الثانية: مسائل النوادر، وهي مسائل مرويّة عن أصحاب المذهب المذكورين، لكن لا في الكتب المذكورة، بل إما في كتب أخر لمحمد غيرها كـ"الكيسانيات"، و"الهارونيات"، و"الجرجانيات"، و"الرقيات"، وإنما قيل لها غير ظاهرة الرواية؛ لأنها لم تُرو عن محمد بروايات ظاهرة ثابتة صحيحة كالكتب الأولى.
•
وإما في كتب غير محمد كـ كتاب "المجرد للحسن بن زياد وغيرها، ومنها كتب الأمالي لأبي يوسف و"الأمالي" جمع إملاء، وهو أن يقعد العالم - وحوله تلامذة بالمحابر والقراطيس فيتكلم العالم بما فتحه الله تعالى عليه من ظهر قلبه في العلم وتكتبه التلامذة، ثم يجمعون ما يكتبونه، فيصير كتابا، فيسمونه "الإملاء" و"الأمالي". وكان ذلك عادة
Layers of Issues. Know that the issues of our Hanafi companions are of three layers: The first is the issues of principles (usul), also called Zahir al-Riwayah, and they are issues narrated from the founders of the school: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, called the 'three scholars'. Zufar, al-Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa may also be joined to them, but the common prevailing in Zahir al-Riwayah is the statement of the three or some of them. Then these issues called al-Riwayah and al-Usul are what is found in the books of Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. They are called Zahir al-Riwayah because they were narrated from Muhammad manifestly by trustworthy narrators, so they are established from him either mutawatir or mashhur. The second: issues of al-Nawadir, which are issues narrated from the mentioned founders but not in the mentioned books; rather either in other books of Muhammad like al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, al-Ruqyat. They are called non-Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not narrated from Muhammad with manifest, established, correct chains like the first books. Or they may be in books other than Muhammad's, like the book al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and others, including the books of al-Amali by Abu Yusuf. 'Amali' is the plural of imla', which is when a scholar sits – around him students with inkwells and papers – and the scholar speaks what Allah has opened for him from his heart in knowledge, and the students write, then they gather what they write, and it becomes a book, so they call it 'al-Imla'' and 'al-Amali'. And that was a custom.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a systematic classification (qawida definition) of Hanafi legal sources into three hierarchical levels. The author states that Hanafi masail are of three layers: First, Masail al-Usul (also called Zahir al-Riwayah) – these are rulings narrated from the three main imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) found in the six books of Imam Muhammad. They are called 'Zahir al-Riwayah' because they are transmitted with strong chains, either mutawatir or mashhur. Second, Masail al-Nawadir – these are rulings from the same imams but not in the six books; instead they are in other books by Muhammad (like Kaysaniyat) or in books by other scholars (like al-Mujarrad by Hasan ibn Ziyad or the Amaali of Abu Yusuf). These are called 'non-Zahir al-Riwayah' due to weaker transmission. The third layer (Masail al-Nawazil) is not detailed here but is implied as later fatwa collections. The passage also explains how 'Amali' books were compiled through dictation sessions. This hierarchy is essential for proper fatwa practice: only Zahir al-Riwayah is default binding, while Nawadir require careful verification.

Key Terms
مسائل الأصول (masa'il al-usul): The fundamental issues of the Hanafi school, synonymous with Zahir al-Riwayah.
مسائل النوادر (masa'il al-nawadir): Rarely transmitted issues from the founders, found outside the six core books.
الأمالي (al-amali): Dictated works compiled from a scholar's oral sessions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What characterizes the second layer of Hanafi masail (Nawadir)?
A) They are found in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
B) They are transmitted through mutawatir chains.
C) They are narrated from the founders but not in the six core books.
D) They are rulings from later scholars only.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of Hanafi masail (Usul, Nawadir, Nawazil) dictates that fatwa must be based on the highest available authoritative layer, with Zahir al-Riwayah being the default.
