Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Three Layers of Hanafi Legal Issues: The Hierarchy of Authority
Classification of Hanafi masail into three authority layers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Hanafi legal issue into one of three authority layers and apply the hierarchy to determine which ruling is most authoritative for a fatwa.

Core Idea
Hanafi legal authority is sealed: Zahir al-Riwayah governs, Nawadir supplements, Later Fatawa adapts.

This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti introduces the essential rasm (rule) of Hanafi ifta: the three-layer hierarchy of masail. A mufti must know not just the law, but which stratum of transmission a ruling belongs to. This classification—usul/zahir al-riwayah, nawadir, and fatawa/waqi'at—determines the binding force of every opinion. We will unpack each layer and see how later compilations sometimes mix them, warning the student of a common error.

Guided Path
1
Name the three layers
Identify the three categories: usul (zahir al-riwayah), nawadir, and fatawa/waqi'at. Note that usul is also called 'zahir al-riwayah' and is the most authoritative.
These layers are based on the strength and reliability of transmission from the founders.
2
Map each layer to its source books
For layer 1, list the six books of Imam Muhammad (al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir). For layer 2, list other books of Muhammad (al-Kaysaniyyat, etc.) and books of other early scholars (al-Mujarrad, al-Amali). For layer 3, note later compilations like al-Nawazil, Majmu' al-Nawazil, al-Waqi'at, and mixed collections like Fatawa Qadikhan.
Layer 2 includes narrations not in the six core books, hence weaker.
3
Assess transmission strength
Layer 1 is mutawatir or mashhur, established with certainty. Layer 2 is not as widely transmitted (ghayr zahir al-riwayah). Layer 3 is derived by later mujtahids without direct transmission from the founders.
This affects the binding force: layer 1 is qat'i, layers 2 and 3 are zanni.
4
Identify the hierarchy of fatwa reference
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must first search the zahir al-riwayah corpus. If no ruling is found, then consult nawadir. Only if both fail, use later fatawa. Later scholars may contradict the founders only if they have stronger evidence.
This hierarchy is a fundamental rasm al-mufti.
5
Analyze a later compilation
Examine how some later books (like al-Muhit) maintain the distinction by listing usul first, then nawadir, then fatawa. Others (like Fatawa Qadikhan) mix layers, requiring the mufti to identify the source.
The author praises al-Muhit's method as a model.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن مسائل أصحابنا الحنفية على ثلاث طبقات: الأولى مسائل الأصول، وتسمى ظاهر الرواية أيضا، وهي مسائل رويت عن أصحاب المذهب، وهم أبو حنيفة، وأبو يوسف، ومحمد ، ويقال لهم "العلماء الثلاثة". وقد يلحق بهم زفر والحسن وغيرهما ممن أخذ الفقه عن أبي حنيفة، لكن الغالب الشائع في ظاهر الرواية أن يكون قول الثلاثة، أو قول بعضهم. ثم هذه المسائل التي تسمى بـ الرواية والأصول، هي ما وجد في كتب محمد التي هي "المبسوط"، و"الزيادات"، و"الجامع الصغير"، و"السير" الصغير"، و"الجامع الكبير" ، والسير الكبير. وإنما سميت بظاهر الرواية؛ لأنها رويت عن محمد ظاهر برواية الثقات، فهي ثابتة عنه إما متواترة أو مشهورة عنه. الثانية: مسائل النوادر، وهي مسائل مرويّة عن أصحاب المذهب المذكورين، لكن لا في الكتب المذكورة، بل إما في كتب أخر لمحمد غيرها كـ"الكيسانيات"، و"الهارونيات"، و"الجرجانيات"، و"الرقيات"، وإنما قيل لها غير ظاهرة الرواية؛ لأنها لم تُرو عن محمد بروايات ظاهرة ثابتة صحيحة كالكتب الأولى. • وإما في كتب غير محمد كـ كتاب "المجرد للحسن بن زياد وغيرها، ومنها كتب الأمالي لأبي يوسف و"الأمالي" جمع إملاء، وهو أن يقعد العالم - وحوله تلامذة بالمحابر والقراطيس فيتكلم العالم بما فتحه الله تعالى عليه من ظهر قلبه في العلم وتكتبه التلامذة، ثم يجمعون ما يكتبونه، فيصير كتابا، فيسمونه "الإملاء" و"الأمالي". وكان ذلك عادة السلف من الفقهاء والمحدثين وأهل العربية وغيرها في علومهم، فاندرست لذهاب العلم والعلماء - وإلى الله المصير – وعلماء الشافعية يسمون مثله "تعليقة". وإما بروايات مفردة مثل رواية ابن سماعة، و"معلى بن "منصور" وغيرهما في مسائل معينة. الثالثة الفتاوى والواقعات وهي مسائل استنبطها المجتهدون المتأخرون لما سئلوا عن ذلك، ولم يجدوا فيها رواية عن أهل المذهب المتقدمين. وهم أصحاب أبي يوسف ومحمد وأصحاب أصحابهما، وهلم جرا. وهم كثيرون، موضع معرفتهم كتب الطبقات لأصحابنا، وكتب التواريخ. فمن أصحاب أبي يوسف ومحمد حمله مثل عصام بن يوسف، وابن رستم، ومحمد بن سماعة وأبي سليمان الجوزجاني، وأبي حفص البخاري ومن بعدهم مثل محمد بن سلمة ومحمد بن مقاتل، ونصير بن يحى، وأبي النصر القاسم بن سلام. وقد يتفق لهم أن يخالفوا أصحاب المذهب لدلائل وأسباب ظهرت لهم. وأول كتاب جمع في فتواهم فيما بلغنا كتاب" النوازل" للفقيه أبي الليث السمرقندي، ثم جمع المشايخ بعده كتبا أخر، كـ"مجموع النوازل والواقعات للناطفي، والواقعات" للصدر الشهيد. ثم ذكر المتأخرون هذه المسائل مختلطة غير متميزة، كما في "فتاوى قاضي خان" و" الخلاصة" وغيرهما. وميز بعضهم كما في "كتاب المحيط" لرضي الدين السرخسي، فإنه ذكر أولا مسائل الأصول، ثم النوادر، ثم الفتاوى، ونعم ما فعل.
Know that the issues of our Hanafi companions are of three layers: The first: issues of usul (principles), also called zahir al-riwayah, and they are issues narrated from the founders of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad – they are called 'the three scholars'. Zufar, al-Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa may also be joined to them, but the prevalent majority in zahir al-riwayah is the statement of the three, or some of them. Then these issues, called riwayah and usul, are what is found in the books of Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. They are called zahir al-riwayah because they were narrated from Muhammad through apparent (clear) narrations of reliable narrators, so they are established from him either mutawatir or mashhur. The second: issues of nawadir (rare narrations), which are issues narrated from the aforementioned founders of the madhhab, but not in the mentioned books; rather either in other books of Muhammad besides those, such as al-Kaysaniyyat, al-Haruniyyat, al-Jurjaniyyat, and al-Ruqiyyat. They are called non-zahir al-riwayah because they were not narrated from Muhammad through apparent, established, authentic narrations like the first books. • And either in books other than Muhammad's, like the book al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and others, and among them are the books of al-Amali of Abu Yusuf. 'Al-Amali' is the plural of imla' (dictation), which is: a scholar sits with students around him holding inkwells and papers, and the scholar speaks what Allah opens for him from his heart in knowledge, and the students write it down; then they collect what they wrote, and it becomes a book, and they call it 'al-Imla'' and 'al-Amali'. This was the practice of the early scholars of fiqh, hadith, Arabic, and others in their sciences, but it became extinct due to the departure of knowledge and scholars – and to Allah is the destination. The Shafi'i scholars call the like of it 'ta'liqa'. • And either through isolated narrations such as the narration of Ibn Sama'a, Mu'alla ibn Mansur, and others in specific issues. The third: fatawa and waqi'at, which are issues deduced by the later mujtahids when they were asked about something and did not find a narration regarding it from the earlier madhhab founders. They are the companions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and the companions of their companions, and so on. They are many; their knowledge is found in the books of tabaqat of our companions and books of history. Among the companions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are: 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibn Rustam, Muhammad ibn Sama'a, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, Abu Hafs al-Bukhari; and after them: Muhammad ibn Salama, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Nasir ibn Yahya, and Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Salam. It may happen that they disagree with the founders of the madhhab due to proofs and reasons that became apparent to them. The first book compiled on their fatawa, as far as we know, is the book al-Nawazil by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Then later shaykhs compiled other books, like Majmu' al-Nawazil wa al-Waqi'at by al-Natafi, and al-Waqi'at by al-Sadr al-Shahid. Then the later scholars mentioned these issues mixed up without distinction, as in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa and others. Some distinguished them, as in the book al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he mentioned first the issues of usul, then the nawadir, then the fatawa – and what an excellent thing he did!
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational rasm (rule) of Hanafi usul al-ifta: the three-layer hierarchy of legal issues. The author, from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, begins by declaring that all Hanafi masail fall into three categories. The first layer is 'masail al-usul' (also called 'zahir al-riwayah'). These are rulings that are transmitted directly from the three primary founders – Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani – through reliable chains, primarily through the six books of Imam Muhammad (the 'zahir al-riwayah' corpus). These rulings carry the highest authority and are the backbone of the madhhab. The second layer is 'masail al-nawadir' (rare issues). These come from the same founders but are transmitted through less widely reported books (like al-Kaysaniyyat) or books of other early scholars (like al-Mujarrad of Hasan ibn Ziyad), or through individual narrations. Their authenticity is considered weaker than zahir al-riwayah, so they are not the primary reference for fatwa. The third layer is 'fatawa wa waqi'at' – issues deduced by later mujtahids when no explicit transmission from the early imams exists. These later scholars, like 'Isam ibn Yusuf and others, might even disagree with the founders based on new evidence. The text then notes how later compilations often mix these layers, but some like al-Muhit of Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi maintain the distinction, which is highly praised. The key point for a mufti: when issuing a fatwa, one must prioritize the layers: first zahir al-riwayah, then nawadir, then fatwa of later scholars, but always aware of the authority weight.

Key Terms
طبقات المسائل (tabaqat al-masail): The three-tier classification of Hanafi legal issues based on transmission strength and source: usul (zahir al-riwayah), nawadir, and fatawa/waqi'at.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the founders through clear, reliable chains, found in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare narrations from the founders that are not part of the six main books of Imam Muhammad; they are less authoritative.
الفتاوى والواقعات (al-fatawa wa al-waqi'at): Rulings derived by later mujtahids (mutakhkhirin) for novel issues not addressed in earlier transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following books belongs to the first layer (usul/zahir al-riwayah) of Hanafi legal issues?
A) Al-Mabsut by Imam Muhammad
B) Al-Mujarrad by Hasan ibn Ziyad
C) Al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi
D) Fatawa Qadikhan

Key Takeaway
The mufti must always prioritize rulings from zahir al-riwayah (first layer), then nawadir, then later fatawa, checking the authority layer before issuing a fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
8 min
The Three Classes of Legal Issues in Hanafi Iftaa
Classification of Hanafi legal sources into three tiers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the three classes of Hanafi rulings (usul, nawadir, fatawa) and apply the correct hierarchy when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must first consult the usul, then nawadir, and only then later fatwas.

This lesson introduces the foundational hierarchy (طبقات المسائل) that governs Hanafi iftaa. Understanding this classification is essential for a mufti to correctly prioritize sources and avoid relying on weaker positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Categories
Find in the passage the explicit naming of three classes: الأصول, النوادر, الفتاوى والواقعات. Note that they are listed in order of authority.
2
Define Each Category
Usul are the core transmitted texts from Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah). Nawadir are rare individual transmissions (e.g., from Ibn Sama'a). Fatawa are later rulings derived by mujtahids when no earlier transmission exists.
The Shafi'i equivalent is called ta'liqa.
3
Understand the Precedence
The mufti must first seek a ruling in usul; if not found, then in nawadir; if still not found, then in later fatawa. This hierarchy is binding.
Later scholars may oppose earlier ones if they have clear proof, but this is exceptional.
4
Analyze the Mixing Problem
Later compilations like Fatawa Qadi Khan mix categories without distinction, which can mislead a mufti. Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi's al-Muhit properly separates them, serving as a model.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Given a modern fatwa request, mentally trace the hierarchy: check al-Mabsut (usul), then al-Nawadir, then Fatawa Qadi Khan. Conclude based on the highest tier that contains a ruling.
Always cite the source tier when issuing the fatwa.

لرضي الدين السرخسي، فإنه ذكر أولا مسائل الأصول، ثم النوادر، ثم الفتاوى، ونعم ما فعل.

ملخصا
Classes of rulings. Commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: The predecessors among jurists, hadith scholars, linguists and others in their sciences passed away, so [their works] became extinct due to the loss of knowledge and scholars—and to Allah is the return. The Shafi'i scholars call something similar 'ta'liqa.' And [transmission] sometimes through individual transmissions like the transmission of Ibn Sama'a, and 'Ala' ibn Mansur, and others in specific issues. The third [category]: al-fatawa and al-waqi'at, which are issues inferred by later mujtahids when asked about them, and they did not find a transmission from the earlier scholars of the madhhab. They are the students of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and the students of their students, and so forth. They are numerous; the books of classes (tabaqat) of our scholars and history books are the place to know them. Among the students of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad one carries their madhhab, such as 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Ibn Rustam, Muhammad ibn Sama'a, Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, Abu Hafs al-Bukhari, and after them such as Muhammad ibn Salama, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Nasir ibn Yahya, and Abu al-Nasr al-Qasim ibn Sallam. It may happen that they oppose the scholars of the madhhab due to proofs and reasons that became apparent to them. The first book compiled on their fatwas, as far as we have heard, is the book 'al-Nawazil' by the jurist Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Then the later scholars compiled other books, such as 'Majmu' al-Nawazil wa al-Waqi'at' by al-Natiqi, and 'al-Waqi'at' by al-Sadr al-Shahid. Then later scholars mentioned these issues intermixed without distinction, as in 'Fatawa Qadi Khan' and 'al-Khulasa' and others. Some distinguished them, as in the book 'al-Muhit' by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he first mentioned the usul issues, then the nawadir, then the fatawa—and excellent is what he did. Copies of al-Mabsut: Know that the copies of al-Mabsut transmitted from Muhammad are numerous, the most apparent of which is the Mabsut of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani. A group of later scholars commented on al-Mabsut, such as Shaykh al-Islam Bakr known as 'Khawhar Zadah', which is called 'al-Mabsut al-Kabir', and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and others. Their Mabsuts are actually commentaries; they mentioned them intermixed with Mabsut Muhammad, just as the commentators of al-Jami' al-Saghir did, such as Fakhr al-Islam and Qadi Khan and others, so it is said: Qadi Khan mentioned it in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but what is meant is his commentary. Similarly in others. From 'Sharh al-Bayri 'ala al-Ashbah', and the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il al-Nabulsi on 'Sharh al-Durar'. Ended, summarized.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is about the classification of legal rulings (طبقات المسائل) in the Hanafi school, a fundamental principle for a mufti. It first notes that earlier works in various disciplines have become extinct due to loss of scholars. The Shafi'i equivalent is called 'ta'liqa' (a gloss). Then it enumerates three classes: First, the usul (core texts from Imam Muhammad's Zahir al-Riwayah). Second, the nawadir (rare transmissions via individual routes like Ibn Sama'a or 'Ala' ibn Mansur). Third, al-fatawa wa al-waqi'at (later fatwas by mujtahids like the students of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, who may sometimes diverge from earlier positions due to new evidence. The first collection of such fatwas was al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. Later works like Fatawa Qadi Khan mix categories; Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi's al-Muhit properly separates usul, nawadir, and fatawa. Finally, it discusses copies of Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut: the most authoritative is Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani's version; later commentaries, like Khawhar Zadah's, often interweave their own additions with the original text, similar to commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir. The passage thus establishes the hierarchy a mufti must follow: rely first on usul, then nawadir, then later fatwas.

Key Terms
طبقات المسائل (tabaqat al-masa'il): The hierarchical classification of Hanafi legal rulings into three layers: usul (core), nawadir (rare transmissions), and fatawa (later juristic opinions).
الأصول (al-usul): The core transmitted texts from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, i.e., Zahir al-Riwayah (the six books).
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare or unusual transmissions from early Hanafi authorities, not part of the standard corpus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Fatawa wa al-Waqi'at
B) Al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah)
C) Al-Nawadir
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The mufti must prioritize usul, then nawadir, then fatawa when issuing a fatwa.

Textual Criticism of al-Mabsut: Distinguishing Original from Commentary
Textual notes on the copies and commentaries of al-Mabsut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authoritative copy of al-Mabsut and differentiate between Imam Muhammad's original text and later commentary layers.

Core Idea
The most authoritative copy of al-Mabsut is Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani's; later commentaries must be distinguished from the core text.

This lesson delves into the textual transmission of one of the most important Hanafi usul works—al-Mabsut of Imam Muhammad. It highlights the practical challenge of source identification when multiple copies and commentaries interweave, a crucial skill for any mufti or researcher.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Multiple Copies
The passage states that al-Mabsut has multiple transmissions (نسخ متعددة). The most apparent (أظهرها) is that of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani.
2
Recognize the Commentaries
Later scholars wrote extensive commentaries on al-Mabsut, such as Khawhar Zadah (al-Mabsut al-Kabir) and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. These often intermix their own additions with the original text.
This is similar to commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir, where citations may actually refer to the commentary rather than the matn.
3
Understand the Implication
When a later authority like Qadi Khan says 'al-Mabsut,' they may mean the commentary, not the original. This can lead to misattribution if not checked.
4
Apply to Research
When citing a ruling from al-Mabsut, first verify which version is being referenced. Prefer al-Juzjani's transmission for core usul rulings.
Use editions that clearly distinguish the original text from commentary, like the printed edition of al-Mabsut with editing.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Distinguishing Zahir al-Riwayah from Riwayat al-Usul
Critical refinement of two key terms in Hanafi fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and identify when a Nawadir transmission qualifies as Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is broader than Riwayat al-Usul — it can include authoritative Nawadir transmissions.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, two terms are often conflated: Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha, in his commentary on al-Hidayah, clarifies that they are not identical. Using a case about a woman's obligation to perform Hajj, he shows that al-Sarakhsi considered a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (a Nawadir source) as Zahir al-Riwayah, even though it is not part of the six core Usul books. This distinction has profound implications for a mufti: the most authoritative ruling may come from outside the six books.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms in dispute
Locate the two terms in the passage: 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'Riwayat al-Usul'. Understand that Riwayat al-Usul refers strictly to the six books of Imam Muhammad, while Zahir al-Riwayah is a broader concept denoting the preponderant transmission.
The six books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami al-Saghir, al-Jami al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir.
2
Analyze the case study
Ibn Kamal Pasha presents a Hajj case: al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut says that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, a woman must own enough for her mahram's expenses. But al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah mention a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that if she can pay her own and her mahram's expenses, Hajj is obligatory. This narration is from al-Hasan, not from Muhammad, so it is from al-Nawadir. Yet al-Sarakhsi calls it Zahir al-Riwayah.
The key insight: al-Sarakhsi used 'Zahir al-Riwayah' for a Nawadir narration.
3
Apply the distinction to another scenario
If a mufti encounters a ruling attributed to Zahir al-Riwayah, he must check whether it comes from the six books or from a Nawadir source. If from Nawadir, it may still be the authoritative position if it is the most well-known and consistent transmission.
Example: The ruling on the 'umrah of a menstruating woman is in Nawadir but is considered Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Evaluate the disagreement
Some later Hanafi commentators denied any difference, claiming Nawadir can never be Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Kamal Pasha refutes them by pointing to al-Sarakhsi's usage and the fact that Muhammad's own narrations were sometimes contradictory.
The practical consequence: a mufti who ignores Nawadir may miss the relied-upon position.
5
State the mufta bihi
The preferred position (Ibn Kamal Pasha, al-Sarakhsi) is that Zahir al-Riwayah includes Nawadir when they are the most apparent and reliable transmission.
This is the operative rule for fatwa: Zahir al-Riwayah > Riwayat al-Usul in scope.

Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah, as he said in his commentary on al-Hidayah regarding the issue of the woman: what it summarizes is: 'It is mentioned in the Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi that according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is a condition that she owns enough for the expenses of her mahram. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if she is able to pay for her own expenses and those of her mahram, Hajj becomes obligatory upon her. And the narrations from Muhammad were contradictory.' Then he said: 'From this it becomes clear that al-Sarakhsi meant by Zahir al-Riwayah the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul becomes clear; for what is meant by al-Usul are al-Mabsut, al-Jami al-Saghir, al-Jami al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir, and the narration of al-Hasan is not in them, but all of them are from Muhammad. And it is known that the narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah, and what is meant by al-Nawadir is a narration other than the aforementioned usul. So memorize this, for the commentators of this book have been negligent of it, and some of them explicitly denied any difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, claiming that the narration of al-Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah.' I say: It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah: 'This is a narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa' does not necessarily mean it contradicts the usul narrations; it may be that al-Hasan narrated it in the books of al-Nawadir, or that Muhammad narrated it in the books of al-Usul, and they merely mentioned al-Hasan's narration because there is no contradiction from him, as evidenced by his statement: 'The narrations from Muhammad were contradictory.' At that point, al-Sarakhsi's statement that 'it is Zahir al-Riwayah'...
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the distinction between two key terms in Hanafi fatwa methodology: Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha, commenting on a Hajj issue in al-Hidayah, notes that al-Sarakhsi used 'Zahir al-Riwayah' to refer to a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, which is not part of the six foundational books (al-Usul: al-Mabsut, al-Jami al-Saghir, etc.). Thus, Zahir al-Riwayah is broader than Riwayat al-Usul; it can include Nawadir (rare narrations) as long as they are the most well-known and relied-upon position. The author stresses that many later commentators missed this point. This distinction is crucial for a mufti: when a ruling is attributed to 'Zahir al-Riwayah', it may come from a source outside the six books, but it still holds authoritative weight.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most apparent and authoritative transmission of a ruling, which may include narrations from non-Usul books (Nawadir) if they are widely accepted.
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): The narrations contained specifically in the six core books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami al-Saghir, al-Jami al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): All transmissions outside the six Usul books, such as those by Hasan ibn Ziyad or other early scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zahir al-Riwayah includes only the six books
B) Zahir al-Riwayah can include narrations from al-Nawadir
C) Riwayat al-Usul includes narrations from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad
D) They are identical terms

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah is not identical to Riwayat al-Usul; it can include Nawadir when they represent the preponderant view.

Meaning of al-Siyar and Classification of Books
Defining al-Siyar and distinguishing Zahir al-Riwayah from Nawadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, define al-Siyar, and identify the chronological hierarchy of the six core Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
A ruling is Zahir al-Riwayah if found in the six books; presence in Nawadir alone does not exclude it.

This lesson clarifies the classification of Hanafi legal sources and the meaning of 'Siyar'. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti to correctly weigh evidence and prioritize rulings. The passage discusses a key dispute about whether a ruling found in Nawadir can still be considered Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of Hanafi transmissions
Recognize that Zahir al-Riwayah (six books by Muhammad al-Shaybani) are the authoritative sources, while Nawadir are rare transmissions with lower authority.
This classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the basis for considering a ruling as Zahir al-Riwayah
If a ruling is also mentioned in the books of principles (i.e., the six books), it becomes Zahir al-Riwayah regardless of being in Nawadir. The author refutes the claim that Nawadir rulings can never be Zahir al-Riwayah.
The key is the presence in the six books.
3
Define 'Siyar' linguistically and technically
Linguistically, al-Siyar is plural of Sirah (way). In Sharia, it specifically refers to the Prophet's military expeditions (maghazi).
The correct pronunciation is with kasra on the seen and fatha on the ya.
4
Arrange the six books in chronological order and note hierarchy
Al-Mabsut (al-Asl) was first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Siyar al-Kabir. Later books take precedence over earlier ones in case of conflict.
Al-Siyar al-Kabir is the most relied-upon in matters of siyar.

Explanation of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti - 23 - Meaning of al-Siyar. The narration: its meaning is that Muhammad mentioned it in the books of principles, so it is one of the narrations from him. Thus it does not necessarily follow that a narration from the Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah; yes, it becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if mentioned in the books of principles. Likewise this issue: its mention in the books of Nawadir does not necessarily mean it has no mention in the books of principles. Rather what he said would be correct if it were established that this issue has no mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. The expressions of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira do not indicate that. Therefore, there is no basis to assert negligence against the commentators of al-Hidayah, whose statements agree with what we have presented. And Allah knows best. Meaning of al-Siyar: Supplement: al-Siyar is the plural of Sirah, which means the way in matters. In Sharia, it is specific to the military expeditions (maghazi), as in al-Hidayah. The Prophet's Sirah. He said in al-Mughrib: 'They said al-Siyar al-Kabir, describing it with the masculine adjective because it takes the place of the implied noun which is 'kitab', like saying 'Salat al-Zuhr'. 'Siyar al-Kabir' is a mistake, like 'Jami' al-Saghir' and 'Jami' al-Kabir'. Thus 'al-Siyar al-Kabir' is with kasra on the seen and fatha on the ya in the plural form, not with fatha on the seen and sukun on the ya in the singular form, as some who have no knowledge pronounce it. Al-Mabsut became famous as 'al-Asl' because it preceded the six books in authorship, and similarly al-Jami' al-Saghir after it, so what is in it is relied upon over al-Asl due to precedence. And the last of the year in authorship was al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is the relied-upon (book).
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion about the classification of Hanafi legal sources and the meaning of the term 'Siyar'. The author begins by clarifying that if a ruling is mentioned by Imam Muhammad in his books of principles (i.e., the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah), it is considered part of Zahir al-Riwayah. However, the mere fact that a ruling is found in the Nawadir (rare transmissions) does not automatically exclude it from being Zahir al-Riwayah; it becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also mentioned in the six books. The author refutes the claim that the commentators of al-Hidayah were negligent, arguing that their statements are consistent with this understanding. Then follows a supplement (tatimma) giving the lexical definition of 'Siyar' as the plural of 'Sirah' (way or conduct). In Islamic legal terminology, it specifically refers to the Prophet's military expeditions (maghazi). Next, the author corrects a common mispronunciation of 'al-Siyar al-Kabir' — it should be pronounced with kasra on the seen and fatha on the ya, as a plural, not as a singular. Finally, he explains the hierarchy of the early Hanafi texts: al-Mabsut (al-Asl) was compiled first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, and finally al-Siyar al-Kabir. Because al-Jami' al-Saghir came after al-Asl, its rulings take precedence over al-Asl in cases of apparent conflict. Al-Siyar al-Kabir, being the latest of the six, is the most relied-upon in matters of siyar.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted narrations (from Abu Hanifa) that are well-known and authoritative, compiled by Muhammad al-Shaybani in six books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions, narrations from Abu Hanifa or his companions that are not included in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, often transmitted by scholars like Hasan ibn Ziyad.
السير (al-Siyar): Plural of Sirah, meaning conduct; in Sharia, specifically refers to the Prophet's military expeditions (maghazi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) Al-Muhit
D) Al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
A ruling's authority depends on its presence in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, not on its absence from Nawadir.

Method of Preponderance: The Mufti and Muqallid in Cases of Disagreement
Rules for determining authoritative opinion for mufti and muqallid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchical rules for determining the preponderant opinion in the Hanafi school and apply them to distinguish the method of the mujtahid from the muqallid.

Core Idea
The mujtahid weighs proofs; the muqallid follows the last compilation unless later masters overrule.

This passage from Sharh al-Ashbah lays down a critical rasm al-mufti rule. It clarifies the different obligations of the mujtahid and the muqallid when authentic differences exist within the school. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for both issuing fatwa and following it correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between the mujtahid (capable of ijtihad) and the muqallid (lay follower). Each has a different method for determining the correct ruling.
The mujtahid must look at proofs (dalil); the muqallid must rely on scholarly authority.
2
State the duty of the mujtahid
The mujtahid must examine the proofs and determine the preponderant (rajih) opinion based on evidence, not on mere school authority.
This is a reminder that ijtihad is personal reasoning within the school framework.
3
State the duty of the muqallid
The muqallid should follow the 'last compilation' (al-tasnif al-akhir), which is identified as al-Siyar al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad. This is the default authority.
The muqallid does not weigh proofs; he relies on the latest authoritative compilation.
4
Note the exception for later mashayikh
If later scholars (mashayikh mutakhkhirin) choose an opinion contrary to the last compilation, the muqallid must follow that chosen opinion, even if it is the saying of Zufar (a weaker authority in the school).
This shows that authority is with the later consensus, not rigidity to older texts.
5
Recognize the ultimate authoritative texts
The passage highlights al-Kafi (collection of the six books) and its commentary al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi as the most reliable sources. Nothing works contrary to al-Mabsut.
These texts form the backbone of Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه ترجيح الراجح عند الاختلاف وفي "شرح الأشباه" للبيري: "قال علماؤنا : إذا كانت الواقعة مختلفا فيها، فالأفضل والمختار للمجتهد أن ينظر بالدلائل، وينظر إلى الراجح عنده والمقلد يأخذ بالتصنيف الأخير، وهو السير إلا أن يختار المشايخ المتأخرون خلافه فيجب العمل به ولو كان قول زفر ويجمع الست كتاب الكافي للحاكم الشهيد فهو الكافي أقوى شروحه الذي كالشمس مبسوط شمس الأمة السرخسي معتمد النقول ليس يعمل يخلفه وليس عنه يعدل منهم مبسوط شمس الأمة: فيه تغيير اقتضاه الوزن، فإنه ملقب بـ"شمس الأئمة"، جمع إمام. فائدة: لقب بـ"شمس الأئمة" جماعة أئمتنا، من شمس الأئمة الحلواني، ومنهم تلميذه شمس الأئمة السرخسي، ومنهم شمس الأئمة محمد عبد الستار الكردري، ومنهم شمس الأئمة بكر بن محمد الزرنجري، ومنهم ابنه شمس الأئمة عماد الدين عمر بن بكر بن محمد الزرنجري، ومنهم شمس الأئمة البيهقي، ومنهم شمس الأئمة الأوزجندي، واسمه محمود، وكثيرا ما يلقب بـ"شمس الإسلام"، كذا في "حاشية نوح آفندي" على الدرر "والغرر في فصل المهر.
Method of preponderance of the preferred opinion when there is disagreement. And in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Bayri: 'Our scholars said: When an incident is subject to disagreement, the best and chosen method for the mujtahid is to look at the proofs, and to look at what is preponderant in his view. The muqallid takes the last compilation, which is al-Siyar, unless the later mashayikh choose its opposite, then it is obligatory to act by it, even if it is the saying of Zufar. And the six books are collected in the book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, so it is sufficient; its strongest commentary, which is like the sun, is al-Mabsut of Shams al-Ummah al-Sarakhsi, the reliable source of transmissions, nothing works contrary to it and nothing is turned away from it. Al-Mabsut of Shams al-Ummah: in it there is a change required by meter, for he was nicknamed Shams al-A'immah, a plural of Imam. Benefit: The title Shams al-A'immah is given to a group of our imams: Shams al-A'immah al-Hulwani, his student Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, Shams al-A'immah Muhammad Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari, Shams al-A'immah Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, his son Shams al-A'immah Imad al-Din Umar ibn Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, Shams al-A'immah al-Bayhaqi, Shams al-A'immah al-Uzjandi, his name is Mahmud, and often he is nicknamed Shams al-Islam. As in the hashya of Nuh Afandi on al-Durar wa al-Ghurur in the chapter of mahr.'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule for determining the preponderant (rajih) opinion in cases of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between the mujtahid (one capable of ijtihad) and the muqallid (lay follower). The mujtahid must examine the proofs and identify the preponderant view based on evidence. The muqallid, however, should follow the 'last compilation' (al-tasnif al-akhir), which is identified as 'al-Siyar' (al-Siyar al-Kabir), unless later mashayikh have chosen a different opinion, in which case that opinion must be acted upon, even if it is the view of Zufar. The passage then emphasizes the reliability of the book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which collects the six main books of the school, and its commentary al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, described as the strongest commentary and the reliable source that cannot be substituted. Finally, it provides a benefit about the title 'Shams al-A'immah' (Sun of the Imams), listing several Hanafi scholars who bore this title, distinguishing it from 'Shams al-Islam'. This rule guides the mufti and muqallid in navigating disagreements within the school.

Key Terms
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion determined through evidence and proof.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who has the ability to derive rulings from proofs and weigh conflicting evidence.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A lay follower who does not have ijtihad capability and must follow the relied-upon school opinion.
التصنيف الأخير (al-tasnif al-akhir): The last compilation (al-Siyar al-Kabir) which is the final authority for the muqallid in cases of ikhtilaf.
الكافي (al-Kafi): A book by al-Hakim al-Shahid that collects the six main books of the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah).
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): A commentary on al-Kafi by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, considered the strongest and most reliable explanation.
شمس الأئمة (Shams al-A'immah): Title meaning 'Sun of the Imams', given to several prominent Hanafi scholars such as al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, and others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The opinion of the mujtahid

C) The view of Zufar always
D) The earliest compilation available

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule: the mujtahid uses proofs, the muqallid follows the last compilation unless later scholars select a different opinion, which then becomes binding.

The Authority of al-Kafi and al-Mabsut in Hanafi Fatwa
Establishing the textual hierarchy of fatwa sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchical relationship between al-Kafi and al-Mabsut and apply the rule that al-Mabsut is the ultimate authority for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the final authority for fatwa; no contrary opinion is acted upon.

A mufti must know which texts carry the greatest weight when deriving a fatwa. This passage from the tradition of Rasm al-Mufti establishes two foundational works: al-Kafi, a summary of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, and its commentary al-Mabsut, which holds supreme authority. The passage not only defines their relationship but also declares a binding rule: the mufti must rely on al-Mabsut and act upon its rulings to the exclusion of contrary opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key works
Locate the names 'al-Kafi' and 'al-Mabsut' in the passage. Note that al-Kafi is a compilation of Imam Muhammad's six books (Zahir al-Riwayah), and al-Mabsut is a commentary on al-Kafi by al-Sarakhsi.
Al-Kafi is also called a Mukhtasar (summary).
2
Extract the fatwa rule
Find the direct quote from al-Tarsusi: 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is such that one does not act contrary to it, does not rely except on it, does not give fatwa except by it, and does not depend except on it.' This is the operative rule for a mufti.
The rule is a dabt (sub-maxim) that governs fatwa methodology.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The passage explains that when 'al-Mabsut' is used generically, it refers to al-Sarakhsi's work. It also lists other Mabsuts but clarifies that al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is the one that holds ultimate authority. Al-Kafi is the base, but al-Mabsut is the authoritative commentary.
This hierarchy is crucial for resolving conflicts between sources.
4
Resolve the common misconception
The passage addresses a confusion by al-Khayr al-Ramli: al-Sarakhsi's statement about 'Sharh al-Mukhtasar' does not mean his work is a commentary on a different Mukhtasar. Al-Kafi itself is a Mukhtasar, so al-Mabsut is indeed a commentary on al-Kafi.
The passage uses evidence from Ghayat al-Bayan to support this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في "فتح القدير" وغيره: "إن "كتاب الكافي" هو جمع كلام محمد كتبه الست التي هي كتب ظاهر الرواية".
وفي شرح الأشباه للعلامة إبراهيم البيري: "اعلم أن من كتب مسائل الأصول كتاب الكافي للحاكم الشهيد، وهو كتاب معتمد في نقل المذهب، شرحه جماعة من المشايخ منهم شمس الأئمة السرخسي، وهو المشهور بـ" مبسوط السرخسي".
قال الشيخ إسماعيل النابلسي: قال العلامة الطرسوسي: مبسوط السرخسي لا يعمل بما يخالفه ولا يركن إلا إليه، ولا يفتى ولا يعول إلا عليه".
وذكر التميمي في طبقاته أشعارا كثيرة في مدحه، منها ما أنشده لبعضهم:
عليك بمبسوط السرخسي إنه هو البحر والدر الفريد مسائله ولا تعتمد إلا عليه فإنه يجاب بإعطاء الرغائب سائله
قال العلامة الشيخ هبة الله البعلي في شرحه على "الأشباه": "المبسوط" للإمام الكبير محمد بن محمد بن أبي سهل السرخسي، أحد الأئمة الكبار المتكلم الفقيه الأصولي، لزم شمس الأئمة عبد العزيز الحلواني وتخرج به حتى صار أنظر أهل زمانه، وأخذ بالتصنيف "وأملى "المبسوط" نحو خمسة عشر مجلدا، وهو في السجن بأوزجند، بكلمة كان فيها من الناصحين توفي سنة أربع مائة وتسعين".

وللحنفية مبسوطات كثيرة منها لأبي يوسف، ولمحمد ويسمى مبسوطه بـ "الأصل" ومبسوط الجرجاني، والخواهر زاده، ولشمس الأئمة الحلواني، ولأبي اليسر البزدوي، ولأخيه علي البزدوي، وللسيد ناصر الدين السمرقندي، ولأبي الليث نصر بن محمد.
"
وحيث أطلق المبسوط، فالمراد به مبسوط "السرخسی" هذا، وهو شرح "الكافي"، و"الكافي" هذا هو كافي الحاكم الشهيد، العالم الكبير، محمد ابن محمد أحمد بن بن عبد الله، ولّي قضاء بخارى، ثم ولاه الأمير المجيد، صاحب خراسان وزارته سمع الحديث من كثيرين، وجمع كتب محمد ابن الحسن في مختصره هذا ذكره الذهبي، وأثنى عليه.
وقال الحاكم في تاريخ نيسابور": ما رأيت في جملة من كتبت عنهم من أصحاب أبي حنيفة أحفظ للحديث وأهدى برسومه، وأفهم له منه. قتل ساجدا في ربيع الأول سنة أربع وثلاثين وثلاث مائة. قلت : وللحاكم الشهيد "المختصر"، و"المنتقى"، و"الإشارات" وغيرها. وقول السرخسي فرأيت الصواب في تأليف "شرح المختصر"، لا يدل على أن مبسوط السرخسي "شرح المختصر" لا شرح "الكافي" كما توهمه الخير الرملي في حاشية "الأشباه" فإن الكافي مختصر أيضاً؛ لأنه اختصر فيه كتب ظاهر الرواية كما علمت وقد أكثر النقل في "غاية البيان" عن "الكافي" بقوله : قال الحاكم الشهيد في مختصره المسمى بـ "الكافي". والله تعالى أعلم.
He said in "Fath al-Qadir" and others: "Indeed 'Kitab al-Kafi' is a compilation of the speech of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) from his six books which are the books of Zahir al-Riwayah."
And in Sharh al-Ashbah by Allamah Ibrahim al-Bayri: "Know that among the books of the issues of the principles is Kitab al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, and it is a relied-upon book in transmitting the madhhab. A group of mashayikh commented on it, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is famous as 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi'."
Shaykh Ismail al-Nabulsi said: Allamah al-Tarsusi said: "Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is such that one does not act contrary to it nor rely except on it, and one does not give fatwa except by it nor depend except on it."
And al-Tamimi mentioned in his Tabaqat many poems in its praise, among them what he quoted from someone:
"You must adhere to Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, for it is the sea and the unique pearl, its issues; do not depend except on it, for its asker is answered by granting desires."
Allamah Shaykh Hibat Allah al-Ba'li said in his commentary on al-Ashbah: "'Al-Mabsut' by the great Imam Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarakhsi, one of the great imams, the theologian, jurist, and usuli. He adhered to Shams al-A'imma Abd al-Aziz al-Halwani and graduated under him until he became the most insightful of the people of his time. He undertook authorship and dictated 'al-Mabsut' about fifteen volumes while he was in prison in Uzjand, due to a word he had uttered as one of the sincere advisors. He died in the year 490."

And the Hanafis have many Mabsuts, among them by Abu Yusuf, and by Muhammad, and his Mabsut is called 'al-Asl', and Mabsut al-Jurjani, and al-Khahar Zada, and by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and by Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, and by his brother Ali al-Bazdawi, and by al-Sayyid Nasir al-Din al-Samarqandi, and by Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad.
"
And wherever 'al-Mabsut' is used absolutely, it refers to this Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, and it is a commentary on 'al-Kafi', and this 'al-Kafi' is the Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid, the great scholar, Muhammad ibn Muhammad Ahmad ibn ibn Abd Allah. He was appointed judge of Bukhara, then the glorious prince, the ruler of Khurasan, appointed him as his vizier. He heard hadith from many and collected the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in this compendium. Al-Dhahabi mentioned him and praised him.
And al-Hakim said in Tarikh Naysabur: "I have not seen among those from whom I wrote among the followers of Abu Hanifa anyone more preserving of hadith, more guided in its ways, and more understanding of it than him." He was killed while prostrating in Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 334. I say: And al-Hakim al-Shahid has 'al-Mukhtasar', 'al-Muntaqa', 'al-Isharat' and others. And the statement of al-Sarakhsi, "I saw the correctness in authoring 'Sharh al-Mukhtasar'" does not indicate that Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is a commentary on 'al-Mukhtasar' and not a commentary on 'al-Kafi', as al-Khayr al-Ramli imagined in his Hashiyah on al-Ashbah, for al-Kafi is also a Mukhtasar because he summarized in it the books of Zahir al-Riwayah as you have learned. And he frequently transmitted in 'Ghayat al-Bayan' from 'al-Kafi' with his statement: "Al-Hakim al-Shahid said in his Mukhtasar called 'al-Kafi'." And Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a rasm_rule establishing the textual authority of two foundational Hanafi works: al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid and al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi. The passage begins by defining al-Kafi as a compilation of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, thus it is a primary source. It then notes that many scholars wrote commentaries on al-Kafi, the most famous being al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi. The authority of al-Mabsut is emphasized: it is the book that must be followed and relied upon for fatwa, and no contrary opinion is to be acted upon. The passage includes a poem praising al-Mabsut, and a biographical note about al-Sarakhsi, who dictated the work in prison. It then lists many other Mabsuts by Hanafi scholars, clarifying that when 'al-Mabsut' is used generically, it means al-Sarakhsi's work, which is a commentary on al-Kafi. The passage resolves a confusion by al-Khayr al-Ramli: al-Sarakhsi's statement about 'Sharh al-Mukhtasar' does not mean his Mabsut is a commentary on a different Mukhtasar, because al-Kafi itself is a mukhtasar (summary) of the Zahir al-Riwayah. Thus, the Mabsut is indeed a commentary on al-Kafi, as evidenced by frequent citations from al-Kafi in al-Sarakhsi's other work. The key rule for the mufti: al-Mabsut is the highest authority; al-Kafi is the foundational compilation; both are essential for fatwa.

Key Terms
الكافي (al-Kafi): A summary of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah compiled by al-Hakim al-Shahid.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The extensive commentary by al-Sarakhsi on al-Kafi, considered the highest authority for fatwa.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted texts from Imam Muhammad's six books; the core of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which book is considered the ultimate authority for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Kitab al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid
B) Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi
C) Al-Asl by Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Sharh al-Ashbah by Ibrahim al-Bayri

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate textual authority for Hanafi fatwa, and no other source may contradict it.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Distinguishing Qawlan and Riwayah in Hanafi Fatwa
Rasm rule on handling conflicting opinions and narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the difference between a mujtahid's two opinions (qawlan) and two narrations (riwayah), and apply the Hanafi rules for preferring between them according to the mufti's level.

Core Idea
A mujtahid cannot hold two contradictory opinions; the later opinion is final.

When transmitting rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa, a mufti may encounter two apparently conflicting statements. Are these his own changing views (qawlan) or errors in transmission (riwayah)? This lesson clarifies the distinction and provides a clear hierarchy for resolving such conflicts, essential for sound fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of conflict
Determine whether the conflict is between two opinions directly from the mujtahid (qawlan) or between two narrations (riwayah) attributed to him. The former originates from the mujtahid himself; the latter from the transmitters.
2
Apply rules for qawlan
If it is qawlan, first check if a chronological order is known. The later opinion is considered a retraction. If no date is known, look for internal strength or other preferencing factors. A qualified follower (mujtahid fil-madhhab) may use his heart's testimony.
3
Apply rules for riwayah
If it is riwayah, the error is in the narration, not the imam. Examine the reliability of the transmitters and chains. The more authentic narration is preferred.
4
Determine the acting person's level
The procedure differs based on who is making the choice: a mujtahid, a follower with ijtihad capacity, a mutafaqqih (fiqh student), or a common person (ammi). Each has a different guidance.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a case
Given a specific case with two conflicting transmissions, classify the conflict, apply the appropriate rule, and determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi) following the hierarchy.
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف القول والرواية
واعلم بأن عن أبي حنيفه جاءت روايات غدت منيفه
اختار منها بعضها والباقي يختار
منه
سائر الرفاق
فلم يكن لغيره جواب كما عليه أقسم الأصحاب
[القولان لمجتهد]
اعلم بأن المنقول عن عامة العلماء في كتب الأصول : أنه لا يصح في مسألة لمجتهد قولان للتناقض، فإن عرف المتأخر منهما تعين كون ذلك رجوعا، وإلا وجب ترجيح المجتهد بعده بشهادة قلبه، كما في بعض كتب الحنفية المشهورة. وفي بعضها أنه إن لم يعرف تاريخ، فإن نقل في أحد القولين عنه ما يقويه، فهو الصحيح عنده، وإلا فإن وجد متبع بلغ الاجتهاد في المذهب، رجح بما مر من المرجحات إن وجد، وإلا يعمل بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه. وإن كان عاميا اتبع فتوى المفتي فيه الأتقى الأعلم. وإن كان متفقهاً تبع المتأخرين، وعمل بما هو أصوب وأحوط عنده. كذا في "التحرير" للمحقق ابن الهمام.
اختلاف القول والرواية ]
واعلم أن اختلاف الروايتين ليس من باب اختلاف القولين؛ لأن القولين نص المجتهد عليهما بخلاف الروايتين، فالاختلاف في القولين من جهة المنقول عنه لا الناقل والاختلاف في الروايتين بالعكس، كما ذكره المحقق ابن أمير حاج في "شرح التحرير".
لكن ذكر بعده عن الإمام أبي بكر البليغي في "الدرر" : أن الاختلاف في الرواية عن أبي حنيفة من وجوه:
Difference of Opinion and Narration. And know that from Abu Hanifa have come narrations that became lofty. Some of them he chose, and the rest are chosen by the rest of the associates. So there is no answer for others, as the companions have sworn. Two Opinions for a Mujtahid: Know that what is transmitted from the general body of scholars in usul works is that it is not valid for a mujtahid to have two opinions on one issue because of contradiction. If the later of the two is known, then that is determined to be a retraction. Otherwise, the mujtahid must prefer afterwards by the testimony of his heart, as in some famous Hanafi books. In some [books], if the date is not known, and in one of the two opinions there is something transmitted that strengthens it, then that is the correct one according to him. Otherwise, if there is a follower who has reached the level of ijtihad in the madhhab, he gives preference by the aforementioned preferencing factors if they exist; otherwise, he acts by whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart. If [the questioner] is a common person, he follows the fatwa of the mufti who is most pious and most knowledgeable. If he is a mutafaqqih (one who has studied fiqh), he follows the later scholars and acts by what is most correct and most precautionary according to him. This is in al-Tahrir by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam. Difference of Opinion and Narration: And know that the difference of two narrations is not of the category of difference of two opinions. Because the two opinions are explicitly stated by the mujtahid, unlike the two narrations. So the difference in two opinions is from the perspective of the one from whom it is transmitted, not the transmitter, and the difference in two narrations is the opposite, as mentioned by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Hajj in Sharh al-Tahrir. However, he mentioned after that from Imam Abu Bakr al-Balighi in al-Durar that the difference in narration from Abu Hanifa is of several types:
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage addresses a key rasm al-mufti rule regarding how to handle conflicts in legal transmission from a mujtahid (specifically Abu Hanifa). First, it establishes that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory opinions on a single issue; if he does, the later one is considered his final position. If the chronological order is unknown, the mujtahid (or a qualified scholar) must prefer based on internal strength or his heart's conviction. For a common person, they ask the most qualified mufti; for a mutafaqqih (intermediate student), they follow the later scholars' preference. Then, the passage distinguishes between 'ikhtilaf al-qawl' (difference of opinion, where the imam himself expressed two views) and 'ikhtilaf al-riwayah' (difference of narration, where the discrepancy is due to narrators, not the imam). In ikhtilaf al-riwayah, the error lies with the transmitter, so the scholar must investigate the reliability of the transmissions. The passage cites al-Balighi's al-Durar, indicating that there are multiple types of such differences in narrations from Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
قولان (qawlan): Two explicitly stated opinions by a mujtahid on the same issue, which cannot both be valid simultaneously.
رواية (riwayah): A transmission from the imam through a chain; differences in riwayah are attributed to the narrators, not the imam.
متفقه (mutafaqqih): One who has studied fiqh to some depth but has not reached ijtihad; follows later scholars' preferences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two contradictory narrations from Abu Hanifa are found and the dates are unknown, how should a mufti who is a common person (ammi) act?
A) He chooses the one that seems stronger to his heart.
B) He follows the fatwa of the most pious and knowledgeable mufti.
C) He follows the opinion of the later scholars.
D) He suspends judgment and does not give a fatwa.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting transmissions from a mujtahid must be resolved by distinguishing qawlan from riwayah and applying the appropriate preference hierarchy based on the actor's level.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Resolving Contradictory Statements from a Mujtahid
Rule for resolving contradictory statements from a mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy for resolving conflicting statements attributed to a Hanafi mujtahid, distinguishing the duties of a mujtahid, mutafaqqih, and commoner.

Core Idea
A mujtahid cannot hold two contradictory opinions; the later statement abrogates the earlier.

Mujtahids of the past sometimes left conflicting rulings on the same issue. How do we determine which one represents their final view? The Hanafi usul tradition provides a clear protocol: chronology first, then preponderators, then personal judgment. This lesson walks through that hierarchy as laid out by Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the general principle
Recognize that two contradictory statements cannot both be valid from one mujtahid on the same issue. Contradiction (تناقض) is logically impossible.
This is a usul maxim, not a fiqh ruling.
2
Check chronology
If the dates of the statements are known, the later statement (متأخر) is considered a retraction of the earlier one, and it becomes the relied-upon position.
This assumes the mujtahid is the same person; if statements from different mujtahids, other rules apply.
3
If chronology is unknown – mujtahid's own action
If the mujtahid is alive, he should prefer one statement by his own ijtihad (shahadat qalb). If deceased, the follower takes over.
The phrase 'شهادة قلبه' 'testimony of his heart' indicates a type of ijtihad.
4
Apply the hierarchy for followers
Identify the level of the follower: a mujtahid fil madhhab uses preponderators (murajjahat); if none, he may choose by his heart. A mutafaqqih follows the later scholars and chooses what is more correct and cautious. A commoner follows the most pious and knowledgeable mufti.
Preponderators include strength of evidence, number of narrators, etc. (mentioned earlier in the text).
5
Simulate a scenario
Take a case: two conflicting reports from Abu Hanifa on the sale of absent property. Dates unknown. You are a mutafaqqih. According to the hierarchy, you follow later Hanafi scholars and choose the ruling they deemed more correct and precautionary.
This avoids arbitrary personal choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم بأن المنقول عن عامة العلماء في كتب الأصول : أنه لا يصح في مسألة لمجتهد قولان للتناقض، فإن عرف المتأخر منهما تعين كون ذلك رجوعا، وإلا وجب ترجيح المجتهد بعده بشهادة قلبه، كما في بعض كتب الحنفية المشهورة. وفي بعضها أنه إن لم يعرف تاريخ، فإن نقل في أحد القولين عنه ما يقويه، فهو الصحيح عنده، وإلا فإن وجد متبع بلغ الاجتهاد في المذهب، رجح بما مر من المرجحات إن وجد، وإلا يعمل بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه. وإن كان عاميا اتبع فتوى المفتي فيه الأتقى الأعلم. وإن كان متفقهاً تبع المتأخرين، وعمل بما هو أصوب وأحوط عنده. كذا في "التحرير" للمحقق ابن الهمام.
Know that what is transmitted from the generality of scholars in the books of usul is that it is not valid for a mujtahid to have two statements in one issue due to contradiction. If the later of the two is known, then it is determined to be a retraction. Otherwise, the mujtahid must prefer (one) after that by the testimony of his heart, as in some famous Hanafi books. In some of them: if the date is not known, and in one of the two statements there is something that strengthens it, then that is the correct one according to him. Otherwise, if there is a follower who has reached ijtihad in the madhhab, he gives preponderance by the preponderators mentioned earlier if found. Otherwise, he acts with whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart. If he is a commoner, he follows the fatwa of the mufti who is most pious and most knowledgeable. If he is a mutafaqqih, he follows the later scholars and acts with what is more correct and more cautious according to him. Thus in al-Tahrir by the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule regarding how to handle conflicting statements attributed to a single mujtahid on the same issue. The general principle is that a mujtahid cannot simultaneously hold two contradictory opinions on one matter, as that would be logically inconsistent. If the chronology is known, the later statement is considered a retraction of the earlier. If the chronology is unknown, the mujtahid himself, if still alive, should prefer one by his own heart (ijtihad). For a follower (muqallid) who has reached the level of ijtihad within the madhhab, he uses the established preponderators (murajjahat) to choose. If no preponderator is found, he may choose either by his heart. For a commoner (ammi), he follows the fatwa of the most pious and knowledgeable mufti. For a mutafaqqih (a student of fiqh), he follows the later scholars and chooses what is more correct and more precautionary.

Key Terms
قولان (qawlan): Two conflicting statements or opinions attributed to a mujtahid on the same issue.
متأخر (muta'akhkhir): The later of two statements in time, which indicates retraction if known.
متفقهاً (mutafaqqih): A person who has studied fiqh and is capable of distinguishing preferred opinions but not a full mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the date of two conflicting statements from Abu Hanifa on the same issue is unknown, what should a follower who has reached ijtihad in the madhhab do?
A) Follow the statement of the most pious mufti.
B) Use established preponderators (murajjahat) to prefer one.
C) Choose either by the testimony of his heart.
D) Act with whichever is more cautious.

Key Takeaway
Two statements from one mujtahid cannot both be valid; the later abrogates the earlier, and followers must follow a clear hierarchy based on their level of knowledge.

Distinguishing Ikhtilaf al-Qawl from Ikhtilaf al-Riwayah
Clarifying different types of conflicts in juristic transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ikhtilaf al-qawl and ikhtilaf al-riwayah, and identify the aspects of ikhtilaf al-riwayah according to Hanafi usul al-iftaa.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf al-riwayah stems from transmission; ikhtilaf al-qawl from the mujtahid himself.

When a mufti encounters conflicting rulings attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is crucial to determine whether the conflict arises from a genuine change of opinion (ikhtilaf al-qawl) or from transmission issues (ikhtilaf al-riwayah). This passage, from a work on rasm al-mufti, explains the distinction and lists the possible sources of ikhtilaf al-riwayah. Understanding this distinction helps the mufti correctly prioritize and apply the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of conflict
State in your own words the difference between ikhtilaf al-qawl and ikhtilaf al-riwayah. Note that ikhtilaf al-qawl involves two explicit statements from the mujtahid, while ikhtilaf al-riwayah involves conflicting reports about what the mujtahid said.
2
List the four aspects of ikhtilaf al-riwayah from al-Balighi
From the passage, enumerate the four reasons ikhtilaf al-riwayah can occur: error in hearing, unawareness of retraction, qiyas vs istihsan, and ruling vs precaution.
3
Analyse the author's critique
The commentator (qultu) argues that except for the first aspect (error in hearing), the others actually stem from the mujtahid himself. Explain why he says this, and why he concludes the first two aspects are not truly distinct from ikhtilaf al-qawl.
Note the reference to Imam Muhammad's compilations.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
After critique, the author suggests restricting ikhtilaf al-riwayah to the last two aspects (qiyas vs istihsan, and ruling vs precaution) plus the possibility of mujtahid hesitation. State what this means for a mufti's practice.
This is a practical rule for resolving conflicting narrations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن اختلاف الروايتين ليس من باب اختلاف القولين؛ لأن القولين نص المجتهد عليهما بخلاف الروايتين، فالاختلاف في القولين من جهة المنقول عنه لا الناقل والاختلاف في الروايتين بالعكس، كما ذكره المحقق ابن أمير حاج في "شرح التحرير". لكن ذكر بعده عن الإمام أبي بكر البليغي في "الدرر" : أن الاختلاف في الرواية عن أبي حنيفة من وجوه: منها: الغلط في السماع، كأن يجيب بحرف النفي إذا سئل عن حادثة، ويقول : لا يجوز ، فيشتبه على الراوي فينقل ما سمع. ومنها: أن يكون له قول قد رجع عنه ويعلم بعض من يختلف إليه رجوعه فيروي الثاني والآخر لم يعلمه فيروي الأول. ومنها: أن يكون قال أحدهما على وجه القياس، والآخر على وجه الاستحسان، فيسمع كل واحد أحدهما، فينقل كما سمع". ومنها: أن يكون الجواب في مسألة من وجهين: من جهة الحكم، ومن جهة الاحتياط، فينقل كل كما سمع. قلت: فعلى ما عدا الوجه الأول يكون الاختلاف في الروايتين من جهة المنقول عنه أيضا لابتناء الاختلاف فيهما على اختلاف القولين المرويين، فيكونان من باب واحد ويؤيده أن ناقل الروايتين قد يكون،واحدا، فإن إحدى الروايتين قد تكون في كتاب من كتب الأصول، والأخرى في كتب النوادر ، بل قد يكون كل منهما في كتب الأصول، والكل من جَمْع واحد وهو الإمام محمد حله، وهذا ينافي الوجه الأول، ويبعد الوجه الثاني، فالأظهر الاقتصار على الوجهين الأخيرين، لكن لا في كل فرع اختلفت فيه الرواية، بل بعض ذلك قد يكون لأحدهما، والبعض الآخر للآخر. لكن هذا إنما يتأتى فيما يصلح أن يكون فيه قياس واستحسان أو احتياط وغيره، نعم! يتأتى الوجهان الأولان فيما إذا اختلف الراوي. وقد يقال: إن من وجوه الاختلاف أيضا، تردد المجتهد في الحكم لتعارض الأدلة عنده بلا ،مرجح أو لاختلاف رأيه في مدلول الدليل
And know that the difference between the two narrations is not of the category of difference between the two statements, because the two statements are the explicit text of the mujtahid upon them, unlike the two narrations. Thus the difference in statements arises from the one from whom it is transmitted (manqul 'anhu), not the transmitter, while the difference in narrations is the opposite, as mentioned by the muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Haj in Sharh al-Tahrir. However, he mentioned after that from Imam Abu Bakr al-Balighi in al-Durar that the difference in narration from Abu Hanifa has several aspects: among them: error in hearing, such as when he answers with the particle of negation when asked about an incident and says 'it is not permissible', then the narrator is confused and transmits what he heard. Among them: that he has a statement from which he has retracted, and some of those who attend to him know his retraction, so he narrates the second, while another did not know it, so he narrates the first. Among them: that he said one of them by way of qiyas, and the other by way of istihsan, then each of two listeners hears one of them and narrates as he heard. Among them: that the answer in an issue has two aspects: from the aspect of legal ruling and from the aspect of precaution (ihtiyat), so each narrator narrates as he heard. I (the author) say: However, aside from the first aspect, the difference in narrations is also from the aspect of the one from whom it is transmitted (manqul 'anhu), because the difference in them is based on the difference of the two statements that are narrated. Thus they become of the same category. This is supported by the fact that the transmitter of the two narrations may be one person, for one of the two narrations may be in a book of usul and the other in the books of nawadir, indeed both may be in the books of usul, and all from the single compilation of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). This contradicts the first aspect and makes the second aspect unlikely. Thus the most apparent is to restrict to the last two aspects, but not in every branch where the narration differs; rather, some of that may be for one aspect and the other for another. But this only applies in what can have qiyas and istihsan or precaution and other than that. Yes! The first two aspects apply when the narrators differ. It may also be said: among the aspects of difference is also the mujtahid's hesitation in the ruling due to conflicting evidences without a preponderator, or his disagreement concerning the meaning of the evidence.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti clarification distinguishing between two types of differences in transmitted rulings: ikhtilaf al-qawl (difference in statements) and ikhtilaf al-riwayah (difference in narrations). The key distinction is that in ikhtilaf al-qawl, the mujtahid himself explicitly held two different opinions (possibly due to retraction), while in ikhtilaf al-riwayah, the conflict arises from the transmission process. The author then lists four aspects of how ikhtilaf al-riwayah can occur, as reported from al-Balighi: (1) error in hearing, (2) unawareness of a retraction, (3) one statement based on qiyas and the other on istihsan, and (4) one answer being from the aspect of ruling and the other from precaution. After listing them, the author (the commentator) critiques these aspects, arguing that except for the first (error in hearing), the others ultimately stem from the mujtahid himself (manqul 'anhu), thus they revert to ikhtilaf al-qawl. He supports this by noting that both narrations may come from the same transmitter (Imam Muhammad) in different books. Therefore, he suggests restricting ikhtilaf al-riwayah to the last two aspects (qiyas vs istihsan, and ruling vs precaution) plus a fifth possibility: the mujtahid's own hesitation due to conflicting evidence.

Key Terms
اختلاف القولين (ikhtilaf al-qawlayn): Conflict between two statements explicitly attributed to the mujtahid himself, indicating a change of opinion.
اختلاف الروايتين (ikhtilaf al-riwayatayn): Conflict between two narrated reports about the mujtahid's ruling, possibly due to transmission issues.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference based on equity, contrary to qiyas in some cases.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary approach, giving a ruling that is more cautious in case of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which aspect of ikhtilaf al-riwayah does the author (qultu) consider as truly separate from ikhtilaf al-qawl?
A) The mujtahid having retracted a statement without the narrator knowing.
B) Error in hearing (ghalat fi al-sama').
C) One statement based on qiyas and the other on istihsan.
D) The mujtahid's hesitation due to conflicting evidence.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between ikhtilaf al-qawl and ikhtilaf al-riwayah is crucial for a mufti to correctly resolve conflicting rulings.
