Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Rulings in the Hanafi Madhhab
Establishes the order of preference among Hanafi imams' opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for preferring opinions among the founding imams and apply it to determine the mufta bihi position when a ruling is disputed.

Core Idea
When Imams differ: Abu Hanifa → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad → Zufar/Hasan.

A mufti or judge within the Hanafi madhhab often encounters conflicting narrations from the founding imams. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti, with its classic commentary, establishes a clear hierarchy for resolving such conflicts. More importantly, it clarifies the limits of a non-mujtahid mufti's freedom to choose, ensuring that fatwas remain grounded in the madhhab's strongest transmitted opinions.

Guided Path
1
Extract the hierarchy order
Read the poem and commentary: list the imams in the order of precedence when issuing a fatwa. Note that Abu Hanifa's ikhtiyār (chosen opinion) comes first, followed by Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al‑Shaybani, then Zufar and al‑Hasan ibn Ziyad.
The hierarchy applies whether or not a later imam agreed with the earlier one.
2
Define 'ikhtiyār'
Understand that ikhtiyār means the imam's own preponderated opinion, not merely a narrated report. The hierarchy relies on recorded ikhtiyār; if none exists for an imam, we move to the next.
Muhammad al‑Shaybani often distinguishes Abu Yusuf's name when narrating from Abu Hanifa out of adab.
3
Analyze the ikhtilāf on companions' consensus
When the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad) agree on a ruling against Abu Hanifa, there is a scholarly difference: some allow the mufti to choose, others restrict choice to the mujtahid mufti. Identify the two views and note which is considered more correct.
The author cites al‑Fatawa al‑Sirajiyya and al‑Tanwir to settle the issue.
4
Differentiate mufti levels
Contrast a non‑mujtahid mufti (muqallid) with a mujtahid mufti (a 'mujtahid fi al‑madhhab'). The hierarchy binds the former; the latter may prefer the stronger evidence.
A mujtahid mufti can overrule the hierarchy if the evidence clearly supports a lower imam's view.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
If a question arises on which Abu Hanifa left no recorded ikhtiyār, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad give different answers: first adopt what Abu Yusuf chose (since he is next), then Muhammad if Abu Yusuf also has no ikhtiyār.
If both companions agree against Abu Hanifa, a non‑mujtahid mufti still follows Abu Hanifa (by hierarchy).

شرح عقود رسم المفتي

تخريجات المشايخ على قواعد الإمام الإمام، فكثير منها مبني على قواعد لهم خالفوا فيها قواعد الإمام؛ لأنهم لم يلتزموا قواعده كلها، كما يعرفه من له معرفة بكتب الأصول. نعم! قد يقال: إذا كانت أقوالهم روايات عنه - على ما مر – تكون تلك القواعد له أيضا لابتناء تلك الأقوال عليها. وعلى هذا أيضا تكون نسبة التخريجات إلى مذهبه أقرب ؛ لابتنائها على قواعده التي رجحها وبنى أقواله عليها. فإذا قضى القاضي بما صح منها، نفذ قضاؤه، كما ينفذ بما صح من أقوال الأصحاب.
فهذا ما ظهر لي تقريره في هذا الباب من فتح الملك الوهاب، والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب، وإليه المرجع والمآب.
وحيث لم يوجد له اختيار فقول يعقوبَ هو المختارُ محمد فقوله الحسنُ ثم زفر وابن زياد الحسن
ثم
وقيل بالتخيير في فتواه إن خالف الإمام صاحباه وقيل من دليله أقوى رُجح وذا لمفت ذي اجتهاد الأصح

الترتيب بين روايات المذهب
قد علمت ما قررناه آنفا أن ما اتفق عليه أئمتنا، لا يجوز لمجتهد في مذهبهم أن يعدل عنه برأيه؛ لأن رأيهم أصح.
وأشرت هنا إلى أنهم إذا اختلفوا يقدم ما اختاره أبو حنيفة، سواء وافقه أحد أصحابه أو لا، فإن لم يوجد له اختيار قدم ما اختاره يعقوب، وهو اسم أبي يوسف أكبر أصحاب الإمام، وعادة الإمام محمد أنه يذكر أبا يوسف بكنيته إلا إذا ذكر معه أبا حنيفة، فإنه يذكره باسمه العلم، فيقول: "يعقوب عن أبي حنيفة"، وكان ذلك بوصية من أبي يوسف تأدباً مع شيخه أبي حنيفة – رحمهم الله جميعا ورحمنا بهم، وأدام بهم النفع إلى يوم القيامة – وحيث لم يوجد لأبي يوسف اختيار، قدم قول محمد بن الحسن أجل أصحاب أبي حنيفة بعد أبي يوسف، ثم بعده يقدم قول زفر والحسن بن زياد، فقولهما في رتبة واحدة لكن عبارة "النهر": ثم بقول الحسن. وقيل: إذا خالفه أصحابه وانفرد بقول يتخير المفتي. وقيل: لا يتخير إلا المفتي المجتهد، فيختار ما كان دليله أقوى.
قال في "الفتاوى السراجية : ثم الفتوى على الإطلاق على قول أبي حنيفة ثم قول أبي يوسف، ثم قول محمد، ثم قول زفر والحسن بن زياد. وقيل: إذا كان أبو حنيفة في جانب، وصاحباه في جانب، فالمفتي بالخيار. والأول أصح إذا لم يكن المفتي مجتهدا. ومثله في متن "التنوير" أول كتاب القضاء.
Commentary on the Treatise on the Code of the Mufti. The derivations of the scholars (mashayikh) upon the principles of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) - many of them are based on their own principles in which they differed from the Imam's principles because they did not adhere to all his principles, as known by one familiar with books of usul. Yes, it may be said: if their statements are narrations from him - as previously mentioned - then those principles are also his because those statements are based on them. Based on this, the attribution of the derivations to his madhhab is closer because they are based on his principles which he preponderated and built his statements upon. So if a judge judges according to what is sound among them, his judgment is executed, just as it is executed with what is sound from the statements of the companions. This is what appeared to me to establish in this chapter from Fath al-Malik al-Wahhab. And Allah knows best the truth, and to Him is the return and destination. And where there is no choice (ikhtiyar) for him, then the statement of Ya'qub is the chosen one; then Muhammad, then his statement; then al-Hasan, then Zufar and Ibn Ziyad al-Hasan. Then it is said: there is choice in his fatwa if the two companions oppose the Imam. And it is said: the one whose evidence is stronger is preponderant, and this is for a mufti who has ijtihad. The order among the narrations of the madhhab. You have already learned what we established earlier: that what our Imams agreed upon is not permissible for a mujtahid within their madhhab to deviate from with his own opinion, because their opinion is more correct. And I indicated here that when they differ, what Abu Hanifa chose is given precedence, whether one of his companions agrees with him or not. Then if no choice is found for him, what Ya'qub chose is given precedence - and he is Abu Yusuf, the greatest of the Imam's companions. The usual practice of Imam Muhammad is that he mentions Abu Yusuf by his kunya except when he mentions him with Abu Hanifa, then he mentions him by his given name, saying 'Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa', and that was by a bequest from Abu Yusuf out of respect for his teacher Abu Hanifa - may Allah have mercy on them all and have mercy on us through them, and make benefit continuous through them until the Day of Judgment. And where no choice is found for Abu Yusuf, the statement of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan is given precedence - he is the most eminent of Abu Hanifa's companions after Abu Yusuf. Then after him, the statement of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad is given precedence, and their statements are on the same rank, but the wording of al-Nahr is: 'then the statement of al-Hasan.' And it is said: if the companions oppose him and he is alone in a statement, the mufti may choose. And it is said: only the mujtahid mufti may choose, and he chooses the one whose evidence is stronger. It is stated in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya: 'Then the fatwa in absolute terms is on the statement of Abu Hanifa, then the statement of Abu Yusuf, then the statement of Muhammad, then the statement of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.' And it is said: if Abu Hanifa is on one side and his two companions on the other, the mufti has a choice. And the first is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid. And similar is in the text of al-Tanwir at the beginning of the Book of Judges.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage establishes the hierarchical rule for preferring opinions within the Hanafi madhhab when the founding imams differ. The passage is a rasm rule (methodological rule for issuing fatwas) from the text Rasm al-Mufti, with commentary. The author begins by explaining that derivations (takhrijat) of later scholars upon the principles of Abu Hanifa are often based on their own principles, not necessarily Abu Hanifa's. However, if those derivations are based on his principles that he himself preponderated, then they are attributable to his madhhab. If a judge rules by a sound opinion from such derivations, his judgment is valid. Then the passage presents the well-known hierarchy: when the imams differ, first follow what Abu Hanifa chose (his ikhtiyar), whether or not any companion agreed with him. If no choice is reported from Abu Hanifa, then follow Abu Yusuf's choice. If none from Abu Yusuf, then follow Muhammad al-Shaybani. Then after him, Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad are on par, though some say al-Hasan is preferred. There is also a discussion: if the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree against Abu Hanifa, there is ikhtilaf: some say the mufti may choose, others say only the mujtahid mufti may choose based on strength of evidence. The author cites al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya affirming the hierarchy and preferring the first view (no choice for non-mujtahid) when the mufti is not a mujtahid. This is critical for practitioners: a non-mujtahid mufti must follow the established hierarchy, while a mujtahid within the madhhab may exercise tarjih by evidence.

Key Terms
اختيار (ikhtiyar): The preferred or chosen opinion of an imam, established by his own ijtihad and tarjih.
قول (qawl): A statement or legal opinion attributed to an imam, forming part of the madhhab's corpus.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of determining which opinion is stronger or more preponderant within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy in this passage, if no ikhtiyar is found from Abu Hanifa, and none from Abu Yusuf, whose opinion is given precedence next?
A) Zufar
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) al-Hasan ibn Ziyad
D) A later scholar like al-Haskafi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must follow a fixed hierarchy of imams' opinions: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar/Hasan; only a mujtahid mufti may depart based on evidence strength.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
Hierarchy of Transmissions in the Hanafi School
Establishes the order of preference among Hanafi imams for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hierarchy of Hanafi opinions to determine the preferred opinion for fatwa, distinguishing between the role of a non-mujtahid and a mujtahid mufti.

Core Idea
The mufti must follow a precise chain: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then others — unless he is a mujtahid, then he follows the strongest proof.

This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti lays out the foundational hierarchy for prioritizing different opinions within the Hanafi school. It is essential for any mufti to know whether to follow the foundational imams or to weigh evidence independently. The text provides the golden rule: when the imams agree, that is binding; when they differ, a strict order of preference applies, with an important exception for the mujtahid mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default hierarchy
List the imams in order of preference: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, then Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. Understand that when Abu Hanifa has a chosen opinion, it takes precedence over all others.
The hierarchy is based on the principle that the Imam's opinion is more correct (ra'yuhum aṣaḥḥ).
2
Recognize the exception for mujtahid mufti
Note that the hierarchy is binding for non-mujtahid muftis. A mujtahid mufti, capable of weighing proofs, may choose based on strength of evidence rather than the fixed hierarchy.
The term 'mujtahid' here refers to ijtihad within the madhhab, not absolute ijtihad.
3
Analyze the scenario when Sahibayn agree against Abu Hanifa
This is the main point of dispute. Some masters say the mufti is free to choose; the preferred view (al-aṣaḥḥ) says the hierarchy still holds for non-mujtahids, while a mujtahid mufti may choose according to proof.
The passage quotes al-Sirajiyya: 'al-awwal aṣaḥḥ idhā lam yakun al-mufti mujtahidan'.
4
Understand the rule from al-Hawi
When Abu Hanifa has no transmission, follow Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then others in seniority. When the companions agree with Abu Hanifa, deviation is only for necessity.
This rule is from the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
5
Apply the criterion of dalil strength
The ultimate standard for a mujtahid mufti is the strength of evidence, not mere hierarchy. The passage concludes: 'al-ṣaḥīḥ anna al-‘ibra li-qūwa al-dalīl'.
This does not negate the hierarchy for non-mujtahids.

شرح عقود رسم المفتي
الترتيب بين روايات المذهب
قد علمت ما قررناه آنفا أن ما اتفق عليه أئمتنا، لا يجوز لمجتهد في مذهبهم أن يعدل عنه برأيه؛ لأن رأيهم أصح.
وأشرت هنا إلى أنهم إذا اختلفوا يقدم ما اختاره أبو حنيفة، سواء وافقه أحد أصحابه أو لا، فإن لم يوجد له اختيار قدم ما اختاره يعقوب، وهو اسم أبي يوسف أكبر أصحاب الإمام، وعادة الإمام محمد أنه يذكر أبا يوسف بكنيته إلا إذا ذكر معه أبا حنيفة، فإنه يذكره باسمه العلم، فيقول: "يعقوب عن أبي حنيفة"، وكان ذلك بوصية من أبي يوسف تأدباً مع شيخه أبي حنيفة – رحمهم الله جميعا ورحمنا بهم، وأدام بهم النفع إلى يوم القيامة – وحيث لم يوجد لأبي يوسف اختيار، قدم قول محمد بن الحسن أجل أصحاب أبي حنيفة بعد أبي يوسف، ثم بعده يقدم قول زفر والحسن بن زياد، فقولهما في رتبة واحدة لكن عبارة "النهر": ثم بقول الحسن. وقيل: إذا خالفه أصحابه وانفرد بقول يتخير المفتي. وقيل: لا يتخير إلا المفتي المجتهد، فيختار ما كان دليله أقوى.
قال في "الفتاوى السراجية": ثم الفتوى على الإطلاق على قول أبي حنيفة ثم قول أبي يوسف، ثم قول محمد، ثم قول زفر والحسن بن زياد. وقيل: إذا كان أبو حنيفة في جانب، وصاحباه في جانب، فالمفتي بالخيار. والأول أصح إذا لم يكن المفتي مجتهدا. ومثله في متن "التنوير" أول كتاب القضاء.
وقال في آخر كتاب "الحاوي القدسي": ومتى لم يوجد في المسألة عن أبي حنيفة رواية، يؤخذ بظاهر قول أبي يوسف، ثم بظاهر قول محمد، ثم بظاهر قول زفر والحسن وغيرهم الأكبر فالأكبر إلى آخر من كبار الأصحاب. وقال قبله ومتى كان قول أبي يوسف ومحمد موافق قوله لا يتعدى عنه إلا فيما مست إليه الضرورة، وعلم أنه لو كان أبو حنيفة رأى ما رأوا، لأفتى به وكذا إذا كان أحدهما معه. فإن خالفاه في الظاهر، قال بعض المشايخ: يأخذ بظاهر قوله. وقال بعضهم: المفتي مخيّر بينهما، إن شاء أفتى بظاهر قوله، وإن شاء أفتى بظاهر قولهما. والأصح أن العبرة لقوة الدليل".
والحاصل أنه إذا اتفق أبو حنيفة وصاحباه على جواب، لم يجز العدول عنه إلا لضرورة، وكذا إذا وافقه أحدهما. وأما إذا انفرد عنهما بجواب وخالفاه فيه، فإن انفرد كل منهما بجواب أيضا، بأن لم يتفقا على شيء واحد فالظاهر ترجيح قوله أيضا وأما إذا خالفاه واتفقا على جواب واحد حتى صار هو في جانب وهما في جانب، فقيل: يرجح قوله أيضا، وهذا قول الإمام عبد الله بن المبارك. وقيل: يتخير المفتي. وقول "السراجية": "والأول أصح إذا لم يكن المفتي مجتهدا" يفيد اختيار القول الثاني إن كان المفتي مجتهدا.
ومعنى تخييره أنه ينظر في الدليل فيفتي بما يظهر له، ولا يتعين عليه قول الإمام. وهذا الذي صححه في "الحاوي" أيضا بقوله: "والأصح أن العبرة لقوة الدليل؛ لأن اعتبار قوة الدليل شأن المفتي المجتهد."
Explanation of the contract: Rasm al-Mufti
Arrangement between the transmissions of the madhhab:
You have already learned what we established earlier: that what our imams agreed upon, it is not permissible for a mujtahid within their madhhab to deviate from it by his own opinion, because their opinion is more correct.
And I indicated here that when they differ, what Abu Hanifa chose is given precedence, whether one of his companions agrees with him or not. If no choice of his is found, what Ya'qub chose is given precedence – and he is Abu Yusuf, the greatest of the Imam's companions. The habit of Imam Muhammad is that he mentions Abu Yusuf by his kunya except when he mentions him with Abu Hanifa, then he mentions him by his personal name, saying: 'Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa.' This was by the will of Abu Yusuf out of respect for his teacher Abu Hanifa – may Allah have mercy on them all and grant us mercy through them, and perpetuate benefit through them until the Day of Judgment –. And where no choice of Abu Yusuf is found, the statement of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the most learned of Abu Hanifa's companions after Abu Yusuf, is given precedence. Then after him, the statement of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad is given precedence; their statements are in one rank, but the expression of al-Nahr is: 'then the statement of al-Hasan.' And it is said: If his companions oppose him and he alone holds a statement, the mufti may choose. And it is said: Only the mujtahid mufti may choose, and he chooses whichever has the stronger proof.
It is said in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya: 'Then fatwa absolutely follows the statement of Abu Hanifa, then the statement of Abu Yusuf, then the statement of Muhammad, then the statement of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. And it is said: If Abu Hanifa is on one side and his two companions on the other, then the mufti has the choice. The first view is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid.' Similar is in the text of al-Tanwir at the beginning of the Book of Judgement.
And he said at the end of the book al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'Whenever there is no transmission from Abu Hanifa on an issue, the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent statement of Muhammad, then the apparent statement of Zufar and al-Hasan and others, the greater then the greater, up to the last of the senior companions.' And he said before that: 'Whenever the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agrees with his statement, one should not deviate from it except in cases of dire necessity, and it is known that if Abu Hanifa had seen what they saw, he would have given fatwa accordingly. Similarly if one of them agrees with him. If they oppose him apparently, some masters said: one takes his apparent statement. And some said: the mufti has the choice between them – if he wishes, he gives fatwa according to his apparent statement, and if he wishes, he gives fatwa according to their apparent statement. The most correct is that the criterion is the strength of the proof.'
The summary is that if Abu Hanifa and his two companions agree on an answer, it is not permissible to deviate from it except for necessity, and similarly if one of them agrees with him. As for when he alone holds an answer and they oppose him in it – if each of them also holds a separate answer, i.e., they do not agree on one thing, then apparently his statement is also given preponderance. As for when they oppose him and agree on one answer, so that he is on one side and they on the other, some said: his statement is also given preponderance – this is the saying of Imam Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak. And some said: the mufti has the choice. And the saying of al-Sirajiyya: 'The first view is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid' indicates the preference for the second saying if the mufti is a mujtahid.
And the meaning of his having choice is that he looks at the proof and gives fatwa according to what appears to him, and the Imam's statement is not binding on him. This is what was also corrected in al-Hawi with his saying: 'The most correct is that the criterion is the strength of the proof; because considering the strength of the proof is the concern of the mujtahid mufti.'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses the crucial methodological rule of the hierarchy between different transmissions and opinions within the Hanafi madhhab. It is a parsing exercise in the rules of fatwa: when the founding imams differ, which opinion should the mufti prefer? The text first reiterates the fundamental principle: whatever the imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) have agreed upon cannot be abandoned for mere personal opinion. The hierarchy then proceeds: first the chosen opinion of Abu Hanifa; if he has no explicit choice, then the chosen opinion of Abu Yusuf (Ya'qub); then Muhammad ibn al-Hasan; then Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad in the same rank, though some prefer al-Hasan. The text notes a dispute: when the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on a position opposite to Abu Hanifa, some say the mufti is free to choose, while the preferred view (aṣaḥḥ) restricts this freedom to a mujtahid mufti. For a non-mujtahid mufti, the safer path is to follow the earlier hierarchy. The passage further details the view in al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī: in the absence of any transmission from Abu Hanifa, one follows the apparent statements of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then others in order of seniority. When Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree with Abu Hanifa, deviation is impermissible except under necessity; if they oppose him, some masters favor his statement, others give the mufti choice. The ultimate criterion emphasized is the strength of proof (qūwa al-dalīl), which is the hallmark of the mujtahid mufti. This passage thus equips the student with a detailed framework for prioritizing conflicting texts within the school, balancing the authority of the founding imams with the mufti's ijtihad.

Key Terms
اختيار (ikhtiyār): The preferred or chosen opinion of an imam within the school.
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known transmitted opinion of an imam.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A mufti capable of weighing proofs and making independent tarjih within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy presented in this passage, what is the first step when Abu Hanifa's chosen opinion is not known?
A) Take the opinion of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
B) Take the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
C) Take the opinion of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
D) The mufti may choose any opinion freely.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of opinions in the Hanafi school prioritizes Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then others, and is binding for non-mujtahid muftis, while mujtahid muftis may follow the strongest proof.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Hierarchy When Imam and Sahibayn Differ
Explaining the ranking of imams' opinions for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of rulings when Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree, distinguishing between a mujtahid and non-mujtahid mufti.

Core Idea
When Imam and Sahibayn differ, the mufti’s authority determines the rule: non-mujtahid follows Imam, mujtahid weighs evidence.

This lesson clarifies a foundational rule in Hanafi ifta: what does a mufti do when the founding imams give conflicting answers? You will learn the three internal opinions and the relied-upon position that distinguishes based on the mufti's level of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize when there is a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and both Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Note also cases where one agrees with Imam or when no Imam text exists.
2
List the Three Internal Opinions
The passage presents three views: (1) Follow Imam absolutely (Ibn al-Mubarak), (2) Mufti has free choice, (3) Distinction between mujtahid and non-mujtahid.
These apply only when both Sahibayn oppose Imam and agree on a single answer.
3
Apply the Tarjih (Preference)
The third opinion (tafsil) is most correct: if the mufti is not a mujtahid, he must follow Imam’s view; if he is a mujtahid, he may choose based on strength of evidence.
This is affirmed by Qadi Khan and in Al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
4
Handle Special Cases
If one Sahib agrees with Imam, there is consensus to follow that. If no Imam text exists, non-mujtahid follows Abu Yusuf then Muhammad; mujtahid may choose.
Also, in matters like muzara'ah or judging by apparent integrity, the Sahibayn's opinion may be taken due to later consensus.

The ordering among the narrations of the madhhab. And he said at the end of the book 'Al-Hawi al-Qudsi': Whenever there is no narration from Abu Hanifa on an issue, the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent statement of Muhammad, then the apparent statement of Zufar and al-Hasan and others, the senior then the senior, up to the last of the senior companions. And he said before it: And whenever the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree with his statement, one does not deviate from it except when necessity compels, and it is known that if Abu Hanifa had seen what they saw, he would have given a fatwa accordingly; likewise if one of them is with him. If they both apparently oppose him, some of the mashayikh said: He takes his apparent statement. And some said: The mufti has a choice between them; if he wishes, he gives a fatwa according to his apparent statement, and if he wishes, he gives a fatwa according to their apparent statement. And the most correct is that the consideration is for the strength of the evidence. The summary: When Abu Hanifa and his two companions agree on an answer, it is not permissible to deviate from it except for necessity, and likewise if one of them agrees with him. But if he alone has an answer and they oppose him, and each of them also has a separate answer (i.e., they do not agree on one thing), then apparently his statement is preferred. But if they oppose him and agree on one answer such that he is on one side and they are on the other, it is said: his statement is preferred as well—this is the statement of Imam 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak. And it is said: the mufti has a choice. And the statement in 'Al-Sirajiyya': 'The first is more correct if the mufti is not a mujtahid' indicates choosing the second opinion if the mufti is a mujtahid. The meaning of his choice is that he looks at the evidence and gives a fatwa according to what appears to him, and he is not bound by the Imam's statement. This is what was corrected in 'Al-Hawi' as well by his saying: 'The most correct is that the consideration is for the strength of evidence, because considering the strength of evidence is the affair of the mujtahid mufti.' The ruling when the two companions oppose the Imam. So concerning when the two companions oppose him, there are three opinions: First: following the Imam's statement without choice. Second: absolute choice. Third—and it is the most correct—the distinction between the mujtahid and other. Qadi Khan affirmed this, as will come. And apparently this is a reconciliation between the two opinions by carrying the opinion of following the Imam's statement for a mufti who is not a mujtahid, and carrying the opinion of choice for the mujtahid mufti. And when there is no explicit text from the Imam, the statement of Abu Yusuf is given precedence, then Muhammad etc., and apparently this applies to the non-mujtahid; as for the mujtahid mufti, he chooses what appears stronger to him, similar to the previous case. The ruling when the two companions oppose the Imam: It has been understood from this that there is no disagreement about following the Imam's statement if one of them agrees with him. For this reason, Imam Qadi Khan said: If the issue is disputed among our companions, and Abu Hanifa has one of his two companions with him, he takes their statement—i.e., the statement of the Imam and those who agree with him—due to the abundance of conditions and the gathering of proofs of correctness in it. But if his two companions oppose him in that, then if their disagreement is a disagreement of time and era—like judging by apparent integrity—he takes the statement of his two companions due to the change in people's conditions. In muzara'ah (sharecropping) and mu'amalah (transaction) and similar matters, he chooses their statement due to the consensus of the later scholars on that. In other than that, the mujtahid mufti has a choice, and he acts according to what his opinion leads to. And 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: He takes the statement of Abu Hanifa. I (the commentator) say: But we have already presented that what is narrated from the Imam—his statement: 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab'—is understood to apply as long as it does not exit from the madhhab entirely, as has become clear.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti discusses the methodological rule for a Hanafi mufti when there are multiple narrations from the founding imams. The author begins by citing Al-Hawi al-Qudsi, which lays out the priority order: first take the apparent statement of Abu Hanifa; if none exists, then Abu Yusuf; then Muhammad; then Zufar, al-Hasan, and others in descending order of seniority. When Abu Hanifa's statement is present and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with it, the mufti cannot depart from it unless necessity demands. If they partially agree (one of them agrees), the same principle applies. If they both oppose him, there is a difference of opinion: some scholars say the mufti must still follow Abu Hanifa, while others give him a choice. The most correct view (al-ashah) is that the consideration is for the strength of evidence (qawat al-dalil). The passage then summarizes three scenarios: (1) Imam and Sahibayn agree—no deviation except necessity. (2) Imam alone vs. each of them having separate opinions—Imam's view preferred. (3) Imam vs. both agreeing on one opinion—three internal opinions: follow Imam (Ibn al-Mubarak), free choice, or the distinction between mujtahid and non-mujtahid mufti. The last is adopted by Qadi Khan and considered the soundest. For the non-mujtahid mufti, he must follow the Imam's view; for the mujtahid, he may choose based on evidence. The passage then adds that when no explicit text exists from Abu Hanifa, the non-mujtahid mufti follows Abu Yusuf then Muhammad, while the mujtahid mufti has choice. Finally, it notes that if one of the Sahibayn agrees with the Imam, there is consensus to follow that. Qadi Khan further states that in matters like judging by apparent integrity (due to changing times) or in transactions like muzara'ah, the opinion of the Sahibayn is preferred because later scholars agreed on it. Otherwise, the mujtahid mufti is free to choose. The commentator clarifies that the Imam's famous statement 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is applied as long as it does not completely exit the madhhab.

Key Terms
التخيير (al-takhayyur): The mufti's freedom to choose between two or more valid opinions within the madhhab based on evidence.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A jurist capable of independently weighing evidence to reach a ruling, even within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when Abu Hanifa has no explicit text on an issue, and the mufti is not a mujtahid?
A) He must perform ijtihad independently.
B) He takes the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar, etc.
C) He can choose any opinion from the madhhab.
D) He follows the opinion of the Sahibayn only.

Key Takeaway
When Imam and Sahibayn differ, the mufti's level of ijtihad determines his obligation: non-mujtahid follows Imam, mujtahid chooses based on strength of evidence.

The Three Opinions on Following Imam When Sahibayn Oppose
Rasm al-mufti rule on choosing between Imam and Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three opinions on following Imam when Sahibayn oppose him, and apply the most correct view by distinguishing between a mujtahid and non-mujtahid mufti.

Core Idea
The mufti’s ijtihad level decides whether he follows Imam unconditionally or may choose when Sahibayn disagree.

When Imam Abu Hanifa and his two primary companions differ, the mufti must know how to navigate these conflicting opinions. This passage presents three positions, culminating in a nuanced distinction based on the mufti's own level of ijtihad. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct fatwa practice within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the three opinions on how to rule when Sahibayn oppose Imam: (1) unconditional following of Imam, (2) absolute choice, (3) distinction between mujtahid and non-mujtahid.
The third is deemed the most correct (asahh).
2
Understand the reconciliation
See how the third opinion reconciles the first two by carrying 'following Imam' to the non-mujtahid mufti and 'choice' to the mujtahid mufti.
This is a key tawfiq (reconciliation) in Hanafi usul al-ifta.
3
Classify the mufti
Learn that a non-mujtahid mufti must follow Imam unconditionally; a mujtahid mufti may choose based on his own tarjih.
The passage also notes that if no text from Imam exists, the order is Abu Yusuf then Muhammad for non-mujtahids.
4
Apply the rule
Given a scenario where Sahibayn oppose Imam, determine whether the mufti is mujtahid or not, and then state the ruling.

حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام

غير
فصار فيما إذا خالفه صاحباه ثلاثة أقوال الأول : اتباع قول الإمام بلا تخيير. الثاني: التخيير مطلقا. الثالث: وهو الأصح، التفصيل بين المجتهد ،وغيره و به جزم قاضي خان كما يأتي. والظاهر أن هذا توفيق بين القولين بحمل القول باتباع قول الإمام على المفتي الذي هو مجتهد وحمل القول بالتخيير على المفتي المجتهد. وإذا لم يوجد للإمام نص، يقدم قول أبي يوسف، ثم محمد إلخ، والظاهر أن هذا في حق غير المجتهد، أما المفتي المجتهد فيتخير بما يترجح عنده دلیله نظير ما قبله.
حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام ]
وقد علم من هذا أنه لا خلاف في الأخذ بقول الإمام إذا وافقه أحدهما، ولذا قال الإمام قاضي خان وإن كانت المسألة مختلفا فيها بين أصحابنا، فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه، يأخذ بقولهما، أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه؛ لوفور الشرائط واستجماع أدلة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك، فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر و زمان كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس. وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك. وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتي المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة". قلت : لكن قدمنا أن ما نقل عن الإمام من قوله: "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي"، محمول على ما لم يخرج عن المذهب بالكلية كما ظهر لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه ولهذا قال في "البحر" عن "التتارخانية": إذا كان الإمام في جانب وهما في جانب، خير المفتي. وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما، إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار الفقيه أبو الليث قول زفر في مسائل.
وقال في رسالته المسماة "رفع الغشاء في وقت العصر والعشاء": لا يرجح قول صاحبيه أو أحدهما على قوله إلا لموجب، وهو إما لضعف دليل الإمام، وإما للضرورة ،والتعامل كترجيح قولهما في المزارعة والمعاملة، وإما لأن خلافهما له بسبب اختلاف العصر والزمان، وأنه لو شاهد ما وقع في عصر هما لوافقهما، كعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة. ويوافق ذلك ما قاله العلامة المحقق الشيخ قاسم في "تصحيحه"، ونصه: "على أن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا ،وصححوا، فشهدت مصنفاتهم بترجيح قول أبي حنيفة، والأخذ بقوله ' في مسائل يسيرة اختاروا الفتوى فيها على قولهما، أو قول أحدهما وإن كان الآخر مع الإمام كما اختاروا قول أحدهما فيما لا نص فيه للإمام؛ للمعاني التي أشار إليها القاضي، بل اختاروا قول زفر في مقابلة قول الكل لنحو ذلك. وترجيحاتهم وتصحيحاتهم باقية، فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
Ruling on opposing the Imam by the two companions. So there are three statements when the two companions oppose him: first, following the Imam's statement without choice. Second, absolute choice. Third, and it is the most correct, the distinction between the mujtahid and others, and Qadi Khan decided upon it as will come. And it appears that this is a reconciliation between the two statements by carrying the statement of following the Imam's statement to the mufti who is not a mujtahid and carrying the statement of choice to the mufti who is a mujtahid. And if there is no text from the Imam, the statement of Abu Yusuf is given precedence, then Muhammad etc., and it appears that this is for the non-mujtahid; as for the mujtahid mufti, he chooses based on what is preponderant to him according to his evidence, similar to what preceded.
Ruling on opposing the Imam by the two companions. And it is known from this that there is no disagreement in adopting the Imam's statement if one of them agrees with him. Therefore, Imam Qadi Khan said: And if the issue is disputed among our companions, if Abu Hanifa is supported by one of his two companions, their statement (i.e., the Imam and his supporter) is taken due to the abundance of conditions and the gathering of evidence of correctness. And if his two companions oppose him in that, then if their disagreement is a disagreement of era and time, like ruling based on apparent uprightness, the statement of the two companions is taken due to the change in people's conditions. And in sharecropping (muzara'a) and business dealings (mu'amala) and the like, their statement is chosen due to the consensus of later scholars on that. And beyond that, the mujtahid mufti is given choice and acts according to what his opinion leads him to. And Abdullah ibn Mubarak said: Take the statement of Abu Hanifa. I say: But we have presented that what is transmitted from the Imam, his words: 'If a hadith is authentic, that is my madhhab,' is interpreted as not exiting the madhhab entirely, as became apparent to us from the previous discussion. And its implication is the permissibility of following the evidence even if it opposes what one of his two companions agreed with him. For this reason, it is said in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyya: If the Imam is on one side and they [the Sahibayn] are on the other, the mufti is given choice. And if one of them is with the Imam, their statement is taken, unless the mashayikh have agreed on the other statement, then they are followed, as the faqih Abu al-Layth chose the statement of Zufar in some issues.
And he said in his treatise named 'Raf al-Ghisha' fi Waqt al-Asr wa al-Isha': The statement of his two companions or one of them is not given preference over his statement except for a cause: either due to the weakness of the Imam's evidence, or due to necessity and common practice like preferring their statement in sharecropping and business dealings, or because his disagreement with them is due to a difference of era and time, and that if he had witnessed what occurred in their era he would have agreed with them, like not ruling based on apparent uprightness. And this is supported by what the verifying scholar Shaykh Qasim said in his correction: 'Indeed, the mujtahids were not lost, they examined the disputed matters, gave preponderance, and corrected, so their works bear witness to preferring the statement of Abu Hanifa, and adopting his statement in a few issues in which they chose the fatwa over his two companions or one of them even if the other was with the Imam, as they chose the statement of one of them when there was no text from the Imam, due to the meanings indicated by the Qadi. Rather, they chose the statement of Zufar in opposition to the statement of all for similar reasons. And their tarjihat and corrections remain, so it is upon us to follow the preponderant and act upon it as if they had issued fatwa in their lifetimes.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses a crucial methodological rule in the Hanafi madhhab: how to determine the preferred position when Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion conflicts with that of his two primary companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The author presents three positions: (1) unconditional following of the Imam; (2) absolute choice; (3) the most correct view, which distinguishes between a mujtahid mufti and a non-mujtahid. The non-mujtahid mufti follows the Imam strictly, while the mujtahid mufti may choose based on his own preponderance. Qadi Khan's analysis is cited: if one companion agrees with the Imam, their combined opinion is taken due to the strength of evidence. If both companions disagree, then a further distinction is made: if the disagreement is due to changing times or customs (like the issue of judging by apparent uprightness), the companions' view is preferred. In transactions like muzara'a (sharecropping), later scholars have concurred with the companions. In all other cases, the mujtahid mufti is given discretion. The text also discusses the famous principle attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'If the hadith is authentic, that is my madhhab,' and clarifies that this does not mean abandoning the madhhab entirely but allows following evidence within the madhhab's framework. Finally, references to later scholars like those from al-Bahr and al-Tatarkhaniyya confirm that the mufti has choice when the Imam stands alone, but if one companion joins him, their view is authoritative unless the later mashayikh have favored another view. The passage ends with a quote from Shaykh Qasim affirming that later mujtahids in the madhhab have made tarjihat (preference rulings) that remain binding.

Key Terms
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two primary students and companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A jurist qualified to derive rulings from evidence, here meaning within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab).
مفتي (mufti): A jurist who issues fatwas; the text distinguishes between a mufti who is a mujtahid and one who is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition does a non-mujtahid mufti have choice when Sahibayn oppose Imam?
A) When the disagreement is about sharecropping.
B) When the disagreement is due to change of era.
C) He never has choice; he must follow the Imam.
D) When the Sahibayn agree with each other.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's ijtihad level determines whether he must strictly follow Imam or may choose when Sahibayn disagree; the third opinion (tafsil) is the most correct.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Exceptions: When to Prefer the Sahibayn's View Over the Imam's
Detailed scenarios from Qadi Khan and later scholars on exceptions to following Imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific scenarios where the Sahibayn's opinion is preferred over Imam Abu Hanifa's, and apply the rule of 'change of era' and 'later consensus' to justify the preference.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn's view prevails over Imam's when times change, transactions evolve, or later scholars have agreed.

While the default is to follow Imam, there are recognized exceptions. Qadi Khan and later scholars detail when the Sahibayn's position is actually stronger: when the issue is time-sensitive (like judicial evidence), in commercial matters (like sharecropping), or when later mashayikh have concurred. This lesson unpacks those exceptions and shows how later tarjihat remain authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptions
List the categories given by Qadi Khan where Sahibayn's view is taken: (a) change of era/customs (e.g., qada bi-zahir al-adala), (b) transactions like muzara'a and mu'amala, (c) when later scholars have agreed upon their view.
In all other cases, the mujtahid mufti has choice.
2
Understand the rationale behind each exception
For each exception, explain why the Sahibayn's view is preferred: (a) change of era – the Imam would have agreed if he saw contemporary conditions; (b) transactions – necessity and common practice ('urf); (c) consensus of later scholars – their tarjih binds the mufti.
3
Recognize the role of later scholars (mashayikh)
Even when Sahibayn oppose Imam, if later mashayikh have resolved on a particular view, the mufti must follow that view, as with Abu al-Layth choosing Zufar.
This emphasizes that tarjihat of later mujtahids are authoritative.
4
Apply the exceptions to a modern scenario
Given a new financial contract or a judicial procedure, determine whether it falls under one of the exceptions and which view should be followed.
Consider whether the change in conditions is analogous to the classical exceptions.

Source Text

حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام

غير
فصار فيما إذا خالفه صاحباه ثلاثة أقوال الأول : اتباع قول الإمام بلا تخيير. الثاني: التخيير مطلقا. الثالث: وهو الأصح، التفصيل بين المجتهد ،وغيره و به جزم قاضي خان كما يأتي. والظاهر أن هذا توفيق بين القولين بحمل القول باتباع قول الإمام على المفتي الذي هو مجتهد وحمل القول بالتخيير على المفتي المجتهد. وإذا لم يوجد للإمام نص، يقدم قول أبي يوسف، ثم محمد إلخ، والظاهر أن هذا في حق غير المجتهد، أما المفتي المجتهد فيتخير بما يترجح عنده دلیله نظير ما قبله.
حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام ]
وقد علم من هذا أنه لا خلاف في الأخذ بقول الإمام إذا وافقه أحدهما، ولذا قال الإمام قاضي خان وإن كانت المسألة مختلفا فيها بين أصحابنا، فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه، يأخذ بقولهما، أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه؛ لوفور الشرائط واستجماع أدلة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك، فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر و زمان كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس. وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك. وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتي المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة". قلت : لكن قدمنا أن ما نقل عن الإمام من قوله: "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي"، محمول على ما لم يخرج عن المذهب بالكلية كما ظهر لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه ولهذا قال في "البحر" عن "التتارخانية": إذا كان الإمام في جانب وهما في جانب، خير المفتي. وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما، إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار الفقيه أبو الليث قول زفر في مسائل.

Key Terms
صاحبين (Sahibayn): The two primary students and companions of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
المتأخرون (al-muta’akhkhirun): Later scholars of the Hanafi school, typically from the 6th century Hijri onward.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion over another based on strength of evidence or other factors.

According to Qadi Khan's analysis, when should the mufti take the view of the two companions (Sahibayn) over that of Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) When the disagreement is due to a change in era and customs, such as in 'qada bi-zahir al-adala'.
B) Always, because the two companions are more knowledgeable about contemporary issues.
C) Only when there is an authentic hadith contradicting the Imam's view.
D) Never, because the Imam's opinion is always the strongest.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's view is preferred in cases of changed circumstances, transactions, or when later scholars have concurred; the mufti must recognize these exceptions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Rule for Preferring the Companions' Opinion over the Imam's
Explains when the mufti may prefer Sahibayn over Imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three valid reasons for giving preponderance (tarjeeh) to the opinion of Sahibayn over Abu Hanifa and apply the qawida to new cases.

Core Idea
A mufti may prefer the companions' view only for evidence weakness, custom, or changed times — not whim.

In the Hanafi school, the opinions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions are both authoritative. Yet the mufti is not always bound to follow the Imam. This lesson unpacks the key rule from Rasm al-Mufti that specifies when the companions' view may be preferred, and the qawida that governs this tarjeeh.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The default is that the Imam's opinion is followed; the companions' view is not preferred except for a reason.
The qawida: 'لا يرجح قول صاحبيه أو أحدهما على قوله إلا لموجب'.
2
Identify the three reasons
From 'Raf' al-Ghisha': (a) weakness of the Imam's evidence, (b) necessity or custom (e.g., muzara'ah), (c) change of era (e.g., not judging by apparent justice).
These reasons are exhaustive for tarjeeh over the Imam.
3
Apply to scenarios
Given a case, determine if any reason applies; if so, the companions' view may be preferred.
Example: if a later custom has emerged, that can justify preferring Sahibayn.
4
Note the exception
If one companion sides with the Imam, the mufti takes that combined opinion unless later scholars decided otherwise.
This shows the school values consensus and strong combined proof.

Source Text

لوافقهما، كعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة. ويوافق ذلك ما قاله العلامة المحقق الشيخ قاسم في "تصحيحه"، ونصه: "على أن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا، وصححوا، فشهدت مصنفاتهم بترجيح قول أبي حنيفة، والأخذ بقوله في مسائل يسيرة اختاروا الفتوى فيها على قولهما، أو قول أحدهما وإن كان الآخر مع الإمام كما اختاروا قول أحدهما فيما لا نص فيه للإمام؛ للمعاني التي أشار إليها القاضي، بل اختاروا قول زفر في مقابلة قول الكل لنحو ذلك. وترجيحاتهم وتصحيحاتهم باقية، فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم." تتمة قال العلامة البيري: والمراد بالاجتهاد أحد الاجتهادين، وهو المجتهد في المذهب، وعرف بأنه: المتمكن من تخريج الوجوه على منصوص المفتي في زماننا لا يرجح بل يتبع إمامه، أو المتبحر في مذهب إمامه المتمكن من ترجيح قول له على آخر أطلقه. وسيأتي توضيحه. قال: فالآن لا ترجيح بالدليل فليس إلا القول بالتفصيل ما لم يكن خلافه المصححا فنأخذ الذي لهم قد وَضَحَا فإننا نَرَاهُمُوا قد رجحوا مقال بعض صحبه وصححوا من ذاك ما قد رجحوا لزفر مقاله في سبعة وعشر. المفتي في زماننا لا يرجح بل يتبع] قد علمت أن الأصح تخيير المفتي المجتهد فيفتي بما يكون دليله أقوى، ولا يلزمه المشي على التفصيل. ولما انقطع المفتي المجتهد في زماننا ولم يبق إلا المقلد المحض، وجب علينا اتباع التفصيل، فنفتي أولا بقول الإمام ثم، ثم ما لم نر المجتهدين في المذهب صححوا خلافه؛ لقوة دليله، أو لتغير الزمان، أو نحو ذلك مما يظهر لهم، فنتبع ما قالوا كما لو كانوا أحياء وأفتونا بذلك، كما علمته آنفا من كلام العلامة قاسم؛ لأنهم أعلم وأدرى بالمذهب وعلى هذا عملهم، فإننا رأيناهم قد يرجحون قول صاحبيه تارة، وقول أحدهما تارة، وتارة قول زفر في سبعة عشر موضعا ذكرها البيري في رسالة ولسيدي أحمد الحموي منظومة في ذلك، لكن بعض مسائلها مستدرك؛ لكونه لم يختص به زفر. وقد نظمت في ذلك منظومة فريدة أسقطت منها ما هو مستدرك، وزدت على ما نظمه الحموي عدة مسائل وقد ذكرت هذه المنظومة في حاشيتي "رد المحتار" من باب النفقة.
The ruling on the two companions differing from the Imam is from the previous discussion, and its implication is the permissibility of following the evidence even if it contradicts what one of his two companions agreed with him on. For this reason, it is said in 'al-Bahr' from 'al-Tatarkhaniyya': If the Imam is on one side and they are on the other, the mufti is given choice. If one of them is with the Imam, he takes their opinion, unless the mashayikh have agreed on the other opinion, then he follows them, as al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose Zufar's opinion in some issues. And he said in his treatise named 'Raf' al-Ghisha' fi Waqt al-Asr wa al-Isha': The opinion of his two companions or one of them is not given preponderance over his opinion except for a reason; either weakness of the Imam's evidence, or necessity and customary practice like giving preponderance to their opinion in muzara'ah and mu'amalah, or because their disagreement with him is due to difference of era and time, and that had he witnessed what occurred in their era he would have agreed with them, like not judging by apparent justice. And that is supported by what the verifying scholar al-Shaykh Qasim said in his 'Tashih', whose text is: 'Indeed, the mujtahids were not absent until they examined the differences, weighed, and corrected; thus their works testify to giving preponderance to Abu Hanifa's opinion, and taking his opinion in a few issues in which they chose fatwa over his two companions' opinion or one of them, even if the other was with the Imam, just as they chose the opinion of one of them where there is no text from the Imam; for the meanings indicated by the Qadi. Rather, they chose Zufar's opinion against the opinion of all for similar reasons. And their weighings and corrections remain; so we must follow the preponderant and act upon it as if they had given fatwa in their lifetime.' Supplement: al-Allama al-Biri said: What is meant by ijtihad is one of two ijtihads, and it is the mujtahid fi al-madhhab, defined as: one who can derive aspects based on the texts of the mufti in our time, he does not weigh but follows his imam, or one who is deeply rooted in his imam's madhhab, capable of weighing one opinion over another that he has transmitted. And its clarification will come. He said: So now there is no weighing by evidence; there is only the detailed opinion unless its opposite has been corrected; so we take what they have made clear. For we see that they have given preponderance to the saying of some of his companions and corrected from that which they gave preponderance to Zufar's saying in twenty-seven. [Commentary: 'The mufti in our time does not weigh but follows'] You have known that the most authentic is that the mujtahid mufti has choice, he gives fatwa according to what his evidence is stronger, and he is not obliged to follow the detail. And when the mujtahid mufti ceased in our time and only the pure muqallid remains, we are obliged to follow the detail: first we give fatwa according to the Imam's opinion, then, then, as long as we do not see that the mujtahids in the madhhab have corrected its opposite; due to strength of its evidence, or change of time, or similar that appears to them; so we follow what they said, as if they were alive and gave us fatwa accordingly, as you learned earlier from the words of al-Allama Qasim; because they are more knowledgeable and more aware of the madhhab, and on this is their practice. For we see them sometimes giving preponderance to the opinion of his two companions, sometimes to the opinion of one of them, and sometimes to Zufar's opinion in seventeen places mentioned by al-Biri in a treatise, and Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi has a poem on that, but some of its issues are corrected because they were not specific to Zufar. And I composed a unique poem, omitting what is corrected, and added to what al-Hamawi composed several issues, and I have mentioned this poem in my gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar' from the chapter of Nafaqah.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule that establishes the hierarchy of opinions in the Hanafi school and the duty of the mufti in weighing them. The text begins by restating the principle from earlier discussions: when the Imam (Abu Hanifa) takes one position and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) take another, the mufti is not bound to follow the majority; rather, he may choose whichever has stronger evidence. However, if one of the companions sides with the Imam, the mufti should follow the opinion of the two (i.e., the Imam and that companion) unless later scholars have agreed on a different position, as when al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose Zufar's opinion in some issues. The passage then quotes a treatise titled 'Raf' al-Ghisha' which specifies three reasons for giving preponderance to the companions' opinion over the Imam's: (1) weakness of the Imam's evidence, (2) necessity or customary practice (like in muzara'ah and mu'amalah where the companions' view is preferred due to custom), and (3) change of era, implying that if the Imam had witnessed later circumstances he would have agreed with them. This is supported by the statement of al-Shaykh Qasim that later mujtahids have indeed weighed and corrected, and their tarjeeh remains authoritative. The text then introduces a supplement defining ijtihad: the requisite ijtihad is 'ijtihad fi al-madhhab', i.e., the ability to derive rulings from the Imam's principles or to weigh between transmitted opinions. The author then states that in the present time (the author's era), the mufti is no longer a mujtahid but a muqallid, so he must follow the detailed order: first the Imam's opinion, then the companions', then others' unless the senior mujtahids have corrected another position due to stronger evidence, changed custom, etc. The passage concludes with the author's observation that later scholars have weighed in favor of various opinions, including seventeen places where Zufar's opinion is preferred, and he composed a poem listing them, which he mentions in his gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar'.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjeeh): The process of weighing one opinion over another based on strength of evidence or other factors (necessity, custom, time change).
مفتي (mufti): A jurist who issues fatwas; in context, distinguishes between the absolute mujtahid mufti and the muqallid mufti who follows the madhhab's preponderant opinion.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): One who can derive rulings from the Imam's principles and weigh between transmitted opinions, but does not found a new madhhab.
صاحبان (sahibain): The two principal companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the text say is the default rule regarding preferring the companions' opinion over the Imam's?
A) It is always allowed
B) It is never allowed
C) It is allowed only for a valid reason
D) It is allowed only if the majority of scholars agree

Key Takeaway
The mufti may prefer the companions' view only for weakness of evidence, custom, or changed times; otherwise the Imam's view prevails.

The Mufti's Duty After the Closure of Ijtihad: Following Later Tarjeeh
Explains the duty of the mufti after ijtihad ceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the contemporary mufti must follow the tarjeeh of later mujtahids and state the hierarchy of opinions within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When ijtihad ceased, the mufti became a muqallid bound by the tarjeeh of earlier scholars.

The earlier lesson discussed when a mujtahid mufti may exercise choice. But what happens when ijtihad ceases and only muqallids remain? This lesson examines the shift in responsibility: the mufti no longer weighs independently but must follow the detailed hierarchy established by later mujtahids like al-Marghinani, al-Haskafi, and Ibn Abidin.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish types of mufti
Recognize the difference between a mujtahid mufti (who can weigh) and a muqallid mufti (who must follow).
The text says: 'فالآن لا ترجيح بالدليل فليس إلا القول بالتفصيل'.
2
Identify the historical shift
The text states that since mujtahid muftis have ceased, the muqallid mufti must follow the detailed order.
Reference: 'ولما انقطع المفتي المجتهد في زماننا ولم يبق إلا المقلد المحض'.
3
State the hierarchy
First follow Imam Abu Hanifa, then his companions, then Zufar, unless later scholars have corrected otherwise.
The text gives examples of tarjeeh in favor of Sahibayn or Zufar in specific issues.
4
Recognize authoritative tarjeeh
The tarjeeh of later mujtahids (e.g., al-Shaykh Qasim) is binding, as if they gave fatwa in their lifetimes.
"فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم."

حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه ولهذا قال في "البحر" عن "التتارخانية": إذا كان الإمام في جانب وهما في جانب، خير المفتي. وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما، إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار الفقيه أبو الليث قول زفر في مسائل. وقال في رسالته المسماة "رفع الغشاء في وقت العصر والعشاء": لا يرجح قول صاحبيه أو أحدهما على قوله إلا لموجب، وهو إما لضعف دليل الإمام، وإما للضرورة، والتعامل كترجيح قولهما في المزارعة والمعاملة، وإما لأن خلافهما له بسبب اختلاف العصر والزمان، وأنه لو شاهد ما وقع في عصر هما لوافقهما، كعدم القضاء بظاهر العدالة. ويوافق ذلك ما قاله العلامة المحقق الشيخ قاسم في "تصحيحه"، ونصه: "على أن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا، وصححوا، فشهدت مصنفاتهم بترجيح قول أبي حنيفة، والأخذ بقوله في مسائل يسيرة اختاروا الفتوى فيها على قولهما، أو قول أحدهما وإن كان الآخر مع الإمام كما اختاروا قول أحدهما فيما لا نص فيه للإمام؛ للمعاني التي أشار إليها القاضي، بل اختاروا قول زفر في مقابلة قول الكل لنحو ذلك. وترجيحاتهم وتصحيحاتهم باقية، فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم." تتمة قال العلامة البيري: والمراد بالاجتهاد أحد الاجتهادين، وهو المجتهد في المذهب، Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Mufti in Later Times: Follow the Detailed Order
Rule that mufti must follow imam, then sahibayn, then Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the detailed order (al-tafsil) in issuing fatwa and identify the hierarchy of authority: Imam Abu Hanifa, then his two disciples, then Zufar, where later mujtahids have corrected.

Core Idea
A later mufti cannot do tarjih; he must follow the school's established hierarchy.

In the early Hanafi school, mujtahid muftis could weigh evidence directly. But once that era ended, the mufti became a muqallid, bound by the detailed order (al-tafsil) of the school. This lesson explains that order: first the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, then what the school's later mujtahids have corrected, even if that means adopting the opinion of Imam's disciples or Zufar. The mufti's role is to transmit the school's preferred rulings, not to re-ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shift from mujtahid to muqallid
Understand that in earlier times, a mufti could be a mujtahid and choose the strongest evidence. Now, only muqallids remain, so personal tarjih is forbidden.
2
Recall the hierarchy of preference
When issuing fatwa, the mufti must first seek Imam Abu Hanifa's saying. If the school's mujtahids have corrected a different opinion (from Sahibayn or Zufar), he follows that correction.
The correction must be explicit and acknowledged by the school's authorities.
3
Recognize the role of the school's later authorities
Later mujtahids (mujtahids fi al-madhhab) like Ibn Abidin have compiled lists of where Sahibayn or Zufar are preferred. The mufti must rely on those compilations.
Examples include al-Bayri's treatise and al-Hamawi's poem, later refined by Ibn Abidin.
4
Apply the rule: no independent tarjih
In any given case, the mufti should not prefer one opinion over another based on his own reasoning. He must follow the hierarchy unless the school has explicitly corrected it.
This preserves consistency and prevents arbitrary fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتي
٤٢
المفتي في زماننا لا يرجح بل يتبع إمامه، أو المتبحر في مذهب إمامه المتمكن من ترجيح قول له على آخر أطلقه. وسيأتي توضيحه.
فالآن لا ترجيح بالدليل فليس إلا القول بالتفصيل ما لم يكن خلافه المصححا فنأخذ الذي لهم قد وَضَحَا فإننا نَرَاهُمُوا قد رجحوا مقال بعض صحبه وصححوا من ذاك ما قد رجحوا لزفر مقاله في سبعة وعشر
المفتي في زماننا لا يرجّح بل يتبع]
قد علمت أن الأصح تخيير المفتي المجتهد فيفتي بما يكون دليله أقوى، ولا يلزمه المشي على التفصيل. ولما انقطع المفتي المجتهد في زماننا ولم يبق إلا المقلد المحض، وجب علينا اتباع التفصيل، فنفتي أولا بقول الإمام ثم ،وثم ما لم نر المجتهدين في المذهب صححوا خلافه؛ لقوة دليله، أو لتغير الزمان، أو نحو ذلك مما يظهر لهم، فنتبع ما قالوا كما لو كانوا أحياء وأفتونا بذلك، كما علمته آنفا من كلام العلامة قاسم؛ لأنهم أعلم وأدرى بالمذهب وعلى هذا عملهم، فإننا رأيناهم قد يرجحون قول صاحبيه تارة، وقول أحدهما ،تارة وتارة قول زفر في سبعة عشر موضعا ذكرها البيري في رسالة ولسيدي أحمد الحموي منظومة في ذلك، لكن بعض مسائلها مستدرك؛ لكونه لم يختص به زفر. وقد نظمت في ذلك منظومة فريدة أسقطت منها ما هو مستدرك، وزدت على ما نظمه الحموي عدة مسائل وقد ذكرت هذه المنظومة في حاشيتي "رد المحتار" من باب النفقة.
Commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. 42. The mufti in our time does not give preference (tarjih) but rather follows his imam, or the one who is deeply versed in the school of his imam, capable of preferring one saying over another. Its clarification will come. Now there is no preference by evidence; there is only the detailed order (al-tafsil) as long as there is no contrary that has been corrected (musahhah). So we take what they (the mashayikh) have made clear, for we see that they have preferred the saying of some of his companions and corrected from that what they preferred for Zufar in seventeen places. The mufti in our time does not give preference but follows. You have known that the correct view is that the mujtahid mufti has a choice, so he gives fatwa based on the stronger evidence, and he is not bound to follow the tafsil. But when the mujtahid mufti ceased to exist in our time and nothing remains except the pure muqallid, we are obliged to follow the tafsil. So we first give fatwa by the saying of the Imam, then by what the mujtahids of the school have corrected contrary to it, due to the strength of its evidence, or change of time, or similar reasons that appear to them. So we follow what they said, as if they were alive and gave us that fatwa, as you learned earlier from the words of Allama Qasim, because they are more knowledgeable and aware of the school. This is their practice. Indeed, we see that they sometimes prefer the saying of his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), sometimes of one of them, and sometimes of Zufar in seventeen places, which al-Bayri mentioned in a treatise. And there is a poem by Sayyidi Ahmad al-Hamawi on that, but some of its issues are corrected because they are not exclusive to Zufar. I have composed a unique poem in which I omitted what is corrected and added several issues beyond what al-Hamawi composed. I have mentioned this poem in my commentary 'Radd al-Muhtar' under the chapter of Nafaqa.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule. It begins with a verse stating that the mufti in later times does not perform independent tarjih but follows the detailed order. The commentary explains that formerly a mujtahid mufti could choose the strongest evidence, but since that era ended, the mufti must be a pure muqallid and follow the order: first the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, then what the mujtahids of the school have corrected (musahhah). The mashayikh might prefer the Sahibayn or Zufar in certain cases, but these are exceptions recorded by scholars like al-Bayri. The author notes his own poem on the topic, refining earlier works. The key principle: later muftis cannot overstep the hierarchy, but they follow the consensus of the school's authorities.

Key Terms
المفتي (al-mufti): The scholar qualified to issue legal verdicts (fatwa). In this passage, a muqallid mufti of later times who cannot perform independent ijtihad.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preferring one legal opinion over another based on stronger evidence.
التفصيل (al-tafsil): The detailed order of preference in issuing fatwa: Imam, then Sahibayn, then others.
الإمام (al-imam): Imam Abu Hanifa (d. 150 AH), the founder of the Hanafi school.
صاحبيه (sahibayh): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do when the school's mujtahids have corrected a ruling contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Follow the Imam's ruling because he is the founder.
B) Follow the corrected ruling because the mujtahids are more knowledgeable about the school.
C) Perform istihsan to choose the better ruling.
D) Refer the question to a higher authority.

Key Takeaway
A later mufti must follow the detailed order (Imam first, then corrected opinions) and cannot perform independent tarjih.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
Fatwa by Saying of Other than Imam
Ruling: later mufti must follow Imam's saying, not mashayikh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy rule that a later mufti must give fatwa by the Imam's saying unless he is qualified to evaluate evidence.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa; only expert scholars may deviate after evaluating evidence.

This passage addresses a crucial question: how could early Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) give fatwa contradicting Abu Hanifa? The answer lies in a condition—knowledge of evidence—which later ceased to apply. Understanding this clarifies the mufti's duty today, especially for those who are not capable of independent evidence evaluation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the condition
The author raises the puzzle: early Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) issued fatwas contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa while being muqallids. The solution is a transmitted condition: a mufti must know the evidence behind the ruling (dalil) before giving fatwa by the school.
This condition is recorded in al-Sirajiyyah: the scholar 'Isam deviated because he did not know the Imam's evidence.
2
Distinguish early vs later eras
The condition applied in early times when scholars had access to evidence and could evaluate it. In later times, memorization (hifz) of the school's rulings suffices; the condition is dropped. Thus, a later mufti must give fatwa by the Imam's saying without needing to know his evidence.
This shift is supported by texts like al-Qunyah, which state that in our time, mere memorization suffices.
3
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's exception
Ibn al-Humam, a leading later scholar (muhaqqiq), argued that one may deviate from the Imam's saying if the evidence for his view is weak. However, this requires expertise in evidence evaluation. For non-experts, the default remains the Imam's saying.
Ibn al-Humam himself was qualified, but his approach does not apply to ordinary muqallid muftis.
4
Apply the rule to a modern mufti
A contemporary Hanafi mufti who is not a mujtahid must give fatwa according to Imam Abu Hanifa's relied-upon position, even if some mashayikh gave a different ruling. He cannot choose based on his own preference.
The mufta bihi is that memorization of the school's rulings is sufficient for issuing fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام
وقال في "البحر" من كتاب القضاء فإن قلت: كيف جاز للمشايخ الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام الأعظم مع أنهم مقلدون؟ قلت: قد أشكل علي ذلك مدة طويلة، ولم أرَ فيه جوابا إلا ما فهمته الآن من كلامهم، وهو أنهم نقلوا عن أصحابنا: "أنه لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا" حتى نقل في "السراجية": إن هذا سبب مخالفة عصام للإمام، وكان يفتي بخلاف قوله كثيرا؛ لأنه لم يعلم الدليل، وكان يظهر له دليل غيره فيفتي به.
فأقول: إن هذا الشرط كان في زمانهم أما في زماننا فيكتفى بالحفظ كما في "القنية" وغيرها، فيحل الإفتاء بقول الإمام، بل يجب، وإن لم نعلم من أين قال؟ وعلى هذا فما صححه في "الحاوي" - أي من أن الاعتبار لقوة الدليل- مبني على ذلك الشرط، وقد صححوا أن الإفتاء بقول الإمام فينتج من هذا أنه يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؛ لأنهم إنما أفتوا بخلافه لفقد الشرط في حقهم، وهو الوقوف على دليله وأما نحن فلنا الإفتاء وإن لم نقف على دليله. وقد وقع للمحقق ابن الهمام في مواضع الرد على المشايخ في الإفتاء بقولهما، بأنه لا يُعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله، لكن هو أهل للنظر في الدليل، ومن ليس بأهل للنظر فيه، فعليه الإفتاء بقول الإمام.
Giving fatwa by the saying of other than the Imam. He said in 'al-Bahr' from the book of judiciary: If you say: How was it permissible for the mashayikh to give fatwa by the saying of other than the Great Imam while they were muqallids? I say: This was difficult for me for a long time, and I did not see an answer except what I now understood from their words: that they transmitted from our companions: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our school until he knows from where we said it,' as it is narrated in 'al-Sirajiyya' that this was the cause of 'Isam's opposition to the Imam; he used to give fatwa contrary to his saying often, because he did not know the evidence, and the evidence of others appeared to him, so he gave fatwa by it. So I say: This condition applied in their time. As for our time, memorization (al-hifz) suffices, as in 'al-Qunyah' and others, so it is permissible to give fatwa by the saying of the Imam, rather it is obligatory, even if we do not know from where he said it. Based on this, what has been corrected in 'al-Hawi' - that consideration is based on strength of evidence - is built on that condition. And they have corrected that the fatwa is by the saying of the Imam. It follows from this that we must give fatwa by the saying of the Imam even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, because they only gave fatwa contrary due to the loss of the condition in their right, which is knowledge of his evidence. As for us, we may give fatwa even if we do not know his evidence. And it occurred to the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in several places to reject the mashayikh in giving fatwa by the saying of the two (Sahibayn), stating that one should not deviate from his (the Imam's) saying except due to weakness of its evidence. But he (Ibn al-Humam) is qualified to consider evidence. As for one who is not qualified to consider evidence, upon him is to give fatwa by the saying of the Imam.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule addressing a specific problem: how could early Hanafi mashayikh give fatwa contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa while being muqallids? The answer lies in a condition transmitted from the companions of Abu Hanifa: a mufti must know the evidence behind the ruling. The mashayikh knew the evidence, so they could sometimes prefer other opinions. However, in later times, this condition is dropped; mere memorization of the ruling suffices. Therefore, the later mufti must follow the Imam's saying. The text critiques Ibn al-Humam's approach, noting that only those qualified to weigh evidence can deviate from the Imam.

Key Terms
الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام (al-ifta' bi qawl ghayr al-imam): Issuing a legal verdict based on an opinion other than that of Imam Abu Hanifa, such as those of his disciples.
المشايخ (al-mashayikh): The early Hanafi scholars who were muqallids of Abu Hanifa but sometimes gave fatwa contrary to his opinion.
الشرط (al-shart): The condition of knowing the evidence (dalil) behind the Imam's ruling, required for earlier scholars to give fatwa by the school.
الحفظ (al-hifz): Memorization of the school's rulings as transmitted, sufficient for a later mufti to issue fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a later mufti who does not know the evidence behind Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling?
A) He must still give fatwa by the Imam's saying, and it is obligatory.
B) He may choose the saying of the disciples if he finds it stronger.
C) He must refrain from giving fatwa until he learns the evidence.
D) He must follow the majority of the mashayikh.

Key Takeaway
A later Hanafi mufti must give fatwa by Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling; only a fully qualified scholar may deviate after evaluating evidence.

Following Imam Abu Hanifa in Fatwa: The Muqallid's Obligation
Discussing the permissibility of giving fatwa according to other imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule that obligates a muqallid mufti to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's statement and identify when deviation is permissible.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa even without knowing his evidence — deviation requires ijtihad capacity.

This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti tackles a critical question: can a later Hanafi mufti give fatwa according to an imam other than Abu Hanifa? The author resolves the apparent conflict between early mashayikh's practice and later obligation by distinguishing between those who knew the evidence and those who merely memorize. The lesson establishes a clear hierarchy: the mufti who cannot independently evaluate evidence must adhere strictly to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
Determine the central issue: why did some early mashayikh give fatwa contrary to Imam Abu Hanifa despite being muqallids?
The question arises from a statement in al-Bahr.
2
Distinguish the two conditions
Understand that early scholars required knowing the evidence (dalil) before giving fatwa; later scholars suffice with mere memorization of the ruling.
The condition changed over time, as noted in al-Qunyah.
3
Apply the rule for later muftis
For a muqallid today, it is obligatory to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, even if the evidence is unknown.
The text says 'فيحل الإفتاء بقول الإمام، بل يجب'.
4
Recognize the exception
Only a mujtahid who can weigh evidence may follow a stronger proof from another imam.
Ibn al-Humam is cited as an example of one qualified to do so.
5
Understand the practical implication
The mufti must adhere to Imam Abu Hanifa unless he has the capacity for ijtihad; otherwise, his fatwa is invalid.
This prevents arbitrary selection of opinions (tatabbu' al-rukhas).

He said in al-Bahr from the chapter of Qada: If you say: How did the mashayikh permit giving fatwa according to other than the Great Imam while they are muqallids? I say: This perplexed me for a long time, and I saw no answer except what I now understand from their words: they narrated from our companions: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it,' as narrated in al-Sirajiyya: This is the reason for 'Isam's opposition to the Imam; he used to give fatwa contrary to his statement often because he did not know the evidence, and another evidence would appear to him so he would give fatwa accordingly. Based on this, what was corrected in al-Hawi—that consideration is for the strength of the evidence—is built on that condition. They have corrected that giving fatwa according to the Imam's statement leads to the conclusion that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, because they only gave fatwa contrary to it due to the absence of the condition in their case, which is knowing his evidence; while we can give fatwa even if we do not know his evidence. And it occurred from the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in places refuting the mashayikh regarding giving fatwa according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that one does not deviate from his statement except due to weakness of his evidence, but he is qualified to examine the evidence, and whoever is not qualified to examine it must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement.

Commentary
This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses the rasm rule concerning giving fatwa by statements other than Imam Abu Hanifa. The author begins by citing a question from al-Bahr: How did early mashayikh permit giving fatwa according to other imams when they were muqallids? The answer is that they required knowing the evidence (dalil) for the Imam's ruling. However, in later times, mere memorization of the ruling suffices, and it becomes obligatory to follow Imam Abu Hanifa even without knowing the evidence. The passage concludes that one who is not qualified to weigh evidence must adhere to Imam Abu Hanifa's position. This establishes the hierarchy: the mufti who is not a mujtahid must follow the Imam; deviation is only for those capable of ijtihad.

Key Terms
الإفتاء بقول غير الإمام (al-ifta' bi qawl ghayr al-imam): Giving a legal ruling based on the opinion of an imam other than Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's statement even without knowing his evidence; only a mujtahid may deviate based on evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
