Qualification for Ifta and the Rule of Knowing the Evidence
Defines mufti qualification and explains the ruling on knowing evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the qualification (ahliyyah) for a mufti according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between the role of a mujtahid mufti and a muqallid mufti in relation to knowing the evidence.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid mufti does not need to know the evidence; he reports the tarjih of the mashayikh.

This lesson addresses a foundational question in Hanafi ifta: what qualifies a person to issue fatwa? The source passage defines the attributes of a mufti, introduces the crucial principle that Shariah follows the prevalent (al-ghalib), and then tackles a key tension: Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that no one may give fatwa by his statement without knowing the evidence. Through careful analysis, the passage shows that this requirement applies to the mujtahid mufti, while a muqallid mufti acts as a reporter (haki) of the preponderant position established by the later mashayikh.

Guided Path
1
Define ahliyyah for fatwa
Identify the specific qualifications mentioned: being knowledgeable, able to distinguish between sayings, and capable of tarjih. Note that the mufti's correct opinions must outnumber his errors.
This condition is derived from the qawida: Shariah matters are based on the more common and prevalent.
2
Understand the qawida of al-ghalib
Examine the maxim 'إن أمور الشرع مبنية على الأعم الأغلب' and see how it grounds the qualification condition: correctness must prevail because the Shariah follows the prevalent.
This is a wusta (intermediate) maxim used in many fiqh chapters.
3
Analyze the apparent contradiction
The passage presents an objection: Imam Abu Hanifa's statement seems to forbid fatwa without knowing evidence, yet later scholars oblige following the Imam's statement even without knowing his evidence. Identify why this appears contradictory.
The objection is raised by al-Khayr al-Ramli.
4
Resolve using the concept of hikayah
The resolution: a non-mujtahid does not actually 'give fatwa' but reports (hikayah) what the mujtahid said. The Imam's prohibition applies only to the mujtahid mufti, not to the reporter. The mashayikh are the ones who have already done the tarjih.
This key distinction preserves the integrity of both positions.
5
Apply the ruling to the mufti's role
Conclude that a later mufti must follow the preponderant views as identified by the mashayikh, and may not deviate unless the mashayikh themselves indicated a different position. This is the operative rule for fatwa today.
Reference is made to Ibn al-Shalabi's fatwa: a judge cannot rule against Abu Hanifa unless the mashayikh have already given preponderance to another view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهلية النظر والفتوى
والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفا مميزا بين الأقاويل، له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض، ولا يصير أهلا للفتوى ما لم يصر صوابه أكثر من خطأه؛ لأن الصواب متى كثر فقد غلب، ولا عبرة في المغلوب بمقابلة الغالب؛ فإن أمور الشرع مبنية على الأعم الأغلب، كذا في "الولوالجية" وفي مناقب الكردري قال ابن المبارك وقد سئل: "متى يحل للرجل أن يفتي ويلي القضاء؟ قال: إذا كان بصيرا بالحديث والرأي عارفا بقول أبي حنيفة حافظا له وهذا محمول على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا، وقبل استقرار المذهب، أما بعد التقرر، فلا حاجة إليه؛ لأنه يمكنه التقليد".
11
أقول: ولا يخفى عليك ما في هذا الكلام من عدم الانتظام، ولهذا اعترضه محشيه الخير الرملي بأن قوله: "يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام، وإن لم نعلم من أين "قال مضاد لقول الإمام لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؛ إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به على وجوبه؟ فنقول: ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا، وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكي فتواهم لا غير، فليتأمل.
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
وتوضيحه أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون: "الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف مثلا. وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم
أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره باجتهادهم. وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا إلى أن قال: فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
وفي فتاوى العلامة ابن الشلبي: ليس للقاضي ولا للمفتي العدول عن قول الإمام إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره. فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره، ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض.
ا لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا] ثم اعلم أن قول الإمام: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا إلخ يحتمل معنيين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به ما هو المتبادر منه وهو أنه إذا ثبت عنده مذهب إمامه في حكم كوجوب الوتر مثلا، لا يحل له أن يفتي بذلك حتى يعلم دليل إمامه ولا شك أنه على هذا خاص بالمفتي المجتهد دون
Qualification for consideration and fatwa. And what is meant by qualification here is that he be knowledgeable, distinguishing between sayings, having the ability to give preponderance to some over others. And he does not become qualified for fatwa until his correct becomes more than his error; because when correctness increases, it prevails, and no consideration is given to the infrequent in comparison to the frequent; for the matters of the Shariah are based on the more common and prevalent, as in al-Wilwalijiyya. And in Manaqib al-Kardari, Ibn al-Mubarak said, when asked: 'When is it permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship?' He said: 'When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's statement, and memorizes it.' And this is carried on one of the two narrations from our companions, and before the establishment of the school, but after establishment, there is no need for it because he can do taqlid. I say: It is not hidden from you what in this speech is of lack of organization. Hence, his commenter al-Khayr al-Ramli objected to it, that his statement: 'It is obligatory upon us to give fatwa by the Imam's statement, even if we do not know from where he said' is contradictory to the Imam's statement: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said'; for it is explicit in the impermissibility of fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad. So how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? So we say: What issues from other than the qualified is not really fatwa; rather, it is a report from the mujtahid that he said such and such. By this consideration, reporting the statement of other than the Imam is permissible. So how can it be obligatory upon us to give fatwa by the Imam's statement, even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it? And we only report their fatwa, nothing else. So let it be contemplated. It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. And its clarification is that the mashayikh had access to the Imam's evidence, and knew from where he said, and had access to the evidence of his companions, so they give preponderance to the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and they give fatwa accordingly. And it should not be thought that they turned away from his statement out of ignorance of his evidence; for we see them have filled their books with the presentation of evidences, then they say: 'The fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf, for example.' And since we ourselves are not qualified to examine the evidence, and have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of derivation and foundation, we must report what they say, for they are the followers of the school who set themselves to establish and refine it by their ijtihad. And look at what we presented from the statement of Allama Qasim: 'The mujtahids are not absent; they looked at the divergent, and gave preponderance and corrected until he said: So upon us is to follow the preponderant and act by it, just as if they gave fatwa in their lifetime.' And in the Fatawa of Allama Ibn al-Shalabi: It is not for the judge or the mufti to deviate from the Imam's statement unless one of the mashayikh explicitly says that the fatwa is on another's statement. So the judge may not judge by a statement other than Abu Hanifa's in a matter where another's statement has not been given preponderance, and they have given preponderance to Abu Hanifa's evidence over his own evidence. If he judges in it, his judgment is not valid; he has nothing but to overturn it. 'So it is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said' – then know that the Imam's statement 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our statement etc.' may have two meanings: One of them is that what is meant is what is apparent from it: that when the madhhab of his imam is established for him regarding a ruling, like the obligation of witr for example, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa on that until he knows the evidence of his imam. Without doubt, this is specific to the mujtahid mufti, not to...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti discusses two interconnected topics: first, the qualification (ahliyyah) required for a mufti, and second, the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the necessity of knowing the evidence before issuing fatwa. The author begins by defining the qualification as the ability to distinguish between different scholarly positions and to weigh them against each other. A crucial condition is that the mufti's correct opinions must outnumber his errors, because Shariah rulings are based on the more prevalent and frequent cases. This is supported by a quotation from Ibn al-Mubarak, who states that a mufti must be well-versed in hadith and opinion (ra'y) and must know and memorize the statements of Abu Hanifa. However, the commentator notes that this condition applied only before the school's positions were fully established; after that, a mufti may simply follow the school (taqlid). The author then raises an objection by al-Khayr al-Ramli: there is an apparent contradiction between the ruling that we must give fatwa according to the Imam even without knowing his evidence, and the Imam's own statement that no one may give fatwa by his statement without knowing the evidence. The author resolves this by explaining that what a non-mujtahid does is not technically 'fatwa' but rather a report (hikayah) of what the mujtahid said. The subsequent section clarifies that the mashayikh (later scholars) did have access to the evidences and sometimes gave preponderance to the companions' views over those of Abu Hanifa Himself. Since later muftis are not qualified for ijtihad, they must simply report the preponderant positions determined by those mashayikh. The passage concludes with the statement that Imam Abu Hanifa's saying has two possible interpretations: one applies to a mujtahid mufti who must know the evidence, while the other (cut off here) presumably applies to a non-mujtahid.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Qualification or competency to perform a specific legal function, here issuing fatwa.
إفتاء (ifta'): The act of issuing a legal opinion (fatwa).
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preponderance to one evidence or opinion over another based on strength of proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the condition that a mufti's correct opinions must outnumber his errors?
A) It is derived from the consensus of the Companions.
B) It is based on the maxim that Shariah matters are built on the more common and prevalent (al-ghalib).
C) It is a condition stated in the Qur'an.
D) It is a requirement only for judges, not muftis.

Key Takeaway
The qualification for a mufti includes the ability to distinguish and weigh opinions, with correct outnumbering errors, but the later non-mujtahid mufti acts as a reporter of the mashayikh's tarjih, not as an independent evidence-verifier.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Mufti's Obligation to Know Evidence: Taqlid vs Ijtihad
Commentary on a rasm al-mufti rule about evidence knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two interpretations of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement on fatwa and evidence, and identify which interpretation applies to a muqallid mufti.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti need not know the evidence; only a mujtahid mufti is required to do so.

Imam Abu Hanifa said: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa with our saying until he knows [the evidence].' But who is 'anyone'? Does this include a mere transmitter of the madhhab? The classical Hanafi scholars debated this, arriving at a nuanced distinction between the mujtahid mufti and the muqallid mufti. In this lesson, we will parse the key terms and settle the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The ruling is a rasm al-mufti principle: a mufti must know the evidence behind the madhhab position before issuing fatwa. Determine what exactly is being required: knowledge of evidence or mere transmission.
The passage opens with the rule and then offers clarification from the mashayikh.
2
Define taqlid, mujtahid, and muqallid
Parse the key terms as they appear in the passage. Taqlid is accepting another's statement without knowing the evidence. A mujtahid derives rulings from evidence; a muqallid follows without such knowledge.
This step is crucial to understanding who is addressed by the Imam's statement.
3
Analyze the two interpretations of the Imam's statement
The passage presents two possible meanings: 1) It applies generally to all muftis, even muqallids. 2) It applies only to mujtahid muftis, excluding muqallids because taqlid by definition lacks evidence knowledge.
The first is the apparent meaning; the second is the preferred interpretation.
4
Apply the preferred interpretation to a scenario
Consider a mufti who is a mujtahid in the madhhab (but not absolute). According to the passage, he is not required to know the evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa because he is not an absolute mujtahid; he must simply follow the preferred rulings of the earlier mashayikh.
This shows the practical consequence: the mufti's rank determines his obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم.
وتوضيحه أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون: "الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف مثلا. وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره باجتهادهم. وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم: "إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا إلى أن قال: فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم".
وفي فتاوى العلامة ابن الشلبي: ليس للقاضي ولا للمفتي العدول عن قول الإمام إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره. فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره، ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض.
ثم اعلم أن قول الإمام: "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا إلخ يحتمل معنيين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به ما هو المتبادر منه وهو أنه إذا ثبت عنده مذهب إمامه في حكم كوجوب الوتر مثلا، لا يحل له أن يفتي بذلك حتى يعلم دليل إمامه ولا شك أنه على هذا خاص بالمفتي المجتهد دون المقلد المحض؛ فإن التقليد: "هو الأخذ بقول الغير بغير معرفة دليله".
أخذه قالوا: فخرج مع معرفة دليله فإنه ليس بتقليد؛ لأنه أخذ من الدليل لا من المجتهد بل قيل: إن أخذه مع معرفة دليله نتيجة الاجتهاد؛ لأن معرفة الدليل إنما تكون للمجتهد؛ لتوقفها على معرفة المعارض، وهي متوقفة على استقراء الأدلة كلها، ولا يقدر على ذلك إلا المجتهد أما مجرد معرفة أن المجتهد الفلاني أخذ الحكم الفلاني من الدليل الفلاني فلا فائدة فيها فلا بد أن يكون المراد من وجوب معرفة الدليل على المفتي أن يعرف حاله، حتى يصح له تقليده في ذلك مع الجزم به وإفتاء غيره به وهذا لا يتأتى إلا في المفتي المجتهد في المذهب، وهو المفتي حقيقة، أما غيره فهو ناقل.
لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد؛ لأن هذا المفتي حيث لم يكن وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق يلزمه التقليد لمن وصل إليها، ولا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه إلا على قول. قال في "التحرير":
مسألة: غير المجتهد المطلق يلزمه التقليد، وإن كان مجتهدا في بعض مسائل الفقه، أو بعض العلوم كالفرائض، على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق، فيقلد غيره فيما لا يقدر عليه وقيل في العالم: إنما يلزمه التقليد بشرط تبين صحة مستند المجتهد، وإلا لم يجز له تقليده. والأول قول الجمهور، والثاني قول لبعض المعتزلة، كما ذكره شارحه، فقوله: يلزمه التقليد" مع ما قدمناه من تعريف التقليد، يدل على أن معرفة الدليل للمجتهد المطلق فقط، وأنه لا يلزم غيره ولو كان ذلك الغير مجتهدا في المذهب.
It is not permissible to give fatwa with our saying until he knows the evidence. And its clarification is that the mashayikh examined the evidence of the Imam, and they knew from where he said, and they examined the evidence of his companions, so they prefer the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and they give fatwa with it, and it is not assumed that they deviated from his saying due to ignorance of his evidence; for we see that they have filled their books with setting up the evidences, then they say: 'The fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf, for example.' And since we are not ourselves worthy of scrutiny of the evidence, and we have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of furu' and usul, it is upon us to narrate what they say, because they are the followers of the madhhab who set themselves up for its determination and verification by their ijtihad. And look at what we have presented from the saying of Allama Qasim: 'The mujtahids did not cease until they looked into what is disputed, and they gave preference and corrected, until he said: So it is upon us to follow the preferred (rajih) and act upon it, just as if they had given fatwa in their lifetimes.' And in the fatawa of Allama Ibn al-Shilbi: It is not for the judge nor the mufti to deviate from the saying of the Imam unless one of the mashayikh clearly states that the fatwa is on the saying of someone else. So it is not for the judge to judge by the saying of other than Abu Hanifa in a matter in which no other saying has been preferred, and they have preferred therein the evidence of Abu Hanifa over his evidence; if he judges therein, his judgment is not enforceable; he has nothing but annulment. Then know that the saying of the Imam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa with our saying, etc.' carries two possible meanings: One of them is that what is meant is what is immediately understood from it, which is that when the madhhab of his Imam is established for him regarding a ruling, such as the obligation of witr, for example, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa with that until he knows the evidence of his Imam. And there is no doubt that this is specific to the mujtahid mufti, not the pure muqallid, for taqlid is: 'Accepting the saying of another without knowing his evidence.' They said: So what comes with knowledge of his evidence is not taqlid, because it is taking from the evidence, not from the mujtahid. Rather, it is said that taking it with knowledge of its evidence is a result of ijtihad, because knowledge of the evidence is only for the mujtahid, because it depends on knowledge of counter-evidence, and that depends on surveying all the evidences, and no one can do that except the mujtahid. As for mere knowledge that such-and-such a mujtahid took such-and-such a ruling from such-and-such an evidence, there is no benefit in it. So it must be that what is meant by the obligation of knowing the evidence upon the mufti is that he knows his condition, so that his taqlid in that is valid with certainty and with giving fatwa to others. And this is not achieved except in the mufti who is a mujtahid in the madhhab, and he is the mufti in reality; as for others, they are mere transmitters. But it is unlikely that this is what is meant, because this mufti, since he has not reached the rank of absolute ijtihad, taqlid is binding upon him to those who have reached that rank, and he is not required to know the evidence of his Imam except according to one opinion. It is said in al-Tahrir: Issue: Other than the absolute mujtahid, taqlid is binding upon him, even if he is a mujtahid in some issues of fiqh or some sciences like fara'id, according to the opinion of partial ijtihad, which is the truth. So he performs taqlid of others in what he is not capable of. And it is said regarding the scholar: Taqlid is binding upon him only on condition that the validity of the mujtahid's basis is evident; otherwise, it is not permissible for him to imitate him. The first is the saying of the majority, and the second is a saying of some Mu'tazila, as mentioned by its commentator. So his saying 'taqlid is binding' along with what we have presented of the definition of taqlid indicates that knowledge of the evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid, and it is not binding upon others, even if that other is a mujtahid in the madhhab.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rasm al-mufti rule: 'It is not permissible to give fatwa with our saying until he knows [the evidence].' The author explains that the early mashayikh (like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) knew the evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, and they sometimes preferred the companion's evidence and gave fatwa accordingly. This was not due to ignorance but due to their own ijtihad. Later muftis who are not at that level must simply transmit the preferred rulings as determined by those mujtahids. The fatwa of Ibn al-Shilbi emphasizes that a judge or mufti cannot deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's saying unless a mashaykh has declared the fatwa to be on another's saying. The Imam's statement is then analyzed: it may mean that a mufti must know the evidence before giving fatwa, but this only applies to a mujtahid mufti, not a muqallid. Taqlid is defined as accepting another's saying without knowing the evidence; if one knows the evidence, it is not taqlid but ijtihad. However, the text concludes that requiring knowledge of evidence for non-mujtahids is impractical and unlikely; the obligation of taqlid for non-absolute mujtahids is affirmed, following the majority view.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Accepting the saying of another without knowing his evidence.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): One who has the ability to derive rulings from evidences, either absolutely or within the madhhab.
المقلد (al-muqallid): One who accepts the saying of a mujtahid without knowledge of the evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon interpretation of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement regarding knowing the evidence?
A) Every mufti must know the evidence.
B) Only the mujtahid mufti must know the evidence; the muqallid need not.
C) Only the absolute mujtahid must know the evidence; the mujtahid fī l-madhhab need not.
D) Both the mujtahid and the muqallid must know the evidence.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti is not required to know the evidence; he must simply transmit the preferred rulings of the mujtahids of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Definition of Taqlid and Knowing Evidence for a Mufti
Defines taqlid and clarifies the mufti's required knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define taqlid as per Hanafi usul, explain what 'knowing evidence' means for a mufti, and identify the mufta bihi position on the obligation of knowing evidence.

Core Idea
Taqlid is accepting another's statement without knowing their evidence; a mufti need only know the reliability of the imam, not the proof itself.

This passage establishes a foundational rule for muftis: what does it mean to 'know the evidence'? The author defines taqlid precisely and then clarifies that for a mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid, the required knowledge is about the mujtahid's trustworthiness, not the detailed proofs. This distinction protects the integrity of fatwa by ensuring the mufti follows authoritative sources without overburdening him with impossible demands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of taqlid
Locate the exact Arabic definition: 'al-akhdhu bi-qawli al-ghayri bi-ghayri ma'rifati dalilihi'. Understand that the defining feature is the absence of knowledge of the evidence.
This is a negative definition—it specifies what is missing.
2
Distinguish between pure muqallid and mujtahid
Note that once a person knows the evidence, he is no longer a muqallid; he becomes a mujtahid (even if within the madhhab). The text says knowledge of evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid.
This is a key epistemological boundary.
3
Explain the intended meaning of 'knowing evidence' for a mufti
The author argues that the mufti must know the state (hal) of the mujtahid he follows—i.e., his reliability and trustworthiness—not the detailed proofs. This is what makes his taqlid valid.
This is the operative condition for fatwa.
4
Analyze the dispute on the obligation of knowing evidence
The majority (including Hanafis) hold that a non-absolute mujtahid must do taqlid without needing to know the evidence. A minority (some Mu'tazila) require knowing the basis of the mujtahid. Identify which view is mufta bihi.
The text sides with the majority.
5
Apply the ruling to a mufti's practice
Understand that a Hanafi mufti at the level of mujtahid fi al-madhhab does not need to verify each proof; he relies on the imam's authority. The true mufti is one who can derive within the madhhab.
This defines the hierarchy of muftis.

لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم . المقلد المحض؛ فإن التقليد: "هو الأخذ بقول الغير بغير معرفة دليله". أخذه قالوا: فخرج مع معرفة دليله فإنه ليس بتقليد؛ لأنه أخذ من الدليل لا من المجتهد بل قيل: إن أخذه مع معرفة دليله نتيجة الاجتهاد؛ لأن معرفة الدليل إنما تكون للمجتهد؛ لتوقفها على معرفة المعارض، وهي متوقفة على استقراء الأدلة كلها، ولا يقدر على ذلك إلا المجتهد أما مجرد معرفة أن المجتهد الفلاني أخذ الحكم الفلاني من الدليل الفلاني فلا فائدة فيها فلا بد أن يكون المراد من وجوب معرفة الدليل على المفتي أن يعرف حاله، حتى يصح له تقليده في ذلك مع الجزم به وإفتاء غيره به وهذا لا يتأتى إلا في المفتي المجتهد في المذهب، وهو المفتي حقيقة، أما غيره فهو ناقل. لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد؛ لأن هذا المفتي حيث لم يكن وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق يلزمه التقليد لمن وصل إليها، ولا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه إلا على قول. قال في "التحرير": مسألة: غير المجتهد المطلق يلزمه التقليد، وإن كان مجتهدا في بعض مسائل الفقه، أو بعض العلوم كالفرائض، على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق، فيقلد غيره فيما لا يقدر عليه وقيل في العالم: إنما يلزمه التقليد بشرط تبين صحة مستند المجتهد، وإلا لم يجز له تقليده. والأول قول الجمهور، والثاني قول لبعض المعتزلة، كما ذكره شارحه، فقوله: يلزمه التقليد مع ما قدمناه من تعريف التقليد، يدل على أن معرفة الدليل للمجتهد المطلق فقط، وأنه لا يلزم غيره ولو كان ذلك الغير مجتهدا في المذهب. لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم. لكن نقل الشارح عن الزركشي من الشافعية: "أن إطلاق إلحاقه بالعامي الصرف فيه نظر، لا سيما في أتباع المذاهب المتبحرين؛ فإنهم لم ينصبوا أنفسهم نصبة المقلدين، ولا شك في إلحاقهم بالمجتهدين؛ إذ لا يقلد مجتهد مجتهدا، ولا يمكن أن يكون واسطة بينهما؛ لأنه ليس لنا سوى حالتين. قال ابن المنير: والمختار أنهم مجتهدون ملتزمون أن لا يحدثوا مذهباً، أما كونهم مجتهدين فلأن الأوصاف قائمة بهم، وأما كونهم ملتزمين أن لا يحدثوا مذهباً فلأن إحداث مذهب زائد بحيث يكون لفروعه أصول وقواعد مباينة لسائر قواعد المتقدمين، فمتعذر الوجود؛ لاستيعاب المتقدمين سائر الأساليب. نعم لا يمتنع عليهم تقليد إمام في قاعدة، فإذا ظهر له صحة مذهب غير إمامه في واقعة، لم يجز له أن يقلد إمامه، لكن وقوع ذلك مستبعد؛ لكمال نظر من قبله."
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. The pure muqallid: for taqlid is: 'taking the statement of another without knowing his evidence.' [Some] said: So excluding [one] with knowledge of his evidence, for it is not taqlid because it is taking from the evidence, not from the mujtahid. It is said: taking with knowledge of his evidence is a result of ijtihad because knowledge of evidence is only for the mujtahid, since it depends on knowledge of counterevidence, which depends on surveying all evidences, and only the mujtahid is capable of that. As for mere knowledge that a certain mujtahid took a certain ruling from a certain evidence, there is no benefit in it. So the intended meaning of the obligation of knowledge of evidence upon the mufti must be that he knows his state [i.e., the trustworthiness of the mujtahid], so that his taqlid of him in that matter is valid, with certainty, and so that he can give fatwa to others by it. And this is only possible for the mufti who is a mujtahid in the madhhab, and he is the true mufti; as for other than him, he is a transmitter. But this interpretation is remote, because this mufti, since he has not reached the rank of absolute ijtihad, is obligated to do taqlid of one who has reached it, and he is not obligated to know the evidence of his imam except according to one opinion. It is stated in at-Tahrir: Issue: The non-absolute mujtahid is obligated to do taqlid, even if he is a mujtahid in some fiqh issues or some sciences like fara'id, according to the opinion of the divisibility of ijtihad – which is the truth – so he does taqlid of others in what he is incapable of. And it is said concerning the scholar: he is only obligated to do taqlid on condition that the basis of the mujtahid is clear, otherwise it is not permissible for him to do taqlid. The first is the position of the majority, the second is the position of some Mu'tazila, as mentioned by its commentator. So his statement: 'He is obligated to do taqlid,' along with what we have presented of the definition of taqlid, indicates that knowledge of the evidence is only for the absolute mujtahid, and that it is not obligatory for others, even if that other is a mujtahid in the madhhab. It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. But the commentator narrated from az-Zarkashi of the Shafi'is: 'That the absolute inclusion of him with the pure layman is subject to consideration, especially among the followers of the deep madhhabs; for they have not appointed themselves as muqallids, and there is no doubt in their inclusion among the mujtahids, for a mujtahid does not do taqlid of a mujtahid, and there cannot be an intermediary between them, because we only have two states. Ibn al-Munir said: The chosen opinion is that they are mujtahids who are committed not to originate a new madhhab. As for their being mujtahids, because the descriptions exist in them; as for their being committed not to originate a madhhab, because originating an additional madhhab such that its furu' have usul and qawa'id distinct from all the rules of the predecessors is impossible to exist, because the predecessors have covered all methods. Yes, it is not prohibited for them to do taqlid of an imam in a principle; so if it appears to him the correctness of a madhhab other than his imam in a particular case, it is not permissible for him to do taqlid of his imam, but the occurrence of that is unlikely due to the perfection of [his] earlier consideration.'
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-based discussion (rasm rule) on the condition of 'knowledge' for a mufti. The author begins by defining taqlid as accepting another's statement without knowing the evidence. Then he clarifies that 'knowing the evidence' in the sense required for giving fatwa does not mean knowing all the proofs—that is only for the absolute mujtahid. Rather, it means knowing the reliability of the mujtahid being followed. The true mufti is one who is a mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab); otherwise, he is merely a transmitter (naqil). The author then notes that this interpretation is problematic because a non-absolute mujtahid is still obligated to do taqlid of an absolute mujtahid, and he is not required to know the evidence of his imam except according to a minority view. The text quotes at-Tahrir to show that even a mujtahid in some areas (like fara'id) must do taqlid in what he cannot handle, supporting the divisibility of ijtihad. The first view (obligation of taqlid unconditionally) is the majority view, while the second (condition of knowing the basis) is attributed to some Mu'tazila. The passage concludes with a quote from az-Zarkashi, who argues that advanced followers of madhhabs are not to be treated as pure laymen; they are mujtahids committed not to create a new madhhab, but they may still do taqlid of their imam in general principles. In Hanafi fiqh, this reinforces the idea that a Hanafi mufti must be qualified to understand the usul of the school to issue accurate fatwas.

Key Terms
التقليد (at-taqlid): أخذ قول الغير بغير معرفة دليله
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): المفتي الذي لم يصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق ولكنه يعرف أصول إمامه ويستطيع التفريع عليها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the majority position on whether a non-absolute mujtahid must know the evidence of his imam?
A) He must know the evidence in detail.
B) He must only know the reliability of the imam, not the proof.
C) He must know the evidence if he is a mujtahid in other areas.
D) He is not obligated to do taqlid at all.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid means following without proof knowledge; a Hanafi mufti is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab who relies on the imam's authority, not on detailed verification of evidence.

Fatwa by Takhrij: Deriving Rulings from the Imam's Principles
Expands on the second interpretation of 'until he knows' as takhrij from the imam's usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of takhrij as a method of ifta' and identify the conditions required for a mufti to practice it according to Hanafi rasm al-mufti.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti may give fatwa by deriving rulings from the Imam's principles, not by transmitting them verbatim.

This passage introduces the second interpretation of the phrase 'until he knows' in the rule governing muftis. While the first interpretation required knowledge of evidence at the level of absolute ijtihad, this second interpretation expands the scope: a mufti may give fatwa by takhrij—derivation from the usul of his Imam—provided he meets strict conditions. This method reflects the practice of the early Hanafi masters and allows the school to address novel issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
Recognize that the phrase 'until he knows' in the ruling 'No fatwa by our statement until he knows' has two possible meanings: (1) knowing the evidence for ijtihad, or (2) ability to derive from the imam's usul.
The passage focuses on the second interpretation.
2
Define takhrij
Takhrij is giving a fatwa by deriving a ruling from the imam's principles (usul) and not by merely transmitting his exact words (naql 'ayn).
This allows for growth within the madhhab.
3
List the conditions for takhrij
From the text: the mufti must be acquainted with the imam's foundations (mabani), competent to examine them, able to derive furu' from his principles, skilled in differentiation (farq) and combination (jam'), and possess a faculty of competence (malakat al-qtidar) for istinbat.
These conditions distinguish a mujtahid fi al-madhhab from a mere transmitter.
4
Note the historical evidence
The commentary on at-Tahrir points out that the companions of Abu Hanifa (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) practiced takhrij, sometimes differing with the Imam in usul and many furu'.
This validates the interpretation and shows its acceptance.
5
Understand the hierarchy
Takhrij is the domain of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, who derives rulings within the school's framework, as opposed to a pure transmitter or an absolute mujtahid.
This clarifies the mufti's rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني من الاحتمالين: أن يكون المراد الإفتاء بقول الإمام تخريجاً واستنباطاً من أصوله. قال في "التحرير" وشرحه: مسألة: "إفتاء غير المجتهد بمذهب مجتهد تخريجا على أصوله لا نقل عينه إن كان مطلعا على مبانيه - أي مأخذ أحكام المجتهد أهلاً للنظر فيها، قادرا على التفريع على قواعده، متمكنا من الفرق والجمع والمناظرة في ذلك بأن يكون له ملكة الاقتدار على استنباط أحكام مستبعد وما استبعده غير بعيد كما أفاده في شرح التحرير، فإنه واقع في مثل أصحاب الإمام الأعظم، فإنهم خالفوه في بعض الأصول وفي فروع كثيرة جدا إلخ."
The second of the two probabilities: that the intended meaning is giving fatwa by the statement of the imam by way of takhrij and istinbat from his usul. It is stated in at-Tahrir and its commentary: Issue: 'The giving of fatwa by a non-mujtahid according to the madhhab of a mujtahid by way of takhrij based on his usul, not by transmission of his exact ruling, provided that he is acquainted with his foundations – i.e., the sources of the mujtahid's rulings, competent to examine them, able to derive furu' from his principles, skilled in differentiation and combination and debate in that matter, such that he has the faculty of competence to derive rulings – is unlikely [but] what he [the author of at-Tahrir] deemed unlikely is not unlikely, as indicated in the commentary of at-Tahrir, for it actually occurred among the companions of the Great Imam [Abu Hanifa], for they differed with him in some usul and in very many furu' etc.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents the second interpretation of the phrase 'until he knows' in the rule 'لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم'. Instead of requiring the mufti to know the evidence in the sense of ijtihad, this interpretation holds that the mufti should be able to give fatwa by takhrij (derivation) from the principles (usul) of his imam. The text quotes at-Tahrir, which states that a non-mujtahid may give fatwa according to a mujtahid's madhhab by takhrij based on his usul, not by merely transmitting the exact ruling. The conditions for this are strict: the mufti must be fully acquainted with the imam's foundations (mabani), be able to derive subsidiary rulings, and possess the ability to differentiate and combine. Although at-Tahrir initially deems this unlikely, the commentary of at-Tahrir refutes that, noting that the companions of Abu Hanifa (like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) actually did this—they sometimes disagreed with the imam in usul and many furu'. Therefore, this is a legitimate method for a Hanafi mufti who is a mujtahid fi al-madhhab to issue fatwas, as long as he masters the school's principles.

Key Terms
التخريج (at-takhrij): استنباط أحكام فقهية من أصول الإمام وقواعده دون نقل عين مذهبه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He must have reached the level of absolute ijtihad
C) He must be acquainted with the imam's foundations and able to derive rulings
D) He must only transmit the exact words of the imam

Key Takeaway
A qualified Hanafi mufti may give fatwa by deriving rulings from the Imam's usul, not just by transmitting his exact words, as demonstrated by the Sahibayn.

Conditions for Fatwa by Non-Mujtahid: Between Takhrij and Taqlid
Debates the permissibility of fatwa by a non-mujtahid who can perform takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for a non-mujtahid to issue a fatwa by takhrij and distinguish the operative position from weaker views.

Core Idea
A non-mujtahid may give fatwa only by takhrij if he knows the imam's proofs; mere transmission is not sufficient.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical question: can a scholar who has not reached absolute ijtihad still issue fatwas? The Hanafi school distinguishes between mere transmission of rulings (naql) and genuine derivation (takhrij). The text explores the conditions under which a 'mujtahid within the school' may give fatwa, and presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether knowledge of the imam's proofs is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Determine the core question: is takhrij required for a non-mujtahid to give fatwa, or is mere transmission sufficient?
2
Distinguish between naql and takhrij
Separate verbatim transmission (naql) of the imam's statements from extraction (takhrij) of new rulings from his principles. The passage emphasizes this distinction.
Takhrij is the method of a mujtahid fi al-madhhab.
3
Analyze the conditions for a mujtahid fi al-madhhab
From al-Tahrir: the non-mujtahid must be informed of the imam's foundations (mabāni), capable of branching out (tafrī'), and able to differentiate, combine, and debate.
These conditions are necessary for fatwa by takhrij.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Zufar require knowledge of proofs; the author of al-Badi' and many scholars allow fatwa by transmission even without such knowledge. Understand each side's basis.
The dispute is about takhrij, not transmission per se.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The chosen view (mukhtar) among later Hanafis is that fatwa by takhrij requires knowledge of proofs. Mere transmission is allowed only with narrator conditions.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يجوز الفتوى بقولنا حتى يعلم. لكن نقل الشارح عن الزركشي من الشافعية: أن إطلاق إلحاقه بالعامي الصرف فيه نظر، لا سيما في أتباع المذاهب المتبحرين؛ فإنهم لم ينصبوا أنفسهم نصبة المقلدين، ولا شك في إلحاقهم بالمجتهدين؛ إذ لا يقلد مجتهد مجتهدا، ولا يمكن أن يكون واسطة بينهما؛ لأنه ليس لنا سوى حالتين. قال ابن المنير : والمختار أنهم مجتهدون ملتزمون أن لا يحدثوا مذهبا، أما كونهم مجتهدين فلأن الأوصاف قائمة بهم، وأما كونهم ملتزمين أن لا يحدثوا مذهباً فلأن إحداث مذهب زائد بحيث يكون لفروعه أصول وقواعد مباينة لسائر قواعد المتقدمين، فمتعذر الوجود؛ لاستيعاب المتقدمين سائر الأساليب. نعم لا يمتنع عليهم تقليد إمام في قاعدة، فإذا ظهر له صحة مذهب غير إمامه في واقعة، لم يجز له أن يقلد إمامه، لكن وقوع ذلك مستبعد؛ لكمال نظر من قبله.
الثاني من الاحتمالين: أن يكون المراد الإفتاء بقول الإمام تخريجاً واستنباطاً من أصوله.
قال في "التحرير" وشرحه:
مسألة: "إفتاء غير المجتهد بمذهب مجتهد تخريجا على أصوله لا نقل عينه إن كان مطلعا على مبانيه - أي مأخذ أحكام المجتهد أهلا للنظر فيها، قادرا على التفريع على قواعده، متمكنا من الفرق والجمع والمناظرة في ذلك بأن يكون له ملكة الاقتدار على استنباط أحكام متجددة التي لا نقل فيها عن صاحب المذهب من الأصول التي مهدها صاحب المذهب، وهذا المسمى بالمجتهد في المذهب جاز، وإلا يكن كذلك لا يجوز.
وفي شرح "البديع للهندي: وهو المختار عند كثير من أصحابنا وغيرهم فإنه نقل عن أبي يوسف وزفر وغيرهما أئمتنا من أنهم قالوا لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا ما لم يعلم من أين قلنا". وعبارة بعضهم: من حفظ الأقاويل و لم يعرف الحجج، فلا يحل له أن يفتي فيما اختلفوا فيه".
وقيل: جاز بشرط عدم مجتهد، واستَقْرَبَه العلامة. وقيل: يجوز مطلقا، أي سواء كان مطلعا على المأخذ أم لا، عدم المجتهد أم لا، وهو مختار صاحب "البديع" وكثير من العلماء؛ لأنه ناقل، فلا فرق فيه بين العالم وغيره. وأجيب بأنه ليس الخلاف في النقل، بل في التخريج؛ لأن النقل لعين مذهب المجتهد يقبل بشرائط الراوي من العدالة وغيرها اتفاقا". انتهى ملخصاً.
أقول: ويظهر مما ذكره الهندي: أن هذا غير خاص بأقوال الإمام بل أقول أصحابه كذلك وأن المراد بالمجتهد في المذهب هم أهل الطبقة الثالثة من الطبقات السبع المارة. وأن الطبقة الثانية - الإمام - أهل اجتهاد مطلق إلا أنهم قلدوه في أغلب أصوله وقواعده، بناء على أن المجتهد له أن يقلد آخر، وفيه عن أبي حنيفة روايتان، جاز: جواب الشرط في قوله: إن كان مطلعاً.
It is not permissible to give fatwa by our statement until he knows. But the commentator transmitted from al-Zarkashi of the Shafi'is: "That absolute annexation to the pure layman has consideration, especially regarding followers of thoroughly researched schools; for they have not set themselves up as mere blind followers, and there is no doubt about their annexation to the mujtahids; since a mujtahid does not imitate another mujtahid, and there cannot be an intermediary between them; because we only have two states." Ibn al-Munir said: "The chosen view is that they are mujtahids who are committed not to create a new school. As for being mujtahids, because the attributes exist in them; as for being committed not to create a new school, because creating an additional school such that its branches have principles and rules opposed to the rules of the predecessors is practically impossible, due to the predecessors having encompassed all methods. Yes, it is not impossible for them to imitate an imam in a principle; so if the correctness of a school other than his imam's appears to him in a particular case, he may not imitate his imam. But the occurrence of that is unlikely, due to the perfection of the reasoning of those before him."
The second of the two probabilities: that the intended meaning is giving fatwa by the imam's statement via extraction (takhrij) and derivation from his principles.
Al-Tahrir and its commentary said: "Issue: Giving fatwa by a non-mujtahid according to the school of a mujtahid via extraction from his principles, not by verbatim transmission, is permissible if he is informed of his foundations - i.e., the sources of the mujtahid's rulings, fit to examine them, capable of branching out upon his rules, able to differentiate, combine, and debate in that, such that he has the capacity to derive rulings for new matters for which there is no transmitted text from the school's founder from the principles that the founder laid down. This is called a mujtahid within the school. It is permissible. Otherwise, it is not permissible."
And in the commentary of al-Badi' al-Hindi: "And it is the chosen view according to many of our companions and others, for it is transmitted from Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and other our imams that they said: 'It is not lawful for anyone to give fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.'" And the expression of some: "One who memorizes sayings and does not know the proofs, it is not lawful for him to give fatwa in matters in which they differed."
And it was said: It is permissible on condition of absence of a mujtahid, and the 'Allama deemed it likely. And it was said: It is permissible absolutely, i.e., whether he is informed of the source or not, whether a mujtahid is absent or not. This is the choice of the author of al-Badi' and many scholars; because he is a transmitter, so there is no distinction between him and a non-scholar. It was answered: The difference is not about transmission, but about extraction; because verbatim transmission of the mujtahid's school is accepted with the conditions of a narrator, such as reliability and others, by agreement." End summarized.
I say: It is evident from what al-Hindi mentioned that this is not specific to the statements of the Imam, but also to those of his companions; and that what is meant by a 'mujtahid within the school' are those of the third level of the seven levels mentioned earlier. And that the second level - the Imam - are people of absolute ijtihad except that they followed him in most of his principles and rules, based on that a mujtahid may imitate another, and regarding that there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. 'Permissible' is the answer to the condition in his saying: 'If he is informed.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions under which a non-mujtahid may issue fatwas according to the Hanafi school. It begins by restating the principle that fatwa by a mere follower is not allowed until he understands the basis of the rulings. The commentator then introduces a discussion from the Shafi'i scholar al-Zarkashi, who argues that advanced adherents of a school are not like ordinary laymen; they possess the attributes of mujtahids but are committed not to create a new school. This view aligns with the second possibility: that the rule refers to giving fatwa by extracting rulings from the Imam's principles (takhrij). The text from al-Tahrir clarifies that a non-mujtahid who is capable of derivation—called a mujtahid within the school—may give fatwa. Then, the view of al-Badi' al-Hindi is presented, stating that the chosen position of many Hanafi imams, including Abu Yusuf and Zufar, is that one must know the proofs before issuing fatwas. Some scholars allowed it absolutely, but the counterargument is that the dispute concerns takhrij, not mere transmission. Finally, the author notes that this rule applies not only to the Imam's sayings but to those of his companions as well, and defines the 'mujtahid within the school' as those of the third level of jtihad hierarchy. The hierarchy is such that the second level (the Imam) are absolute mujtahids who nonetheless follow Abu Hanifa in most principles, and there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa on whether a mujtahid may imitate another.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving a ruling for a new case from the principles of the imam, as opposed to simply transmitting his existing statements.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of deriving rulings from the imam's principles for new cases but not claiming absolute ijtihad. He is of the third level of mujtahids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes a mujtahid fi al-madhhab from a mere transmitter?
A) The ability to memorize many rulings.
B) The capacity to derive rulings from the imam's principles.
C) The permission of the ruler.
D) The memorization of hadith.

Key Takeaway
A non-mujtahid may issue fatwas by takhrij only if he is informed of the imam's foundations and capable of derivation; mere transmission without knowledge of proofs is insufficient for fatwa.

The Condition of Knowing Evidence for Fatwa
A rule about the mufti's knowledge of evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of knowledge of evidence (makhraj) to determine when a mufti may issue a fatwa by istinbat and when he must restrict to narration.

Core Idea
A mufti who derives rulings must know their evidential basis; a narrator may simply transmit.

This lesson unpacks a foundational rasm al-mufti rule: that a mufti must know the evidence behind Hanafi rulings before issuing fatwas. The passage clarifies that this condition applies specifically to those who derive (mujtahid fi al-madhhab), not to mere narrators. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi hierarchy and avoiding fatwa errors.

Guided Path
1
State the Core Rule
Identify the rule as narrated from Abu Yusuf, Zufar: 'It is not permissible for anyone to issue a fatwa with our saying until he knows from where we said it.' Understand that this is a condition for those who derive, not for narrators.
2
Distinguish Between Narration and Derivation
Recognize that the disagreement (ikhtilaf) is about derivation (takhrij), not narration (naql). Narration is accepted with standard transmitter conditions; derivation requires knowledge of the proof.
This resolves the apparent conflict between different scholarly positions.
3
Identify the Relevant Tabaqat
The condition of knowing evidence applies to the third, fourth, and fifth layers of mujtahid fi al-madhhab. The second layer (Imam) has absolute ijtihad but still follows school principles. Lower layers suffice with transmission.
Refer to the seven-layer hierarchy of Hanafi scholars.
4
Apply to a Concrete Scenario
Consider a mufti who memorizes rulings but cannot cite the hadith or qiyas behind them. According to the rule, he may only narrate those rulings; he cannot derive new fatwas. Use Abu Yusuf's mouse example to see how even great scholars occasionally deferred.
5
Determine the Relied-Upon Position
The mufta bihi view is that the condition is mandatory for mujtahid fi al-madhhab; narrators are exempt. Later scholars' derivations (even if not from the Imam) must be followed as transmitted.
This is the established fatwa approach in the Hanafi school.

It is not permissible to issue a fatwa with our saying until he knows. In the commentary "Al-Badi' al-Hindi": And it is the chosen [view] according to many of our companions and others, for it is transmitted from Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and other our imams that they said: It is not permissible for anyone to issue a fatwa with our saying as long as he does not know from where we said it. And the expression of some: He who preserves the sayings but does not know the proofs, it is not permissible for him to issue a fatwa in what they differed about. And it was said: It is permissible on condition of absence of a mujtahid, and the scholar considered it probable. And it was said: It is permissible absolutely, i.e., whether he is aware of the source or not, whether the mujtahid is absent or not, and this is the choice of the author of "Al-Badi'" and many scholars; because he is a narrator, so there is no difference between him and another in that. And it was answered: The disagreement is not about narration, but about derivation; because narrating the exact [known] madhhab of the mujtahid is accepted with the conditions of the narrator including integrity and others by agreement. And that the second layer - the Imam - are people of absolute ijtihad except that they followed him in most of his principles and rules, based on the fact that a mujtahid may follow another, and regarding that there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. And from Muhammad: "He follows one more knowledgeable than him," or that his ijtihad agreed with their ijtihad in it. And they have opposed him in many branches, and despite this, their statements did not leave the madhhab, as has been established earlier. And it appears that the people of the third, fourth, and fifth layers share in that. And that those other than them suffice with transmission. And that it is upon us to follow what they have transmitted to us from their derivations not explicitly stated by the earlier [scholars], and from their preferred opinions, even if they are contrary to the saying of the Imam, as we established at the beginning of this discussion; because they... And Imam al-Haramayn said: I consider every choice of al-Muzani to be a derivation, for he does not oppose the principles of al-Shafi'i, unlike Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, for they oppose their master. Al-Rafi'i said in the chapter of wudu: The unique opinions of al-Muzani are not counted as part of the madhhab if they are not derived from the principles of al-Shafi'i.]

Commentary
This passage addresses a rasm rule: the condition that a mufti must know the evidential basis (makhraj) of the rulings he issues, not merely the rulings themselves. The author begins by stating the core rule: 'It is not permissible to issue a fatwa with our saying until he knows.' He then presents the view of Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and others that a mufti must know 'from where we said it.' Some scholars, however, permitted fatwa for a mere narrator if no mujtahid exists; others permitted it absolutely, arguing that a narrator is like any transmitter. The author clarifies, citing Al-Badi' and Al-Tahrir, that the disagreement applies to 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab' (one who derives rulings), not to pure narrators. He then explains the layers (tabaqat) of mujtahids: the second layer includes those with absolute ijtihad who still follow the Imam's principles; the third, fourth, and fifth layers are 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab' who derive rulings within the school. The ruling is that such mujtahids must know the evidence to issue fatwas by derivation, while those below them (e.g., mere transmitters) may simply narrate. The passage supports this by noting that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad sometimes differed from Abu Hanifa but remained within the madhhab, indicating they exercised ijtihad. The final remark about Shafi'i scholars suggests a parallel discussion: al-Muzani's independence within the Shafi'i school versus Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's greater divergence. The relied-upon position is that the condition applies to those who derive, not to narrators; lay muftis should follow the later scholars' transmitted derivations.

Key Terms
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of deriving rulings within the Hanafi school using its principles and evidence.
الطبقات (al-tabaqat): The hierarchical layers of Hanafi scholars, from absolute mujtahids to mere muqallids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must only memorize the rulings of the school.
B) He must know the evidence (makhraj) from which the ruling is derived.
C) He must be an absolute mujtahid independent of the school.
D) He must have the approval of the current caliph.

Key Takeaway
The fatwa condition distinguishes between those who derive (need evidence) and those who narrate (transmit); knowing one's position in the hierarchy is essential for sound fatwa practice.

Hierarchy of Sources When No Narration
Fatwa hierarchy rule when no riwayah exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy when no direct narration from Abu Hanifa exists and apply it to a hypothetical case.

Core Idea
When no riwayah exists, follow: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, senior companions, later scholars’ majority, then ijtihad with fear.

In this lesson, we examine the hierarchical method for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school when no direct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is available. This is a critical tool for a mufti, ensuring that rulings are based on the strongest available authority. The passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti outlines the precise order, from the early imams to later scholars, and finally to personal ijtihad under strict conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting condition
Recognize that the hierarchy applies only when there is no narration (riwayah) from Abu Hanifa himself. This triggers the search for other authoritative sources.
2
List the order of early imams
The first resort is the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, then the senior companions (kibar al-ashab) in descending order of seniority.
This order is explicit in al-Hawi al-Qudsi as quoted in the passage.
3
Move to later scholars (muta'akhkhirun)
If no clear answer from the early imams, consult the later scholars. If they have one opinion, adopt it. If they differ, adopt the opinion of the majority among the well-known later scholars like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, and al-Tahawi.
The majority opinion among the muta'akhkhirun carries weight.
4
Final resort: mufti's ijtihad
If no transmitted answer exists at all, the mufti must engage in ijtihad with deep reflection and fear of Allah. He must not speak rashly, for this is a grave responsibility only for the ignorant and wretched.
Ijtihad here means deriving a ruling from the principles of the madhhab, not abandoning it.

طريق الإفتاء عند عدم الرواية ]
قال في آخر الحاوي القدسي : ومتى لم يوجد في المسألة عن أبي حنيفة رواية، يؤخذ بظاهر قول أبي يوسف ثم بظاهر قول محمد، ثم بظاهر قول زفر والحسن ،وغيرهم الأكبر فالأكبر هكذا إلى آخر من كان من كبار الأصحاب.

Explanation of the Cords of the Mufti's Code: The Path of Ifta when there is no Narration. Our scholars of deep knowledge. Then if no narration exists and those who came later differed, the one upon which the majority is preferred, like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs al-Kabir, Abu Ja'far, and al-Layth al-Shahir. And if there is no statement from these and need for fatwa arises, then let the mufti look with seriousness and ijtihad and fear the punishment of his Lord on the Day of Return. None dares to give rulings except a misguided, losing individual. The Path of Ifta when there is no Narration: He said in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Whenever there is no narration from Abu Hanifa in a matter, the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf is taken, then the apparent statement of Muhammad, then the apparent statement of Zufar and al-Hasan, and so on, the greater then the greater, until the end of those who were from the senior companions. And if there is no apparent answer from any of them in an incident, and the later scholars have spoken with one opinion, it is taken. If they differ, the opinion of the majority is taken from what the well-known senior scholars have relied upon, like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi, and others, so it is relied upon. And if no answer exists from them at all as a text, the mufti looks into it with consideration, deliberation, and ijtihad to find what brings him closer to discharging his duty. He should not speak rashly due to his position and its sanctity. He should fear Allah Almighty and be mindful of Him, for it is a great matter that none dares to do except every ignorant, wretched person.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage establishes the hierarchical method for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school when no direct narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is available. It first cites a general rule from the earlier scholars, then quotes al-Hawi al-Qudsi detailing the order: take the apparent statement of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, then the senior companions of al-Muhit. If none have a clear answer, then look to the later scholars like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi. If they have one opinion, accept it; if they differ, adopt the majority view. Finally, if no answer at all exists, the mufti must engage in ijtihad with caution, fear of Allah, and not speak rashly. This delineates the authority weight of different layers of Hanafi scholarship for fatwa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars after the founding imams, such as Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, etc.
كبار الأصحاب (kibar al-ashab): The senior companions of the Hanafi school, such as Zufar, al-Hasan, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Take the opinion of the majority
C) Do ijtihad
D) Refer to Zufar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy ensures rulings are grounded in transmitted authority, from the early imams down to personal ijtihad, with the mufti bound to follow the strongest available source.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Mufti Must Say 'I Don't Know'
Ruling on necessity of saying 'I don't know' and procedure for a muqallid mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a muqallid mufti must say 'la adri' and apply the hierarchy of reference for issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti must say 'I don't know' if he cannot find a transmitted ruling – independent opinion is not allowed.

This passage from Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti establishes a critical principle for muftis, especially those who are muqallids (followers). It outlines the steps a mufti must take when faced with an issue not found in the primary sources, culminating in the obligation to refrain from giving an answer when knowledge is lacking. The text emphasizes that even the greatest scholars, including the Prophet ﷺ, acknowledged the limits of their knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scope
What is the ruling about? The passage addresses the conduct of a mufti when he lacks knowledge of a ruling, particularly for a muqallid mufti.
This is a rasm al-mufti rule, not a substantive fiqh ruling.
2
Parse the Hierarchy for a Mujtahid
If the issue is not in Zahir al-Riwayah, first check if it agrees with school principles. If no narration, rely on agreement of later scholars. If they disagree, the mujtahid exerts effort (ijtihad).
The mujtahid has the authority to derive rulings from evidence.
3
Distinguish the Muqallid
For a muqallid mufti, he cannot do ijtihad. He must take the statement of the most learned scholar available, even by correspondence, and attribute the answer to that scholar.
A muqallid is bound to transmit, not derive.
4
Locate the Obligation of 'La Adri'
If the muqallid cannot find the incident in any book and cannot refer to a scholar, he must say 'I don't know'. This is obligatory, as the text says 'he has no right to give fatwa by his opinion'.
The obligation is derived from the practice of the Salaf and the Prophet's example.
5
Understand the Evidence
The rule is supported by the quote from al-Khaniyah and al-Tatarkhaniyah, and the practice of the Companions and the Prophet himself, who said 'I don't know' when appropriate.
This protects against slander against Allah by forbidding the permissible or vice versa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتي
لا بد للعالم من "لا أدري"
وفي الخانية: "وإن كانت المسألة في غير ظاهر الرواية، إن كانت توافق أصول أصحابنا يعمل بها. فإن لم يجد لها رواية عن أصحابنا، واتفق فيها المتأخرون على شيء، يعمل به. وإن اختلفوا، يجتهد ويفتي بما هو أفقه صواب عنده. وإن كان المفتي مقلدا غير مجتهد يأخذ بقول من هو الناس عنده ويضيف الجواب إليه، فإن كان أفقه الناس عنده في مصر آخر، يرجع إليه بالكتاب ويكتب بالجواب ولا يجازف؛ خوفا من الافتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم الحلال وضده".
لا بد للعالم من لا أدري]
قلت وقوله : "وإن كان المفتي مقلدا غير مجتهد إلخ. يفيد أن المقلد عن أحد. ويؤيده ما في "البحر" عن "التاترخانية: وإن اختلف المتأخرون أخذ بقول واحد، فلو لم يجد من المتأخرين يجتهد برأيه إذا كان يعرف وجوه الفقه ويشاور أهله".
فقوله: "إذا كان يعرف إلخ. دليل على أن من لم يعرف ذلك، بل قرأ كتاباً أو أكثر، وفهمه وصار له أهلية المراجعة والوقوف على موضع الحادثة من كتاب مشهور معتمد إذا لم يجد تلك الحادثة في كتاب ليس له أن يفتي فيها برأيه، بل عليه أن يقول: "لا أدري"، كما قال من هو أجل منه قدراً من مجتهدي الصحابة ومن بعدهم، بل من أيد بالوحي ، صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم.
The Mufti Must Have 'I Don't Know'
And in al-Khaniyah: 'If the issue is not from Zahir al-Riwayah, if it agrees with the principles of our school, it is acted upon. If he finds no narration from our school, and the later scholars agreed on something, he acts by it. If they disagreed, he exerts effort and gives fatwa with what is more correct in his view. And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid, he takes the statement of the one who is the most learned in his view and attributes the answer to him. If the most learned in his view is in another city, he refers to him by letter and writes the answer, and does not speak hastily, fearing slander against Allah by forbidding the permissible or vice versa.'
I said: His statement 'If the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid, etc.' indicates that the muqallid is [not allowed to give fatwa] except based on someone. And it is supported by what is in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyah: 'If the later scholars differed, he takes one statement, and if he does not find from the later scholars, he exerts his opinion if he knows the aspects of fiqh and consults its people.'
So his statement: 'If he knows, etc.' is evidence that the one who does not know that, but studied one or more books and understood and attained the ability to reference and locate the incident from a famous reliable book, if he does not find that incident in any book, he has no right to give fatwa by his opinion, rather he must say 'I don't know', as said by those greater in rank than him from the mujtahid Companions and those after them, even from the one supported by revelation, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage addresses two key rules for a mufti: the necessity of saying 'I don't know' when he lacks knowledge, and the procedure for a mufti who is a muqallid (not a mujtahid). It begins by quoting al-Khaniyah on handling issues outside Zahir al-Riwayah: first check if it agrees with school principles; if no narration, rely on the agreement of later scholars; if they disagree, a mujtahid may exercise ijtihad. For a muqallid, he must follow the most learned scholar accessible to him, even if by correspondence. The author then comments that this implies a muqallid cannot give fatwa without a basis. He supports this with a quote from al-Bahr that a muqallid who cannot find a ruling from later scholars should consult his own opinion only if he knows legal methodology and consults experts. The author stresses that one who merely read books but cannot find the exact incident must say 'I don't know', following the example of the greatest scholars and even the Prophet himself. This ruling safeguards against slander against Allah.

Key Terms
لا أدري (la adri): The statement 'I don't know' that a mufti must utter when he does not have knowledge of a ruling.
مقلد (muqallid): A mufti who is not a mujtahid and must follow the rulings of a specific mujtahid or school.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six major works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a muqallid mufti do if he cannot find a ruling in any book and the later scholars differ?
A) He should make ijtihad based on his knowledge.
B) He should say 'I don't know'.
C) He should follow the opinion of the most learned scholar in his city.
D) He should write to a scholar in another city.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must say 'la adri' when he cannot locate a transmitted ruling; this preserves the integrity of fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Prohibition of Fatwa from General Principles (Qawaid)
Rasm rule: prohibition of fatwa from qawaid alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that prohibits issuing fatwa from qawaid alone and state the correct procedure (tawaqquf or hikayah) when explicit naql is missing.

Core Idea
Fatwa from qawaid alone is invalid; only explicit naql or hikayah suffices.

This passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti establishes a foundational rule for Hanafi fatwa: a mufti cannot issue a ruling based solely on general legal principles (qawaid). The reason is that qawaid are akthari (majority rules), not universal, and subtle differences exist between similar cases. The correct approach is to search for explicit textual transmission (naql sarih), and if unavailable, to refrain from answering (tawaqquf) or consult a more knowledgeable scholar. For non-mujtahid muftis, only hikayah (narration) is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forbidden practice
The passage explicitly states it is not permissible (la yahillu) to issue fatwa from qawaid alone. Identify this as the primary prohibition.
Contrast with those who think qawaid can substitute.
2
Understand the rationale
The author explains that fiqh principles are akthari (majority), not kulli (universal), and ulema have written books of furuq to differentiate similar cases. The mufti's understanding may miss subtle distinctions.
Qawaid are not universal; exceptions exist.
3
Recognize the required action when naql is found
If an explicit naql is found, the mufti must rely on it via hikayah (narration). This is the default method for non-mujtahids.
Hikayah is quoting the school's rulings verbatim.
4
Apply the remedy when naql is missing
The text says: 'fa-man lam yajid naqlan sarihan an yatawaqqafa fi al-jawab aw yas'ala man huwa minh' — stop or ask a more knowledgeable scholar.
Tawaqquf is preferred over risk of error.
5
Note the exception
Customary incidents (hawadith 'urfiya) that do not contradict shariah may be handled directly, a point referenced at the poem's end.
This exception is limited and requires caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإفتاء بالقواعد في بعض الحوادث
شرح عقود رسم المفتي والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النص لقلة اطلاعه، أو عدم معرفته بموضع المسألة المذكورة فيه؛ إذ قلّ ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر في كتب المذهب، إما بعينها أو بذكر قاعدة كلية تشملها.
الإفتاء بالقواعد في بعض الحوادث]
ولا يكتفى بوجود نظيرها مما يقاربها؛ فإنه لا يأمن أن يكون بين حادثة وما وجده فرق، لا يصل إليه فهمه فكم من مسألة فرّقوا بينها وبين نظيرتها، حتى ألفوا كتب الفروق لذلك، ولو وكل الأمر إلى أفهامنا لم ندرك الفرق بينهما، بل قال العلامة ابن نجيم في "الفوائد الزينية": "لا يحل الإفتاء من القواعد والضوابط وإنما على المفتي حكاية النقل كما صرحوا به. وقال أيضا: "إن المقرر في الأربعة المذاهب الصريح أن قواعد الفقه أكثرية لا كلية". نقله البيري.
أعلم
فعلى من لم يجد نقلا صريحا أن يتوقف في الجواب، أو يسأل من هو منه ولو في بلدة أخرى، كما يعلم مما نقلناه عن "الخانية". وفي "الظهيرية" : " وإن لم يكن من أهل الاجتهاد لا يحل له أن يفتي إلا بطريق الحكاية، فيحكي ما يحفظ من أقوال الفقهاء". نعم! قد توجد حوادث عرفية غير مخالفة للنصوص الشرعية، فيفتي المفتي بها كما سنذكره آخر المنظومة.
Issuing fatwa based on general principles in some incidents. Commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: And the norm is that his failure to find the text is due to his lack of knowledge, or his ignorance of the location of the mentioned issue in it; for rarely does an incident occur except that it is mentioned in the books of the school, either explicitly or through a universal principle that encompasses it. Issuing fatwa based on general principles in some incidents. And one is not satisfied with the existence of a similar case that approximates it; for he is not safe from there being a difference between the incident and what he found, which his understanding cannot reach. How many a case have they differentiated between it and its similar one, to the extent that they authored books of differences for that reason. Had the matter been entrusted to our understandings, we would not have perceived the difference between them. Rather, Allamah Ibn Nujaym said in al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyyah: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa from general principles and maxims; rather, the mufti must narrate the transmission as they have stated.' And he also said: 'What is established in the four schools is that the principles of fiqh are majority rules, not universal.' Transmitted by al-Bayri. Know: So whoever does not find an explicit transmission must refrain from answering, or ask someone who is more knowledgeable than him, even if in another town, as is known from what we quoted from al-Khaniyyah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: 'If he is not among the people of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of narration; so he narrates what he memorizes of the statements of the jurists.' Yes! There may occur customary incidents that do not contradict the legal texts, so the mufti may give fatwa based on them, as we will mention at the end of the poem.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule for muftis regarding the use of general legal principles (qawaid) in issuing fatwa. The author emphasizes that a mufti must first search for an explicit textual statement (naql) in the school's books, because every incident is likely mentioned either explicitly or under a universal principle. Relying merely on a close parallel (nazir) is dangerous because ulema have written entire books on subtle differences (al-furuq) that separate seemingly similar cases. Ibn Nujaym is quoted stating that it is absolutely forbidden (la yahillu) to issue fatwa from qawaid alone; the mufti must simply narrate (hikayah) the transmitted rulings. He further notes that fiqh rules are akthari (majority, not universal), so exceptions abound. The rule then sets the remedy: if no explicit text is found, the mufti must pause (tawaqquf) or consult a more knowledgeable scholar in another town. For non-mujtahid muftis, only narration is permitted. An exception is made for customary incidents (hawadith 'urfiya) that do not violate shariah, which the mufti may handle directly—this is alluded to the poem's end. The passage teaches intellectual humility: even a trained faqih cannot reliably deduce from analogues without risking error.

Key Terms
قواعد (qawa'id): General legal principles or maxims derived from the school's rulings, used as guidance but not sufficient alone for fatwa.
نقل صريح (naql sarih): An explicit textual transmission of a ruling from the Hanafi school, usually from the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah or later reliable works.
حكاية (hikayah): Narration or verbatim quoting of the school's established rulings without personal ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a mufti do if he cannot find an explicit transmission (naql sarih) for an incident?
A) Issue fatwa based on general principles (qawa'id) alone.
B) Refrain from answering or ask a more knowledgeable scholar.
C) Perform ijtihad to derive a ruling from the Qur'an and Sunnah.
D) Decline to answer permanently without seeking help.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must never issue a fatwa relying solely on general legal principles; he must either have explicit textual transmission or refrain from answering.
