First Rule of Tarjih: Preferring Imam Abu Hanifa in Ibadat
First rule of tarjih: preference of Imam Abu Hanifa in ibadat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the first rule of tarjih in ibadat by identifying when to prefer Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl and when the exception applies.

Core Idea
In ibadat, Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl is the default for fatwa unless an authentic riwaya from him aligns with the Sahibayn.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule of tarjih in the Hanafi school for acts of worship. In matters of ibadat, the school gives precedence to the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, an important exception exists when a riwaya from him is transmitted and the Two Sahibayn have also adopted a ruling consistent with that riwaya. Understanding this rule is essential for any mufti when issuing fatwas in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its domain
The poem specifies that in ibadat (worship), the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa is given absolute preference. Note the phrase 'مطلقا' indicating generality.
2
Locate the exception condition
The rule is qualified by 'ما لم تصح عنه رواية بها الغير أخذ': unless a true narration from the Imam is reported, and that narration was adopted by the other (the two Sahibayn). The example is tayammum with dates.
3
Understand the evidence
The prose from Sharh al-Munyah states that this rule is established by istiqra (inductive survey of the school's fatwa practice). The scholars unanimously follow it.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a worship case, first check the Imam's known qawl. Then see if there is a riwaya from him that agrees with the Sahibayn's ruling. If yes, that riwaya takes precedence; otherwise, stick with the Imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وههنا ضوابط محرره
الفتوى في العبادات
غدت لدى أهل النهى مقرّره
في كل أبواب العبادات رجح قولُ الإمام مطلقا ما لم تصح عنه رواية بها الغير أخذ مثل تيمم لمن تمرا نَبَذ وكل فرع بالقضا تعلّقا قول أبي يوسف فيه يُنتقى
وفي مسائل ذوي الأرحام قد أفتوا
بما
يقوله
محمد
ورجحوا استحسانهم على القياس إلا مسائل وما فيها التباس وظاهر المروي ليس يُعدل عنه إلى خلافه إذ يُنقل لا ينبغي العدول عن درايه إذا أتى بوفقها روايه وكل قول جاء ينفي الكفرا عن مسلم ولو ضعيفا أحرى وكل ما رجع عنه المجتهد صار كمنسوخ فغيره اعتمد وكل قول في المتون أثبتا فذاك ترجيح له ضمنا أتى فرجحت على الشروح والشروح على الفتاوى القدم من ذات رُجوح ما لم يكن سواه لفظا صُححا فالأرجح الذي به قد صُرّحا قواعد الترجيح من الأقوال

الفتوى في العبادات
الأولى: ما في "شرح المنية للبرهان إبراهيم الحلبي من فصل التيمم حيث قال: فلله در الإمام الأعظم ما أدق نظره وما أسد فكره وإلا ما جعل العلماء الفتوى على قوله في العبادات مطلقا، وهو الواقع بالاستقراء
And here are precisely recorded rules: Fatwa in acts of worship has become established among people of understanding. In all chapters of worship, the statement of the Imam [Abu Hanifa] is preferred absolutely unless a narration from him is authentically transmitted which someone else [the two Sahibayn] adopted, like tayammum for one who discarded dates, and every branch related to judicial matters, the statement of Abu Yusuf is selected therein. And in questions of Dhawi al-Arham, they have given fatwa according to what Muhammad says, and they have preferred his istihsan over qiyas, except for cases where there is ambiguity. And the apparent of the transmitted [Zahir al-Riwayah] is not to be deviated from to its contrary, since it is transmitted; one should not deviate from a reliable [transmission] when a narration consistent with it comes. And every statement that negates disbelief from a Muslim, even if weak, is more worthy. And every statement from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like abrogated, so others are relied upon. And every statement that is established in the texts (mutun) has a preferential weight implicitly; then the commentaries (shuruh) are given preference over the texts? Actually: the commentaries are preferred over the fatwa collections of the ancients from those having preponderance, unless there is a clear textual correction by wording; then the preponderant is that which has been explicitly declared preponderant. These are the rules of tarjih among statements. Fatwa in acts of worship: The first [rule] is what is in Sharh al-Munyah by al-Burhan Ibrahim al-Halabi from the chapter of tayammum where he said: 'How excellent is the Imam al-A'zam! How precise his insight and how sound his thought! Otherwise, the scholars would not have made fatwa on his statement in acts of worship absolutely; and that is the reality by inductive survey.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule regarding tarjih (preference) among conflicting opinions within the Hanafi school. It begins with a poetic summary (nazam) that lays down several rules for weighing statements across different domains: in ibadat, Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl is preferred absolutely unless a specific riwaya from him aligns with a ruling adopted by the Sahibayn (like tayammum with dates); in judicial (qada') matters, Abu Yusuf's view is taken; in inheritance of distant kindred (dhawu al-arham), Muhammad's opinion is followed; istihsan is preferred over qiyas unless ambiguous; and other rules regarding text hierarchy. The author then explains the first rule in prose: in all acts of worship, fatwa is given on the qawl of Imam Abu Hanifa without exception—proven by istiqra (inductive survey of the school's positions). The example of tayammum for dates (a specific case where the Sahibayn differed and their view became the fatwa) is an exception that proves the rule: the Imam's view is the default. This rule is foundational for muftis: when faced with ikhtilaf in ibadat, the default is the Imam's opinion unless there is clear evidence that the later fatwa adopted a contrary view.

Key Terms
الإمام الأعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): The Greatest Imam, referring to Abu Hanifa; his qawl is the default in ibadat.
رَوَايَة (riwaya): A transmission from the Imam or Sahibayn; in this context, a narration that may lead to a preferred fatwa contrary to the default.
استقراء (istiqra): Inductive survey of the school's positions to establish the operative rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first rule of tarjih, in which domain is Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl given absolute preference?
A) Ibadat
B) Qada'
C) Dhawi al-Arham
D) All domains

Key Takeaway
The first rule of tarjih in ibadat is that Imam Abu Hanifa's qawl is the default for fatwa, unless an authentic riwaya from him aligns with the Sahibayn's adopted ruling.
